《魏書一 - Book One of the Weishu》

底本：《武英殿二十四史》本《三國志》
《乾隆御覽四庫全書薈要》本《三國志·魏志》

《武帝紀 - Annals of Emperor Wu 》

 English translation: AI and Chinese Text Project users [?] Library Resources
底本：《武英殿二十四史》本《三國志》：武帝紀
《乾隆御覽四庫全書薈要》本《三國志·魏志》：武帝紀
[Show all]
1
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
太祖武皇帝，沛國譙人也，姓曹，諱操，字孟德，漢相國參之後。
Emperor Wu of the Taizu, was a native of Qiao, Pei Guo. His surname was Cao, his given name Cao Cao, courtesy name Mengde; he was a descendant of Han Xiangguo Can.

2
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
太祖一名吉利，小字阿瞞。王沈魏書曰：其先出於黃帝。當高陽世，陸終之子曰安，是為曹姓。周武王克殷，存先世之後，封曹俠於邾。春秋之世，與於盟會，逮至戰國，為楚所滅。子孫分流，或家于沛。漢高祖之起，曹參以功封平陽侯，世襲爵土，絕而復紹，至今適嗣國於容城。桓帝世，曹騰為中常侍大長秋，封費亭侯。司馬彪續漢書曰：騰父節，字元偉，素以仁厚稱。鄰人有亡豕者，與節豕相類，詣門認之，節不與爭；後所亡豕自還其家，豕主人大慙，送所認豕，并辭謝節，節笑而受之。由是鄉黨貴歎焉。長子伯興，次子仲興，次子叔興。騰字季興，少除黃門從官。永寧元年，鄧太后詔黃門令選中黃門從官年少溫謹者，配皇太子書，騰應其選。太子特親愛騰，飲食賞賜與衆有異。順帝即位，為小黃門，遷至中常侍大長秋。在省闥三十餘年，歷事四帝，未甞有過。好進達賢能，終無所毀傷。其所稱薦，若陳留虞放、邊韶、南陽延固、張溫、弘農張奐、潁川堂谿典等，皆致位公卿，而不伐其善。蜀郡太守因計吏修敬於騰，益州刺史种暠於函谷關搜得其牋，上太守，并奏騰內臣外交，所不當為，請免官治罪。帝曰：「牋自外來，騰書不出，非其罪也。」乃寑暠奏。騰不以介意，常稱歎暠，以為暠得事上之節。暠後為司徒，語人曰：「今日為公，乃曹常侍恩也。」騰之行事，皆此類也。桓帝即位，以騰先帝舊臣，忠孝彰著，封費亭侯，加位特進。太和三年，追尊騰曰高皇帝。養子嵩嗣，官至太尉，莫能審其生出本末。續漢書曰：嵩字巨高。質性敦慎，所在忠孝。為司隷校尉，靈帝擢拜大司農、大鴻臚，代崔烈為太尉。黃初元年，追尊嵩曰太皇帝。吳人作曹瞞傳及郭頒世語並云：嵩，夏侯氏之子，夏侯惇之叔父。太祖於惇為從父兄弟。嵩生太祖。
His another name was Jili, and his childhood name was Aman. Wang Shen's "Wei Shu" states: His ancestors originated from the Yellow Emperor. During the reign of Gao Yang, a son of Luzhong named An was the progenitor of the Cao surname. King Wu of Zhou defeated Yin, preserved descendants from previous generations, and enfeoffed Cao Xia at Zhu. During the Spring and Autumn period, they participated in alliances and meetings; by the Warring States period, they were destroyed by Chu. Their descendants dispersed into different branches, some of whom settled in Pei. When Emperor Gaozu of Han rose to power, Cao Can was enfeoffed as the Marquis of Pingyang for his meritorious service. His family inherited the title and fiefdom through generations; although it was once interrupted, it was later restored, and today the legitimate heir holds a state in Rongcheng. During the reign of Emperor Huan, Cao Teng served as Zhongchangshi and Dachangqiu, and was enfeoffed as Marquis of Fei Ting. Sima Biao's "Xu Han Shu" states: Teng's father was Jie, courtesy name Yuanwei, who had long been renowned for his kindness and integrity. A neighbor once lost a pig; when he came to Cao Jie's door, claiming that the pig resembled his own, Jie did not contest it. Later, the lost pig returned to its owner's home; greatly ashamed, the pig owner returned the wrongly claimed pig along with an apology to Jie, who accepted it with a smile. Because of this, his fellow villagers held him in high esteem and admiration. His eldest son was Boxing; the second son was Zhongxing; the third son was Shuxing. Teng, courtesy name Jixing, at a young age became an official of Huangmen Cunguan. In the first year of Yongning, Empress Dowager Deng issued an edict ordering the Huangmen Ling to select young and cautious officials from among the Zhonghuamen Cunguan to serve as scribes for the Crown Prince; Teng was selected. The Crown Prince especially loved and favored Teng, granting him food, drink, and rewards different from those given to others. After Emperor Shun ascended the throne, Teng became a Xiao Huangmen official and was later promoted to Zhongchangshi Dachangqiu. He served in the palace for more than thirty years, serving four emperors successively, and never committed any fault. He was fond of recommending capable and virtuous individuals, and in the end, he caused no harm or damage to anyone. Those he recommended, such as Yu Fang of Chenliu, Bian Shao, Yan Gu of Nanyang, Zhang Wen, Zhang Huan of Hongnong, and Tangxi Dian of Yingchuan, all attained high positions among the gongqing (high-ranking officials), yet Teng never took credit for their achievements. The Tai Shou (governor) of Shu Jun sent a letter of respect to Teng through an official on a mission; Zhang Hao, the Cishi (provincial governor) of Yizhou, discovered this letter at the Hangu Pass and submitted it along with the governor's name to the throne. He also presented a memorial stating that Teng had engaged in improper external dealings as an imperial official, requesting his removal from office and punishment. The emperor said: "The letter came from outside; Teng did not write it himself. It is not his fault." Thus, the memorial submitted by Zhang Hao was put aside and not acted upon. Teng did not take it to heart; he often praised and admired Zhang Hao, considering that Hao had demonstrated proper conduct in serving his superiors. Later, when Zhang Hao became Siku, he told others: "My position as a high-ranking official today is due to the kindness of Grand Secretary Cao." Teng's conduct in affairs was always like this. When Emperor Huan ascended the throne, he honored Teng as a veteran official of the previous emperor and recognized his notable loyalty and filial piety; thus, he enfeoffed him as Marquis of Feiting and granted him the special title Tejin. In the third year of Tahe, Teng was posthumously honored with the title Gao Huangdi (High Emperor). His adopted son Song succeeded him and held office up to Taiwei, but no one could verify the details of his birth or lineage. The "Xu Han Shu" states: Song, courtesy name Jugo. He had a sincere and cautious nature, and wherever he was stationed, he demonstrated loyalty and filial piety. He served as Sili Jiao Wei, and Emperor Ling promoted him to Dashinong, Dahanlu, and he succeeded Cui Lie as Taiwei. In the first year of Huangchu, Song was posthumously honored with the designation Taohuangdi (Grand Emperor). The Wu people's "Cao Man Zhuan" and Guo Ban's "Shiyu" both state: Song was the son of a Xiahou family member, and the uncle of Xiahou Dun. Taizu Cao Cao was thus a cousin to Xiahou Dun through their shared paternal uncle. Song was the father of Taizu Cao Cao.

武帝紀:
太祖少機警，有權數，而任俠放蕩，不治行業，故世人未之奇也；曹瞞傳云：太祖少好飛鷹走狗，游蕩無度，其叔父數言之於嵩。太祖患之，後逢叔父於路，乃陽敗面喎口；叔父怪而問其故，太祖曰：「卒中惡風。」叔父以告嵩。嵩驚愕，呼太祖，太祖口貌如故。嵩問曰：「叔父言汝中風，已差乎？」太祖曰：「初不中風，但失愛於叔父，故見罔耳。」嵩乃疑焉。自後叔父有所告，嵩終不復信，太祖於是益得肆意矣。惟梁國橋玄、南陽何顒異焉。玄謂太祖曰：「天下將亂，非命世之才不能濟也，能安之者，其在君乎！」魏書曰：太尉橋玄，世名知人，覩太祖而異之，曰：「吾見天下名士多矣，未有若君者也！君善自持。吾老矣！願以妻子為託。」由是聲名益重。續漢書曰：玄字公祖，嚴明有才略，長於人物。張璠漢紀曰：玄歷位中外，以剛斷稱，謙儉下士，不以王爵私親。光和中為太尉，以乆病策罷，拜太中大夫，卒，家貧乏產業，柩無所殯。當世以此稱為名臣。世語曰：玄謂太祖曰：「君未有名，可交許子將。」太祖乃造子將，子將納焉，由是知名。孫盛異同雜語云：太祖甞私入中常侍張讓室，讓覺之；乃舞手戟於庭，踰垣而出。才武絕人，莫之能害。博覽群書，特好兵法，抄集諸家兵法，名曰接要，又注孫武十三篇，皆傳於世。甞問許子將：「我何如人？」子將不荅。固問之，子將曰：「子治世之能臣，亂世之姦雄。」太祖大笑。年二十，舉孝廉為郎，除洛陽北部尉，遷頓丘令，曹瞞傳曰：太祖初入尉廨，繕治四門。造五色棒，縣門左右各十餘枚，有犯禁者，不避豪彊，皆棒殺之。後數月，靈帝愛幸小黃門蹇碩叔父夜行，即殺之。京師斂迹，莫敢犯者。近習寵臣咸疾之，然不能傷，於是共稱薦之，故遷為頓丘令。徵拜議郎。魏書曰：太祖從妹夫㶏彊侯宋奇被誅，從坐免官。後以能明古學，復徵拜議郎。先是大將軍竇武、太傅陳蕃謀誅閹官，反為所害。太祖上書陳武等正直而見陷害，姦邪盈朝，善人壅塞，其言甚切；靈帝不能用。是後詔書勑三府：舉奏州縣政理無效，民為作謠言者免罷之。三公傾邪，皆希世見用，貨賂並行，彊者為怨，不見舉奏，弱者守道，多被陷毀。太祖疾之。是歲以災異博問得失，因此復上書切諫，說三公所舉奏專回避貴戚之意。奏上，天子感寤，以示三府責讓之，諸以謠言徵者皆拜議郎。是後政教日亂，豪猾益熾，多所摧毀；太祖知不可匡正，遂不復獻言。
When young, Taizu was intelligent and alert, possessing strategic acumen; however, he indulged in chivalric behavior and lived a reckless life, neglecting scholarly pursuits or professional conduct. Therefore, the people of his time did not consider him extraordinary. The "Cao Man Zhuan" states: When young, Taizu enjoyed falconry and dog racing, wandering about without restraint; his uncle repeatedly reported this to Song. Taizu was troubled by this. Later, when he encountered his uncle on the road, he pretended to have a facial injury and a crooked mouth. His uncle was surprised and asked why this happened; Taizu replied: "I suddenly caught a severe wind." The uncle then informed Song. Song was shocked and called for Taizu, who appeared perfectly normal in both speech and appearance. Song asked: "Uncle said you had a stroke—have you already recovered?" Taizu replied: "I was never struck by wind; I have merely lost my uncle's favor, so he falsely accused me." Song then became suspicious. From that point on, whenever the uncle made accusations, Song no longer believed them; thus, Taizu was able to act with even greater freedom. Only Qiao Xuan of Liang Guo and He Yong of Nanyang regarded him as exceptional. Qiao Xuan said to Taizu: "The world is about to fall into chaos; only a man of extraordinary talent can save it. The one who will bring stability—will it be you?" The "Wei Shu" states: Grand Marshal Qiao Xuan, renowned throughout the world for his ability to discern people's character, observed Taizu and found him remarkable. He said: "I have seen many famous men of the world, but none like you!" "You should take good care of yourself." "I am old now!" "I entrust my wife and children to you." From this, Taizu's reputation grew even greater. The "Xu Han Shu" states: Xuan, courtesy name Gongzu, was strict and prudent with strategic talent; he excelled in judging people's character. Zhang Fan's "Han Ji" states: Xuan held positions both within and outside the capital, was renowned for his firmness and decisiveness, treated scholars with humility and frugality, and did not use his noble rank to favor relatives. During the Guanghe period, he served as Taiwei; due to prolonged illness, he was relieved of his post and later appointed Taizhong Dafu. Upon his death, his family was poor with no property or assets, and there were no funds for a proper burial. He was thus praised by contemporaries as an eminent official. The "Shiyu" states: Xuan said to Taizu: "You have not yet gained a reputation; you should befriend Xu Zijiang." Taizu then visited Zijiang, who accepted him as a friend. Thus, Taizu became well known. Sun Sheng's "Yitong Zayu" states: Taizu once secretly entered the residence of Zhongchangshi Zhang Rang, who discovered him. Taizu then brandished a hand 戟 (a type of weapon) in the courtyard and leaped over the wall to escape. His extraordinary talent and martial prowess made it impossible for anyone to harm him. He extensively studied a wide range of books, especially favoring military strategy. He compiled the strategies from various schools into a work titled Jieyao (Essentials), and also annotated Sun Wu's thirteen chapters on The Art of War, all of which were passed down to later generations. He once asked Xu Zijiang: "What kind of person am I?" Zijiang did not answer. He persisted in asking him, and Zijiang said: "You are a capable minister of peaceful times, yet a cunning and powerful leader of chaotic times." Taizu laughed heartily. At the age of twenty, he was recommended as a filial and upright official (Xiaolian) and appointed as Lang. He was then assigned as Bei Wei of Luoyang, later promoted to Ling of Dunqiu. The "Cao Man Zhuan" states: When Taizu first entered his post as Wei Xie, he repaired and maintained the four gates. He made five-colored rods, hanging more than ten of them on each side of the gates. Anyone who violated the laws or regulations—regardless of whether they were powerful or influential—was beaten to death with these rods. Several months later, the night-time outing of Jie Shuo, the uncle of a favored Xiao Huangmen official under Emperor Ling, was intercepted and he was executed. The capital city became orderly; no one dared to commit offenses. Nobles and favored officials all resented him, yet could not harm him; thus they jointly recommended him, so he was promoted to the position of Ling of Dunqiu. He was later summoned for appointment as Yilang. The "Wei Shu" states: Taizu's cousin's husband, Marquis Huqiang Hou Song Qi, was executed; as a result of being implicated by association, Taizu was dismissed from office. Later, due to his ability and knowledge in classical learning, he was again summoned for appointment as Yilang (Debating Official). Previously, Grand General Dou Wu and Taifu Chen Fan had plotted to eliminate the eunuchs but were instead killed by them. Taizu submitted a memorial, stating that Dou Wu and others had been upright yet wrongfully persecuted; the court was filled with villains while virtuous men were suppressed. His words were very forceful. Emperor Ling did not heed his advice. After this, an imperial edict was issued ordering the three fu (ministries): to submit reports on local officials at the state and county levels who had failed in governance or whose people composed satirical rhymes about them; such officials were to be dismissed. The Three Gong (high officials) were corrupt and biased, all seeking favor by conforming to the times; bribery was rampant. The powerful evaded blame without being reported, while the weak who upheld righteousness often suffered false accusations and ruin. Taizu deeply resented this situation. In that year, due to unusual disasters and omens, the court widely inquired about gains and losses; taking this opportunity, Taizu again submitted a memorial with urgent advice, stating that the Three Gong's reports deliberately avoided implicating powerful relatives. After his memorial was submitted, the emperor was moved and enlightened; he showed it to the Three Fu (ministries) and rebuked them. All those who had been summoned due to rhyming accusations were appointed as Yilang officials. After this, the administration and moral order grew increasingly chaotic; the powerful and lawless became more rampant, causing widespread destruction. Realizing that the situation could not be corrected, Taizu ceased to offer further advice.

武帝紀:
光和末，黃巾起。拜騎都尉，討潁川賊。遷為濟南相，國有十餘縣，長吏多阿附貴戚，贓污狼藉，於是奏免其八；禁斷淫祀，姦宄逃竄，郡界肅然。魏書曰：長吏受取貪饕，依倚貴勢，歷前相不見舉；聞太祖至，咸皆舉免，小大震怖，姦宄遁逃，竄入他郡。政教大行，一郡清平。初，城陽景王劉章以有功於漢，故其國為立祠，青州諸郡轉相倣效，濟南尤盛，至六百餘祠。賈人或假二千石輿服導從作倡樂，奢侈日甚，民坐貧窮，歷世長吏無敢禁絕者。太祖到，皆毀壞祠屋，止絕官吏民不得祠祀。及至秉政，遂除姦邪鬼神之事，世之淫祀由此遂絕。乆之，徵還為東郡太守；不就，稱疾歸鄉里。魏書曰：於是權臣專朝，貴戚橫恣。太祖不能違道取容。數數干忤，恐為家禍，遂乞留宿衞。拜議郎，常託疾病，輙告歸鄉里；築室城外，春夏習讀書傳，秋冬弋獵，以自娛樂。
In the final years of Guanghe, the Huangjin rebels rose up. He was appointed Qiduwei and dispatched to suppress bandits in Yingchuan. He was later promoted to Xiang of Jinan, where the state had more than ten counties. Many local officials flattered powerful relatives and were deeply corrupt; thus, he submitted a report requesting the dismissal of eight of them. He banned superstitious and excessive religious practices, causing criminals to flee or hide; as a result, order was restored throughout the region. The "Wei Shu" states: Local officials accepted bribes and were greedy, relying on powerful connections; previous Xiangs had not reported them. When they heard that Taizu had arrived, all of them were dismissed; both the powerful and the common people were terrified. Criminals fled and hid in other states. Governance and moral instruction flourished, bringing peace and clarity to the entire region. Initially, Chengyang Jingwang Liu Zhang had been honored with a shrine in his state for his meritorious service to the Han dynasty. The various commanderies of Qingzhou followed this example one after another, and Jinan was especially enthusiastic, establishing more than six hundred shrines. Merchants or commoners sometimes imitated the carriages, attire, and retinues of officials ranked at two thousand stones, hiring musicians to accompany them; extravagance grew increasingly severe, leaving people impoverished. For generations, local officials had dared not prohibit such practices. When Taizu arrived in office, he destroyed all the shrines and prohibited both officials and commoners from conducting religious rites or sacrifices. When he later assumed power, he completely eradicated superstitious practices involving demons and deities; from then on, excessive religious rites were abolished. After some time, he was recalled to serve as Tai Shou of Dong Jun. He did not accept the appointment but claimed illness and returned to his hometown. The "Wei Shu" states: At this time, powerful ministers monopolized court affairs, while noble relatives acted with arrogance and impunity. Taizu could not go against his principles to seek favor or approval. Repeatedly clashing with them, fearing disaster for his family, he thus requested permission to remain in the imperial guard. He was appointed as Yi Lang, but often feigned illness and would frequently request leave to return to his hometown; He built a house outside the city walls. In spring and summer, he studied books and historical records; in autumn and winter, he went hunting for recreation.

武帝紀:
頃之，兾州刺史王芬、南陽許攸、沛國周旌等連結豪傑，謀廢靈帝，立合肥侯，以告太祖，太祖拒之。芬等遂敗。司馬彪九州春秋曰：於是陳蕃子逸與術士平原襄楷會於芬坐，楷曰：「天文不利宦者，黃門、常侍貴族滅矣。」逸喜。芬曰：「若然者，芬願驅除。」於是與攸等結謀。靈帝欲北巡河間舊宅，芬等謀因此作難，上書言黑山賊攻劫郡縣，求得起兵。會北方有赤氣，東西竟天，太史上言「當有陰謀，不宜北行」，帝乃止。勑芬罷兵，俄而徵之。芬懼，自殺。魏書載太祖拒芬辭曰：「夫廢立之事，天下之至不祥也。古人有權成敗計輕重而行之者，伊尹、霍光是也。伊尹懷至忠之誠，據宰臣之勢，處官司之上，故進退廢置，計從事立。及至霍光受託國之任，藉宗臣之位，內因太后秉政之重，外有羣卿同欲之勢，昌邑即位日淺，未有貴寵，朝乏讜臣，議出密近，故計行如轉圜，事成如摧朽。今諸君徒見曩者之易，未覩當今之難。諸君自度，結衆連黨，何若七國？合肥之貴，孰若吳、楚？而造作非常，欲望必克，不亦危乎！」
Soon after, Ji Zhou Cishi Wang Fen, Nanyang Xu You, Pei Guo Zhou Jing and others linked up with powerful men to plot the removal of Emperor Ling and the installation of He Fei Hou. They informed Taizu about their plan, but he refused to participate. Wang Fen and his associates were thus defeated. Sima Biao's "Jiu Zhou Chun Qiu" states: At that time, Chen Fan's son Yi and the diviner Xiang Kai of Pingyuan met with Wang Fen. Kai said, "The celestial omens are unfavorable for eunuchs; the Huangmen and Changshi nobles will be destroyed." Yi was pleased. Wang Fen said, "If that is so, I am willing to drive them out." Thus, they conspired with Xu You and others. Emperor Ling intended to tour his former residence in Hejian, and Wang Fen and others planned to take advantage of the situation to launch an uprising. They submitted a memorial stating that the Black Mountain bandits were attacking commanderies and counties, requesting permission to raise troops. At that time, there was a red haze in the north, stretching across the sky from east to west. The imperial astronomer reported, "There is an impending conspiracy; it would be unwise to travel north." The emperor thus abandoned his plan. The emperor ordered Wang Fen to disband his troops. Soon after, he summoned him. Wang Fen was terrified and committed suicide. The "Wei Shu" records Taizu's refusal to Wang Fen, saying: "Deposing or installing an emperor is the most inauspicious act under heaven. Ancient people who weighed success and failure, considering their importance before acting were figures such as Yi Yin and Huo Guang." Yi Yin, with utmost loyalty, held the power of a prime minister and occupied the highest official position; thus, his decisions to advance or remove officials were made decisively. When it came to Huo Guang, who was entrusted with the state's affairs and held a position as a member of the imperial clan, internally he had the authority of the Empress Dowager, and externally he enjoyed the support of high-ranking officials. The Prince of Changyi had just ascended the throne and lacked influence or favor; at court there were no bold ministers to oppose him, and his decisions came from close confidants. Therefore, his plans proceeded as smoothly as turning a wheel, and matters succeeded as easily as breaking decayed wood. Now, you gentlemen only see the ease of past events but have not witnessed the difficulties of today. You should estimate for yourselves: by uniting your followers and forming factions, how do you compare to the Seven States? As for the prestige of He Fei, who can rival Wu and Chu? Yet you are undertaking extraordinary actions, hoping for certain success—does this not seem perilous!"

武帝紀:
金城邊章、韓遂殺刺史郡守以叛，衆十餘萬，天下騷動。徵太祖為典軍校尉。會靈帝崩，太子即位，太后臨朝。大將軍何進與袁紹謀誅宦官，太后不聽。進乃召董卓，欲以脅太后，魏書曰：太祖聞而笑之曰：「閹豎之官，古今宜有，但世主不當假之權寵，使至於此。旣治其罪，當誅元惡，一獄吏足矣，何必紛紛召外將乎？欲盡誅之，事必宣露，吾見其敗也。」卓未至而進見殺。卓到，廢帝為弘農王而立獻帝，京都大亂。卓表太祖為驍騎校尉，欲與計事。太祖乃變易姓名，間行東歸。魏書曰：太祖以卓終必覆敗，遂不就拜，逃歸鄉里。從數騎過故人成臯呂伯奢；伯奢不在，其子與賔客共劫太祖，取馬及物，太祖手刃擊殺數人。世語曰：太祖過伯奢。伯奢出行，五子皆在，備賔主禮。太祖自以背卓命，疑其圖己，手劔夜殺八人而去。孫盛雜記曰：太祖聞其食器聲，以為圖己，遂夜殺之。旣而悽愴曰：「寧我負人，毋人負我！」遂行。出關，過中牟，為亭長所疑，執詣縣，邑中或竊識之，為請得解。世語曰：中牟疑是亡人，見拘於縣。時掾亦已被卓書；唯功曹心知是太祖，以世方亂，不宜拘天下雄儁，因白令釋之。卓遂殺太后及弘農王。太祖至陳留，散家財，合義兵，將以誅卓。冬十二月，始起兵於己吾，世語曰：陳留孝廉衞茲以家財資太祖，使起兵，衆有五千人。是歲中平六年也。
Jincheng's Bian Zhang and Han Sui killed the Cishi and Tai Shou to rebel, mustering more than 100,000 followers and causing unrest throughout the land. Taizu was summoned to serve as a Jianjun Jiao Wei (Military Instructor). At that time, Emperor Ling died and the crown prince ascended the throne; the Empress Dowager assumed power. Grand General He Jin and Yuan Shao plotted to eliminate the eunuchs, but the empress dowager refused to listen. He Jin then summoned Dong Zhuo, intending to use him to intimidate the empress dowager. The "Wei Shu" states: Upon hearing this, Taizu laughed and said, "Eunuch officials have existed in both ancient and modern times; however, it is inappropriate for rulers of each generation not to grant them excessive power or favor, leading to such a situation. Once their crimes are established, the chief evildoers should be punished; one prison official would suffice. Why summon outside generals so recklessly? If you intend to exterminate them entirely, the matter will inevitably be exposed; I foresee your failure." Before Dong Zhuo arrived, He Jin was already killed. When Dong Zhuo arrived in the capital, he deposed the emperor and made him King of Hongnong while installing Emperor Xian as ruler. The imperial city fell into great chaos. Dong Zhuo recommended Taizu for the position of Xiaoqi Jiao Wei and wished to consult with him on matters. Taizu therefore changed his name, traveling secretly back east under an assumed identity. The "Wei Shu" states: Taizu believed that Dong Zhuo would ultimately suffer defeat, so he did not accept the appointment and fled back to his hometown. Accompanied by a few horsemen, Taizu passed through Chenggao where he visited an old acquaintance named Lü Boshen; Lü Boshen was not at home, and his son, together with guests, ambushed Taizu to seize his horses and belongings. Taizu personally killed several of them with his sword. The "Shi Yu" states: Taizu passed by Lü Boshen. Lü Boshen was away on a journey, but his five sons were at home and prepared the proper courtesy for their guest. Taizu, suspecting that they might plot against him because he had defied Dong Zhuo's orders, killed eight people with his own hands at night and left. Sun Sheng's "Za Ji" states: Taizu heard the sound of eating utensils, mistook it as a plot against himself, and so killed them at night. Later, he felt sorrowful and said, "Better that I wrong others than be wronged by them!" He then continued on his journey. After leaving the pass, he passed through Zhongmou and was suspected by a local official. He was arrested and taken to the county office. Some people in the town secretly recognized him and pleaded on his behalf, securing his release. The "Shi Yu" states: Zhongmou suspected he was a fugitive and had him detained in the county office. At that time, the clerk had also received orders from Dong Zhuo; Only the Gong Cao knew it was Taizu. Considering that the world was in chaos, he believed it unwise to detain a man of such talent and influence. He therefore advised the county magistrate to release him. Dong Zhuo then killed the empress dowager and King Hongnong. Taizu arrived at Chenliu, distributed his family's wealth, gathered righteous troops, intending to campaign against Dong Zhuo. In the twelfth month of winter, Taizu raised troops at Jiwu. The "Shi Yu" states: Chenliu's Xiaolian Wei Zi provided funds from his own family to support Taizu in raising an army, which mustered 5,000 men. This was the sixth year of Zhongping.

7
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
初平元年春正月，後將軍袁術、兾州牧韓馥、英雄記曰：馥字文節，潁川人。為御史中丞。董卓舉為兾州牧。于時兾州民人殷盛，兵糧優足。袁紹之在勃海，馥恐其興兵，遣數部從事守之，不得動搖。東郡太守橋瑁詐作京師三公移書與州郡，陳卓罪惡，云「見逼迫，無以自救，企望義兵，解國患難。」馥得移，請諸從事問曰：「今當助袁氏邪，助董卓邪？」治中從事劉子惠曰：「今興兵為國，何謂袁、董！」馥自知言短而有慙色。子惠復言：「兵者凶事，不可為首；今宜往視他州，有發動者，然後和之。兾州於他州不為弱也，他人功未有在兾州之右者也。」馥然之。馥乃作書與紹，道卓之惡，聽其舉兵。豫州刺史孔伷、英雄記曰：伷字公緒，陳留人。張璠漢紀，載鄭泰說卓云：「孔公緒能清談高論，噓枯吹生。」兖州刺史劉岱、岱，劉繇之兄，事見吳志。河內太守王匡、英雄記曰：匡字公節，泰山人。輕財好施，以任俠聞。辟大將軍何進府進符使，匡於徐州發彊弩五百西詣京師。會進敗，匡還鄉里。起家，拜河內太守。謝承後漢書曰：匡少與蔡邕善。其年為卓軍所敗，走還泰山，收集勁勇得數千人，欲與張邈合。匡先殺執金吾胡母班。班親屬不勝憤怒，與太祖并勢，共殺匡。勃海太守袁紹、陳留太守張邈、東郡太守橋瑁、英雄記曰：瑁字元偉，玄族子。先為兖州刺史，甚有威惠。山陽太守袁遺、遺字伯業，紹從兄。為長安令。河間張超甞薦遺于太尉朱儁，稱遺「有冠世之懿，幹時之量。其忠允亮直，固天所縱；若乃包羅載籍，管綜百氏，登高能賦，覩物知名，求之今日，邈焉靡儔。」事在超集。英雄記曰：紹後用遺為揚州刺史，為袁術所敗。太祖稱「長大而能勤學者，惟吾與袁伯業耳。」語在文帝典論。濟北相鮑信信事見子勛傳。同時俱起兵，衆各數萬，推紹為盟主。太祖行奮武將軍。
In the first month of spring, the first year of Chuping, General Youhou Yuan Shu, Ji Zhou Zhu Han Fu, as recorded in the "Yingxiong Ji": Han Fu's courtesy name was Wenjie; he was a native of Yingchuan. He served as Zhongcheng of the Yushi (Imperial Censorate). Dong Zhuo appointed him as Ji Zhou Zhu. At that time, Ji Zhou had a prosperous population and ample supplies of troops and grain. When Yuan Shao was in Bohai, Han Fu feared that he might raise an army and sent several officials to monitor him, preventing any movement. Tao Miao, Tai Shou of Dong Jun, forged a letter from the Three Dukes in the capital and sent it to various states and commanderies. In it he listed Dong Zhuo's crimes, stating, "We are being pressured and have no means to save ourselves; we look forward to righteous troops coming to relieve our country from this crisis." Han Fu received the letter and asked his officials, "Now, should we support Yuan Shu or Dong Zhuo?" Zhi Zhong Cong Shi Liu Zihui said, "Now raising troops for the country—what is there to distinguish between Yuan and Dong!" Han Fu realized his argument was weak and showed a look of shame. Liu Zihui added, "Military action is an ominous matter; one should not take the lead in initiating it; we should now go and observe other states first. If any state takes initiative, we can then join them." Ji Zhou is not weak compared to other states; no one else has yet achieved a feat superior to that of Ji Zhou." Han Fu agreed with this. Han Fu then wrote a letter to Yuan Shao, detailing Dong Zhuo's evils and gave him permission to raise an army. Yu Zhou Cishi Kong Zhou, as recorded in the "Yingxiong Ji": his courtesy name was Gong Xu; he was a native of Chenliu. Zhang Fan's "Han Ji" records Zheng Tai's remarks to Dong Zhuo: "Kong Gong Xu is capable of eloquent and lofty discourse, able to revive the dying with his words." Yan Zhou Cishi Liu Dai—Liu Dai was the elder brother of Liu You; details about him are recorded in the "Wu Zhi." Tai Shou of Hedong Wang Kuang, as stated in the "Yingxiong Ji": his courtesy name was Gongjie; he was a native of Tai Shan. He valued wealth lightly and enjoyed giving to others, gaining fame for his chivalrous conduct. Wang Kuang was appointed as a military officer in the service of Grand General He Jin, and from Xu Zhou he dispatched 500 strong crossbows westward to the capital. When He Jin failed, Wang Kuang returned to his hometown. He was appointed Tai Shou of Hedong from a civilian background. Xie Cheng's "Hou Han Shu" states: Wang Kuang had been on good terms with Cai Yong since his youth. That year, he was defeated by Dong Zhuo's forces and fled back to Tai Shan, where he gathered several thousand strong and brave men, intending to join Zhang Miao. Wang Kuang first killed Hu Mu Ban, the Zhuxinwu (an official title). Hu Mu Ban's relatives were furious and joined forces with Taizu to kill Wang Kuang together. Tai Shou of Bohai Yuan Shao, Tai Shou of Chenliu Zhang Miao, and Tai Shou of Dong Jun Tao Miao—according to the "Yingxiong Ji": Tao Miao's courtesy name was Yuanwei; he was a relative of the Xuan family. He had previously served as Cishi of Yan Zhou and was known for his authority and benevolence. Tai Shou of Shanyang Yuan Yi—Yuan Yi's courtesy name was Boye; he was Yuan Shao's cousin. He served as the magistrate of Chang'an. Zhang Chao of Hejian once recommended Yuan Yi to Taiwei Zhu Jun, praising him as "a man of extraordinary virtue and the capacity to manage affairs in his time." His loyalty, integrity, and uprightness are indeed gifts from heaven; If one considers his ability to master all written works, synthesize the teachings of a hundred schools, compose poetry when inspired by lofty sights, and recognize things upon seeing them—such talents are unmatched in our time." This account is found in Zhang Chao's collected writings. The "Yingxiong Ji" states: Later, Yuan Shao appointed Yuan Yi as Cishi of Yang Zhou, but he was defeated by Yuan Shu. Taizu once said, "Those who grow old while diligently studying are only me and Yuan Boye." This statement is recorded in the "Dian Lun" of Emperor Wen. Bao Xin, Xiang of Jibei—his deeds are recorded in the biography of his son Bao Xun. At the same time, they all raised armies, each with tens of thousands of troops, and they elected Yuan Shao as their leader. Taizu served as General of Martial Valor (Fenwu Jiangjun).

武帝紀:
二月，卓聞兵起，乃徙天子都長安。卓留屯洛陽，遂焚宮室。是時紹屯河內，邈、岱、瑁、遺屯酸棗，術屯南陽，伷屯潁川，馥在鄴。卓兵彊，紹等莫敢先進。太祖曰：「舉義兵以誅暴亂，大衆已合，諸君何疑？向使董卓聞山東兵起，倚王室之重，據二周之險，東向以臨天下；雖以無道行之，猶足為患。今焚燒宮室，劫遷天子，海內震動，不知所歸，此天亡之時也。一戰而天下定矣，不可失也。」遂引兵西，將據成臯。邈遣將衞茲分兵隨太祖。到熒陽汴水，遇卓將徐榮，與戰不利，士卒死傷甚多。太祖為流矢所中，所乘馬被創，從弟洪以馬與太祖，得夜遁去。榮見太祖所將兵少，力戰盡日，謂酸棗未易攻也，亦引兵還。
In the second month, Dou Zhuo learned that troops had been raised against him and thus moved the Son of Heaven to Chang'an. Dou Zhuo remained stationed in Luoyang and proceeded to burn the palaces and buildings. At that time, Yuan Shao was stationed in He Nei; Pei Mo, Dai, Mao, and Yuan Yi were stationed at Suanzao; Yuan Shu was stationed in Nanyang; Zhong Zou was stationed in Yingchuan; and Fu Fu was in Ye. Dou Zhuo's forces were strong, so Yuan Shao and others dared not advance first. Taizu said, "We raised this righteous army to punish the tyrant and chaos; our forces have already gathered. What are you gentlemen hesitating about?" Had Dong Zhuo heard that troops had risen in Shandong, relied on the authority of the imperial court, occupied the strategic positions of the two Zhou regions, and faced east to confront the empire; Even if he had acted without morality, it would still have been sufficient to cause trouble. Now he has burned the palaces and seized the Son of Heaven, causing turmoil throughout the realm and leaving people uncertain where to turn—this is precisely the time for heaven to destroy him. "One battle will decide the fate of the empire; we must not miss this opportunity." He then led his troops westward, intending to occupy Chenggao. Pei Mo sent a general named Wei Zi to lead part of the army and accompany Taizu. When they reached Yingyang by the Bian River, they encountered Xu Rong, a general of Dou Zhuo. They engaged in battle but were defeated, suffering heavy casualties among their soldiers. Taizu was struck by a stray arrow, and the horse he rode was wounded. His cousin Cao Hong gave his own horse to Taizu, allowing him to escape under cover of night. Xu Rong saw that the number of troops Taizu commanded was small and, after a day of fierce fighting, concluded that Suanzao would not be easy to attack. He therefore withdrew his forces as well.

武帝紀:
太祖到酸棗，諸軍兵十餘萬，日置酒高會，不圖進取。太祖責讓之，因為謀曰：「諸君聽吾計，使勃海引河內之衆臨孟津，酸棗諸將守成臯，據敖倉，塞轘轅、太谷，全制其險；使袁將軍率南陽之軍軍丹、析，入武關，以震三輔：皆高壘深壁，勿與戰，益為疑兵，示天下形勢，以順誅逆，可立定也。今兵以義動，持疑而不進，失天下之望，竊為諸君耻之！」邈等不能用。
When Taizu arrived at Suanzao, the combined forces of all the armies totaled more than 100,000. Every day they held grand banquets and drinking sessions without making plans for further military advances. Taizu rebuked them, and then proposed a plan: "If you all follow my strategy, let Bohai lead the troops from He Nei to Lin Mengjin. The generals at Suanzao should hold Chenggao, occupy Aocang, block Huan Yuan and Taigu, and fully control these strategic passes; let General Yuan lead the army from Nanyang to Dan and Xi, enter Wu Guan, and threaten the Three Fu regions: all should build high walls and deep fortifications, avoid battle, create more decoy forces, demonstrate our strategic advantage to the world, and by following righteousness to punish rebellion, we can quickly achieve victory. "Now that our troops have been raised in the name of justice, yet you hesitate and do not advance, this will disappoint the hopes of the people. I secretly feel ashamed for all of you!" Pei Mo and others did not adopt his plan.

武帝紀:
太祖兵少，乃與夏侯惇等詣揚州募兵，刺史陳溫、丹楊太守周昕與兵四千餘人。還到龍亢，士卒多叛。魏書曰：兵謀叛，夜燒太祖帳，太祖手劔殺數十人，餘皆披靡，乃得出營；其不叛者五百餘人。至銍、建平，復收兵得千餘人，進屯河內。
As Taizu's forces were few, he went with Xiahou Dun and others to Yang Zhou to recruit soldiers. Cishi Chen Wen and Tai Shou of Danyang, Zhou Xin, provided more than 4,000 troops for him. When they returned to Longkang, many soldiers defected. The "Wei Shu" states: The troops plotted to rebel and burned Taizu's tent at night. Taizu personally wielded a sword, killing dozens of them; the rest were routed, allowing him to leave the camp; more than 500 soldiers did not rebel. Upon arriving at Zhi and Jianping, he recruited more troops and gathered over a thousand men, then advanced to station in He Nei.

劉岱與橋瑁相惡，岱殺瑁，以王肱領東郡太守。
Liu Dai had a hostile relationship with Qiao Mao; Liu Dai killed Qiao Mao and appointed Wang Geng as the new Tai Shou of Dong Jun.

武帝紀:
袁紹與韓馥謀立幽州牧劉虞為帝，太祖拒之。魏書載太祖荅紹曰：「董卓之罪，暴於四海，吾等合大衆興義兵，遠近莫不響應，此以義動故也。今幼主微弱，制於姦臣，未有昌邑亡國之釁，而一旦改易，天下其孰安之？諸君北面，我自西向。」紹又甞得一玉印，於太祖坐中舉向其肘，太祖由是笑而惡焉。魏書曰：太祖大笑曰：「吾不聽汝也。」紹復使人說太祖曰：「今袁公勢盛兵彊，二子已長，天下羣英，孰踰於此？」太祖不應。由是益不直紹，圖誅滅之。
Yuan Shao plotted with Han Fu to support You Zhou Zhu Liu Yu as emperor, but Taizu opposed this plan. The "Wei Shu" records Taizu's reply to Yuan Shao: "Dong Zhuo's crimes are notorious throughout the world. We gathered a large force and raised a righteous army, and both near and far responded enthusiastically—this was because we acted in accordance with righteousness." "Now the young emperor is weak and controlled by corrupt ministers. There has been no clear sign of a national crisis like that which led to the fall of Changyi, yet we suddenly consider changing the ruler—how will the people know where stability lies?" "You gentlemen may face north and support Yuan Shao; I shall head west on my own path." Yuan Shao once obtained a jade seal and, in Taizu's presence, held it up to his elbow. Upon this, Taizu laughed but felt resentment toward him. The "Wei Shu" states: Taizu burst into laughter and said, "I will not listen to you." Yuan Shao then sent someone else to persuade Taizu, saying: "Now General Yuan's power is strong and his army mighty; his two sons have already grown up. Among the many outstanding figures in the world, who surpasses him?" Taizu did not respond. From then on, Taizu became even more critical of Yuan Shao and plotted to eliminate him.

In spring of the second year, Yuan Shao and Han Fu proceeded to proclaim Liu Yu as emperor; however, Liu Yu ultimately dared not accept it.

武帝紀:
黑山賊于毒、白繞、眭固等眭，申隨反。十餘萬衆略魏郡、東郡，王肱不能禦，太祖引兵入東郡，擊白繞於濮陽，破之。袁紹因表太祖為東郡太守，治東武陽。
The Heishan bandits Yu Du, Bai RAO, Sui Gu, etc., rebelled in Shen sui. With more than 100, 000 troops, they raided Wei Jun and Dong Jun. Wang Geng could not resist them, so Taizu led his army into Dong Jun and attacked Bai RAO in Puyang, defeating him. Yuan Shao therefore recommended Taizu as Tai Shou of Dong Ju, with his seat at Dongwuyang.

17
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
三年春，太祖軍頓丘，毒等攻東武陽。太祖乃引兵西入山，攻毒等本屯。魏書曰：諸將皆以為當還自救。太祖曰：「孫臏救趙而攻魏，耿弇欲走西安攻臨菑。使賊聞我西而還，武陽自解也；不還，我能敗其本屯，虜不能拔武陽必矣。」遂乃行。毒聞之，棄武陽還。太祖要擊眭固，又擊匈奴於夫羅於內黃，皆大破之。魏書曰：於夫羅者，南單于子也。中平中，發匈奴兵，於夫羅率以助漢。會本國反，殺南單于，於夫羅遂將其衆留中國。因天下撓亂，與西河白波賊合，破太原、河內，抄略諸郡為寇。
In spring of the third year, Taizu's army was stationed in Dunqiu when Yu Du and others attacked Dongwuyang. Taizu then led his troops west into the mountains to attack Yu Du's main encampment. The "Wei Shu" states: All the generals believed they should return to defend themselves. Taizu said, "Sun Bin saved Zhao by attacking Wei; Geng Yan wanted to move westward to Xian'an and attack Linzi. If the bandits hear that I have moved west and return, then Wuyang will naturally be relieved; if they do not return, I can defeat their main encampment, and the bandits certainly cannot capture Wuyang." He then proceeded with his plan. Upon hearing this, Yu Du abandoned Wuyang and returned. Taizu ambushed Sui Gu and also defeated the Xiongnu leader Yuluo at Neihuang, achieving decisive victories in both battles. The "Wei Shu" states: Yuluo was the son of Nan Chanyu. During the middle of Zhongping, Xiongnu troops were mobilized, and Yuluo led them to assist the Han dynasty. However, when a rebellion broke out in his homeland and killed Nan Chanyu, Yuluo decided to remain in China with his troops. Taking advantage of the chaos throughout the land, he allied with the Baibo bandits from Xhe and attacked Taiyuan and He Nei, raiding various commanderies as a marauder.

武帝紀:
夏四月，司徒王允與呂布共殺卓。卓將李傕、郭汜等殺允攻布，布敗，東出武關。傕等擅朝政。
In the fourth month of summer (April 23, 192 AD), Situ Wang Yun and Lü Bu jointly killed Dou Zhuo. Dou Zhuo's generals Li Jue and Guo Si, among others, killed Wang Yun and attacked Lü Bu; Lü Bu was defeated and fled east through Wu Guan. Li Jue and others seized control of the imperial government.

19
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
青州黃巾衆百萬入兖州，殺任城相鄭遂，轉入東平。劉岱欲擊之，鮑信諫曰：「今賊衆百萬，百姓皆震恐，士卒無鬬志，不可敵也。觀賊衆羣輩相隨，軍無輜重，唯以鈔略為資，今不若畜士衆之力，先為固守。彼欲戰不得，攻又不能，其勢必離散，後選精銳，據其要害，擊之可破也。」岱不從，遂與戰，果為所殺。世語曰：岱旣死，陳宮謂太祖曰：「州今無主，而王命斷絕，宮請說州中，明府尋往牧之，資之以收天下，此霸王之業也。」宮說別駕、治中曰：「今天下分裂而州無主；曹東郡，命世之才也，若迎以牧州，必寧生民。」鮑信等亦謂之然。信乃與州吏萬潛等至東郡迎太祖領兖州牧。遂進兵擊黃巾於壽張東。信力戰鬬死，僅而破之。魏書曰：太祖將步騎千餘人，行視戰地，卒抵賊營，戰不利，死者數百人，引還。賊尋前進。黃巾為賊久，數乘勝，兵皆精悍。太祖舊兵少，新兵不習練，舉軍皆懼。太祖被甲嬰冑，親巡將士，明勸賞罰，衆乃復奮，承間討擊，賊稍折退。賊乃移書太祖曰：「昔在濟南，毀壞神壇，其道乃與中黃太一同，似若知道，今更迷惑。漢行已盡，黃家當立。天之大運，非君才力所能存也。」太祖見檄書，呵之罪，數開示降路；遂設奇伏，晝夜會戰，戰輙禽獲，賊乃退走。購求信喪不得，衆乃刻木如信形狀，祭而哭焉。追黃巾至濟北。乞降。冬，受降卒三十餘萬，男女百餘萬口，收其精銳者，號為青州兵。
A million Yellow Turban rebels from Qing Zhou entered Yan Zhou, killing Tai Shou Zheng Sui of Rencheng and advancing into Dongping. Liu Dai wanted to attack them, but Bao Xin advised him: "Now the rebels number in the millions; the people are all frightened and terrified, while our soldiers have no fighting spirit. We cannot match their strength. Observing that the rebel forces consist of loosely organized groups, their army lacks supplies and depends solely on plunder for sustenance. Therefore, we should now conserve our strength, train our troops, and first establish a strong defense." "They will be unable to fight if we do not engage them, and they cannot sustain an attack on us. Their forces are bound to disperse eventually. After that, we can select our elite troops, occupy their key positions, and defeat them." Liu Dai did not follow this advice and engaged the rebels in battle. As predicted, he was indeed killed by them. The "Shi Yu" states: After Liu Dai died, Chen Gong said to Taizu: "Now the state has no ruler and imperial authority is cut off. I will go persuade the people of the state; you may follow soon after to govern them. With their support, you can gather strength to control the empire—this would be a path to hegemony or kingship." Chen Gong persuaded Biejia and Zhizhong, saying: "Now the empire is divided and our state has no ruler; Cao Dongjun (Taizu) is a man of extraordinary talent. If we invite him to govern our state, he will surely bring peace and stability to the people." Bao Xin and others also agreed with this view. Bao Xin then went together with state officials Wan Qian and others to Dong Jun to welcome Taizu as the new Tai Ju of Yan Zhou. They then advanced their troops and attacked the Yellow Turbans east of Shouzhang. Bao Xin fought bravely until he died, and only narrowly managed to defeat them. The "Wei Shu" states: Taizu led more than a thousand infantry and cavalry to inspect the battlefield, but unexpectedly encountered the enemy camp. The battle went poorly for them, with hundreds of soldiers killed before they retreated. The rebels soon advanced further. The Yellow Turbans had been bandits for a long time and had won several victories, so their troops were all experienced and fierce fighters. Taizu's veteran forces were few in number, and his new recruits lacked training; the entire army was filled with fear. Taizu donned armor and a helmet, personally inspected the soldiers, clearly encouraged them with rewards and punishments, and thus inspired their morale. Seizing opportunities to attack, they gradually wore down and forced back the rebels. The rebels then sent a letter to Taizu saying: "In the past, in Jinan, you destroyed shrines and altars; your path is similar to that of Zhonghuang Taiyi. It seemed as if you understood the Dao, yet now you are confused again." "The Han dynasty's mandate has ended; it is time for the Huang family to rise and take power. The great course of heaven cannot be altered by your talents or strength." Upon reading the rebels' letter, Taizu rebuked them for their crimes and repeatedly offered them a path to surrender; he then set up ambushes, engaged in battles day and night, capturing many rebels each time they fought. Eventually, the rebels withdrew. Unable to find Bao Xin's body for purchase or recovery, his troops carved a wooden figure resembling him and held a funeral ceremony, weeping over it. They pursued the Yellow Turbans as far as Jibei. The rebels requested to surrender. In winter, they accepted the surrender of more than 300,000 rebel soldiers and over a million men and women. They recruited the most capable among them, naming this force the Qing Zhou Army.

袁術與紹有隙，術求援於公孫瓚，瓚使劉備屯高唐，單經屯平原，陶謙屯發干，以逼紹。太祖與紹會擊，皆破之。
Yuan Shu had a conflict with Yuan Shao and sought support from Gong Sun Zan. Gong Sun Zan sent Liu Bei to station at Gaotang, Liu Jing to station at Pingyuan, and Tao Qian to station at Fagang in order to pressure Yuan Shao. Taizu joined forces with Yuan Shao to attack them and defeated all of their forces.

武帝紀:
四年春，軍鄄城。荊州牧劉表斷術糧道，術引軍入陳留，屯封丘，黑山餘賊及於夫羅等佐之。術使將劉詳屯匡亭。太祖擊詳，術救之，與戰，大破之。術退保封丘，遂圍之，未合，術走襄邑，追到太壽，決渠水灌城。走寧陵，又追之，走九江。夏，太祖還軍定陶。
In spring of the fourth year, Taizu stationed his army at Juancheng. Zhou Jun Zhu Liu Biao cut off Yuan Shu's supply lines. Yuan Shu led his army into Chenliu, stationed at Fengqiu, and was assisted by the remaining Heishan rebels as well as Yuluo and others. Yuan Shu sent a general named Liu Xiang to station troops at Kuangting. Taizu attacked Liu Xiang, and Yuan Shu came to his rescue. They engaged in battle, and Taizu decisively defeated them. Yuan Shu retreated to defend Fengqiu, so Taizu surrounded the city. Before the encirclement was complete, Yuan Shu fled to Xiangyi. Taizu pursued him as far as Taishou and diverted water from a canal to flood the city walls. Yuan Shu fled to Ningling, but Taizu continued in pursuit, forcing him to flee further to Jiujiang. In summer, Taizu returned his army to Dingtao.

下邳闕宣聚衆數千人，自稱天子；徐州牧陶謙與共舉兵，取泰山華、費，略任城。秋，太祖征陶謙，下十餘城，謙守城不敢出。
Que Xuan of Xiapi gathered several thousand followers and proclaimed himself emperor; Tao Qian, the Inspector of Xu Zhou, joined forces with him to raise an army, captured Huai and Fei in Tai Shan, and raided Rencheng. In autumn, Taizu launched a campaign against Tao Qian, capturing more than ten cities; Tao Qian remained within the city and dared not come out to fight.

In this year, Sun Ce accepted a mission from Yuan Shu to cross the Yangtze River and within several years came to control Jiangdong.

武帝紀:
興平元年春，太祖自徐州還，初，太祖父嵩去官後還譙，董卓之亂，避難琅邪，為陶謙所害，故太祖志在復讎東伐。世語曰：嵩在泰山華縣。太祖令泰山太守應劭送家詣兖州，劭兵未至，陶謙密遣數千騎掩捕。嵩家以為劭迎，不設備。謙兵至，殺太祖弟德於門中。嵩懼，穿後垣，先出其妾，妾肥，不時得出；嵩逃于厠，與妾俱被害，闔門皆死。劭懼，棄官赴袁紹。後太祖定兾州，劭時已死。韋曜吳書曰：太祖迎嵩，輜重百餘兩。陶謙遣都尉張闓將騎二百衞送，闓於泰山華、費間殺嵩，取財物，因奔淮南。太祖歸咎於陶謙，故伐之。夏，使荀彧、程昱守鄄城，復征陶謙，拔五城，遂略地至東海。還過郯，謙將曹豹與劉備屯郯東，要太祖。太祖擊破之，遂攻拔襄賁，所過多所殘戮。孫盛曰：夫伐罪弔民，古之令軌；罪謙之由，而殘其屬部，過矣。
In spring of Xingping Yuan Nian, Taizu returned from Xu Zhou. Initially, after his grandfather Cao Song retired from office and returned to Qiao, during the turmoil caused by Dong Zhuo, he fled for safety to Langya but was killed by Tao Qian; thus, Taizu had long been determined to avenge this death and launch an eastern campaign. The Shiyu states: Cao Song was in Huaxian, Tai Shan. Taizu ordered Ying Shao, the Inspector of Tai Shan, to escort his family to Yan Zhou. Before Ying Shao's troops arrived, Tao Qian secretly dispatched several thousand cavalrymen to launch a surprise attack and capture them. Cao Song's family believed that Ying Shao was coming to escort them and did not prepare for defense. When Tao Qian's troops arrived, they killed Taizu's younger brother Cao De at the gate. Cao Song was terrified and dug through the rear wall to escape, sending out his concubine first. The concubine was fat and could not get out quickly; Cao Song fled into the latrine, but he and his concubine were both killed, and all members of their household perished. Fearing for his life, Ying Shao abandoned his post and fled to Yuan Shao. Later, when Taizu pacified Ji Zhou, Ying Shao had already died by then. Wei Yao's Wu Shu states: Taizu went to escort Cao Song back and brought over a hundred carts of supplies and belongings. Tao Qian dispatched Du Wei Zhang Kai to lead 200 cavalrymen as an escort. Zhang Kai killed Cao Song between Huaxian and Feixian in Tai Shan, seized the valuables, and then fled to Huaibei. Taizu blamed Tao Qian for this incident and thus launched a campaign against him. In summer, he ordered Xun Yu and Cheng Yu to defend Juancheng and personally led another campaign against Tao Qian. He captured five cities and continued advancing as far east as Donghai. On his return journey, passing through Tan, Tao Qian's general Cao Bao and Liu Bei were stationed east of Tan to intercept Taizu. Taizu defeated them, then attacked and captured Xiangben, committing many acts of destruction and slaughter in the areas he passed through. Sun Sheng said: Punishing the guilty and relieving the people is an ancient principle; yet to punish Tao Qian for his crimes while mercilessly slaughtering his subordinates was excessive.

武帝紀:
會張邈與陳宮叛迎呂布，郡縣皆應。荀彧、程昱保鄄城，范、東阿二縣固守，太祖乃引軍還。布到，攻鄄城不能下，西屯濮陽。太祖曰：「布一旦得一州，不能據東平，斷亢父、泰山之道，乘險要我，而乃屯濮陽，吾知其無能為也。」遂進軍攻之。布出兵戰，先以騎犯青州兵。青州兵奔，太祖陳亂馳突火出，墜馬，燒左手掌。司馬樓異扶太祖上馬，遂引去。袁暐獻帝春秋曰：太祖圍濮陽，濮陽大姓田氏為反閒，太祖得入城。燒其東門，示無反意。及戰，軍敗。布騎得太祖而不知是，問曰：「曹操何在？」太祖曰：「乘黃馬走者是也。」布騎乃釋太祖而追黃馬者。門火猶盛，太祖突火而出。未至營止，諸將未與太祖相見，皆怖。太祖乃自力勞軍，令軍中促為攻具，進復攻之，與布相守百餘日。蝗蟲起，百姓大餓，布糧食亦盡，各引去。
At this time, Zhang Miao and Chen Gong rebelled to welcome Lu Bu, and the commanderies and counties all responded in support. Xun Yu and Cheng Yu defended Juancheng, while Fan and Donga counties held out resolutely. Taizu therefore withdrew his army. When Lu Bu arrived, he attacked Juancheng but failed to capture it, so he moved west and stationed at Puyang. Taizu said, "Lu Bu gained a whole province in one day but failed to occupy Dongping and cut off the Kangfu and Tai Shan roads. Instead of taking advantage of the terrain to attack me from a strong position, he has stationed at Puyang; I now know that he is incapable." He then advanced his army and attacked Lu Bu. Lu Bu sent out troops to engage in battle, first using cavalry to attack the Qingzhou Army. The Qingzhou soldiers fled in panic; Taizu's formation became disordered as he rushed to break through the flames, fell from his horse, and burned the palm of his left hand. Shimaren Lou Yi helped Taizu back onto his horse, then led him away. Yuan Wei's Spring and Autumn Annals of the Xian Di records: Taizu besieged Puyang, where a prominent local family named Tian conspired to betray Lu Bu from within. With their help, Taizu was able to enter the city. He set fire to its eastern gate as a demonstration of his lack of treacherous intent. When the battle commenced, Taizu's forces were defeated. Lu Bu's cavalry captured Taizu but did not recognize him and asked, "Where is Cao Cao?" Taizu replied, "The one riding the yellow horse who fled was me." Lu Bu's cavalry then released Taizu and pursued the rider on the yellow horse. The fire at the gate was still intense, so Taizu broke through the flames to escape. Before reaching his camp and stopping, none of the generals had yet seen Taizu, and they were all terrified. Taizu then personally visited the troops to encourage them, ordered the army to quickly prepare siege equipment, and launched another attack. He and Lu Bu engaged in a prolonged standoff lasting over 100 days. A locust plague broke out, causing widespread famine among the people; Lu Bu's supplies were also exhausted, so both sides withdrew.

秋九月，太祖還鄄城。布到乘氏，為其縣人李進所破，東屯山陽。於是紹使人說太祖，欲連和。太祖新失兖州，軍食盡，將許之。程昱止太祖，太祖從之。冬十月，太祖至東阿。
In the ninth month of autumn, Taizu returned to Juancheng. Lu Bu arrived at Chengshi but was defeated by a local named Li Jin from the county and retreated eastward, stationing his troops in Shanyang. At this time, Yuan Shao sent envoys to persuade Taizu, seeking an alliance. Taizu had just lost Yan Zhou and his army was out of food; he nearly agreed to the proposal. Cheng Yu dissuaded Taizu, who then followed his advice. In the tenth month of winter, Taizu arrived at Donga.

In this year, a single hu of grain cost over 500,000 coins; people resorted to cannibalism, so Taizu dismissed newly recruited soldiers and officials. Tao Qian died, and Liu Bei succeeded him.

武帝紀:
二年春，襲定陶。濟陰太守吳資保南城，未拔。會呂布至，又擊破之。夏，布將薛蘭、李封屯鉅野，太祖攻之，布救蘭，蘭敗，布走，遂斬蘭等。布復從東緍與陳宮將萬餘人來戰，時太祖兵少，設伏，縱奇兵擊，大破之。魏書曰：於是兵皆出取麥，在者不能千人，屯營不固。太祖乃令婦人守陴，悉兵拒之。屯西有大隄，其南樹木幽深。布疑有伏，乃相謂曰：「曹操多譎，勿入伏中。」引軍屯南十餘里。明日復來，太祖隱兵隄裏，出半兵隄外。布益進，乃令輕兵挑戰，旣合，伏兵乃悉乘隄，步騎並進，大破之，獲其龍車，追至其營而還。布夜走，太祖復攻，拔定陶，分兵平諸縣。布東奔劉備，張邈從布，使其弟超將家屬保雍丘。秋八月，圍雍丘。冬十月，天子拜太祖兖州牧。十二月，雍丘潰，超自殺。夷邈三族。邈詣袁術請救，為其衆所殺，兖州平，遂東略陳地。
In spring of the second year, Taizu launched a surprise attack on Dingtao. Wu Zi, the Inspector of Ji Yin, defended Nancheng and held out; it was not captured. Just then Lu Bu arrived and attacked Taizu's forces, defeating them again. In summer, Lu Bu's generals Xue Lan and Li Feng stationed at Juye. Taizu attacked them, and Lu Bu came to their rescue. When Xue Lan was defeated, Lu Bu fled, and Taizu beheaded Xue Lan and others. Lu Bu then regrouped at Dongjun with Chen Gong and over 10,000 troops to fight again. At the time, Taizu's army was outnumbered; he set up an ambush and launched a surprise attack, decisively defeating them. The Wei Shu records: At this time, most of the soldiers had gone out to harvest wheat; fewer than a thousand remained in camp, and their encampment was not secure. Taizu therefore ordered women to man the city walls while he deployed all his troops for battle. To the west of the encampment was a large dike, and south of it were dense, deep woods. Lu Bu suspected an ambush and said to his men, "Cao Cao is full of tricks; do not fall into an ambush." He led his army and stationed it more than ten li south. The next day, Lu Bu returned; Taizu concealed the main part of his troops behind the dike and deployed half of them in front. Lu Bu advanced further, and Taizu ordered a small force to provoke an attack. After the battle began, his hidden troops suddenly emerged from behind the dike, with infantry and cavalry advancing together, decisively defeating Lu Bu's forces. They captured Lu Bu's dragon chariot and pursued them all the way back to their camp before returning. At night, Lu Bu fled; Taizu launched another attack, captured Dingtao, and dispatched troops to pacify the surrounding counties. Lu Bu fled eastward to seek refuge with Liu Bei; Zhang Miao followed Lu Bu and sent his younger brother Zhang Chao to guard Yongqiu with their family. In the eighth month of autumn, Taizu laid siege to Yongqiu. In the tenth month of winter, the Son of Heaven appointed Taizu as Inspector of Yan Zhou. In December, Yongqiu fell and Zhang Chao committed suicide. The three clans of Zhang Miao were exterminated. Zhang Miao went to Yuan Shu for help but was killed by Yuan's troops; with Yan Zhou pacified, Taizu then moved eastward and launched a campaign in the territory of Chen.

In this year, chaos erupted in Chang'an; the Son of Heaven attempted to move eastward but was defeated at Caoyang and crossed the Yellow River to take refuge in Anyi.

太祖將迎天子，諸將或疑，荀彧、程昱勸之，乃遣曹洪將兵西迎，衞將軍董承與袁術將萇奴拒險，洪不得進。
Taizu planned to escort the Son of Heaven, but some of his generals were doubtful. Xun Yu and Cheng Yu advised him, so he sent Cao Hong with troops westward to meet the emperor. However, Wei Jiangjun Dong Cheng and Yuan Shu's general Chang Nu blocked the mountain passes, preventing Cao Hong from advancing.

32
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
汝南、潁川黃巾何儀、劉辟、黃邵、何曼等，衆各數萬，初應袁術，又附孫堅。二月，太祖進軍討破之，斬辟、邵等，儀及其衆皆降。天子拜太祖建德將軍，夏六月，遷鎮東將軍，封費亭侯。秋七月，楊奉、韓暹以天子還洛陽，獻帝春秋曰：天子初至洛陽，幸城西故中常侍趙忠宅。使張楊繕治宮室，名殿曰揚安殿，八月，帝乃遷居。奉別屯梁。太祖遂至洛陽，衞京都，暹遁走。天子假太祖節鉞，錄尚書事。獻帝紀曰：又領司隷校尉。洛陽殘破，董昭等勸太祖都許。九月，車駕出轘轅而東，以太祖為大將軍，封武平侯。自天子西遷，朝廷日亂，至是宗廟社稷制度始立。張璠漢紀曰：初，天子敗於曹陽，欲浮河東下。侍中太史令王立曰：「自去春太白犯鎮星於牛斗，過天津，熒惑又逆行守北河，不可犯也。」由是天子遂不北渡河，將自軹關東出。立又謂宗正劉艾曰：「前太白守天關，與熒惑會；金火交會，革命之象也。漢祚終矣，晉、魏必有興者。」立後數言於帝曰：「天命有去就，五行不常盛，代火者土也，承漢者魏也，能安天下者，曹姓也，唯委任曹氏而已。」公聞之，使人語立曰：「知公忠於朝廷，然天道深遠，幸勿多言。」
The Yellow Turban rebels He Yi, Liu Bi, Huang Shao, and He Man from Ruanan and Yingchuan each commanded tens of thousands of followers. Initially they had supported Yuan Shu but later submitted to Sun Jian. In the second month, Taizu advanced his army and defeated them, beheading Liu Bi, Huang Shao and others; He Yi and his followers all surrendered. The Son of Heaven appointed Taizu General Jiande. In the sixth month of summer, he was promoted to General Zhendong and enfeoffed as Marquis Feiting. In the seventh month of autumn, Yang Feng and Han Xian escorted the Son of Heaven back to Luoyang. The Spring and Autumn Annals of Emperor Xian records: When the emperor first arrived in Luoyang, he stayed at the former residence of Zhongchangshi Zhao Zhong west of the city. They ordered Zhang Yang to repair and renovate the palace buildings, naming the main hall Yang'an Hall; in August, the emperor moved into his new residence. Yang Feng stationed separately at Liang. Taizu then arrived in Luoyang to guard the capital, and Han Xian fled. The Son of Heaven granted Taizu a ceremonial scepter and axe, authorizing him to oversee official affairs as Grand Secretary. The Records of Emperor Xian states: He was also appointed Inspector-in-Chief (Sili Jiao Wei). Luoyang had been left in ruins, and Dong Zhao and others advised Taizu to make Xu Zhou the new capital. In September, the imperial procession departed Huanyuan and moved eastward; Taizu was appointed Grand General and enfeoffed as Hou of Wuping. Since the Son of Heaven moved westward, the imperial court had grown increasingly chaotic; only now did systems for ancestral temples and state rituals begin to be established. Zhang Fan's Han Ji records: Initially, when the Son of Heaven was defeated at Caoyang, he intended to float downstream along the Yellow River. Shizhong and Taishi Ling Wang Li said, "Since last spring, the planet Venus has invaded Jupiter in the constellations of Niu and Dou, passed through Tianjin, and Mars has also moved retrograde to guard Bei He. This is an omen that must not be ignored." Because of this, the Son of Heaven decided not to cross northward over the Yellow River but instead planned to head east through Zhiguan Pass. Wang Li also told Zongzheng Liu Ai, "Previously, Venus occupied Tian Guan and met with Mars; the conjunction of metal and fire is an omen of a change in dynastic rule. "The Han dynasty's mandate has come to an end; the Jin or Wei must inevitably rise." Later, Wang Li repeatedly advised the emperor saying, "Heaven's mandate has its departures and arrivals; the Five Elements do not remain in perpetual dominance. The element that succeeds fire is earth, and the one that inherits from Han is Wei. He who can bring peace to the world will be of the Cao surname; all you need do is entrust authority to the Cao family." Upon hearing this, Gong sent someone to tell Wang Li, "I know you are loyal to the court, but heavenly principles are profound and distant. I hope you will not speak so much."

33
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
天子之東也，奉自梁欲要之，不及。冬十月，公征奉，奉南奔袁術，遂攻其梁屯，拔之。於是以袁紹為太尉，紹恥班在公下，不肯受。公乃固辭，以大將軍讓紹。天子拜公司空，行車騎將軍。是歲用棗祗、韓浩等議，始興屯田。魏書曰：自遭荒亂，率乏糧穀。諸軍並起，無終歲之計，饑則寇略，飽則棄餘，瓦解流離，無敵自破者不可勝數。袁紹之在河北，軍人仰食桑椹。袁術在江、淮，取給蒲蠃。民人相食，州里蕭條。公曰：「夫定國之術，在於彊兵足食，秦人以急農兼天下，孝武以屯田定西域，此先代之良式也。」是歲乃募民屯田許下，得穀百萬斛。於是州郡例置田官，所在積穀。征伐四方，無運糧之勞，遂兼滅羣賊，克平天下。
When the Son of Heaven traveled eastward, Feng, starting from Liang, wished to intercept him but failed to catch up. In the tenth month of winter, Gong launched a campaign against Feng. Feng fled south to Yuan Shu, and thus Gong attacked Feng's encampment at Liang and captured it. Therefore, Yuan Shao was appointed as Taiwei (Grand Commandant), but Shao felt ashamed that his rank was below Gong's and refused to accept the post. Gong then firmly declined, offering the position of Grand General to Yuan Shao. The Son of Heaven appointed Gong as Sikong and granted him the acting title of Jiangjun of Chariot and Cavalry. In this year, following the proposals of Zao Zhi, Han Hao, and others, the system of military farming was first initiated. The Wei Shu states: Since suffering from famine and chaos, provisions were generally scarce. All the armies arose together, without long-term planning; when hungry they raided and plundered, and when well-fed they discarded leftovers. Troops disintegrated and scattered, falling apart on their own without facing an enemy—such cases were too numerous to count. When Yuan Shao was in Hebei, his soldiers relied on mulberries for food. Yuan Shu in the Jiang and Huai regions obtained supplies from lotus seeds. The people resorted to cannibalism, and villages lay desolate. Gong said, "The method to stabilize a state lies in strengthening the military and ensuring sufficient food. The Qin people unified the world by enforcing agricultural policies, and Emperor Wu of Han pacified the Western Regions through 屯田 (military farming). These are exemplary models from previous dynasties." In this year, he recruited civilians to cultivate farmland in Xu Xia and harvested a million hu of grain. Thus, the states and commanderies followed suit by establishing agricultural officials, accumulating grain reserves wherever they were stationed. Campaigning in all directions without the burden of transporting provisions, he eventually eliminated the various bandits and achieved peace throughout the land.

34
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
呂布襲劉備，取下邳。備來奔。程昱說公曰：「觀劉備有雄才而甚得衆心，終不為人下，不如早圖之。」公曰：「方今收英雄時也，殺一人而失天下之心，不可。」
Lü Bu attacked Liu Bei and captured Xuzhou's Xiaopi. Liu Bei came to seek refuge. Cheng Yu advised Gong, "Observing Liu Bei, he possesses great talent and has won the hearts of many people. He will never remain subordinate to others; it is better to deal with him early." Gong replied, "Now is the time to gather heroes. To kill one man and lose the hearts of all under heaven would be unacceptable."

35
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
張濟自關中走南陽。濟死，從子繡領其衆。
Zhang Ji fled from Guanzhong to Nanyang. After Zhang Ji's death, his nephew Zhang Xiu took command of his troops.

武帝紀:
二年春正月，公到宛。張繡降，旣而悔之，復反。公與戰，軍敗，為流矢所中，長子昂、弟子安民遇害。魏書曰：公所乘馬名絕影，為流矢所中，傷頰及足，并中公右臂。世語曰：昂不能騎，進馬於公，公故免，而昂遇害。公乃引兵還舞陰，繡將騎來鈔，公擊破之。繡奔穰，與劉表合。公謂諸將曰：「吾降張繡等，失不便取其質，以至于此。吾知所以敗。諸卿觀之，自今已後不復敗矣。」遂還許。世語曰：舊制，三公領兵入見，皆交戟叉頸而前。初，公將討張繡，入覲天子，時始復此制。公自此不復朝見。
In the first month of spring in the second year, Gong arrived at Wan. Zhang Xiu surrendered, but soon regretted it and rebelled again. Gong engaged in battle with him, suffered a defeat, was struck by an arrow, and his eldest son Cao Ang and his nephew Anmin were killed. The Wei Shu records: The horse that Gong rode was named Jueying, and it was struck by a stray arrow, wounding its jaw and foot. The arrow also pierced Gong's right arm. The Shi Yu states: Cao Ang could not ride a horse and presented his own horse to Gong, thus allowing Gong to escape while Ang was killed. Gong then led his troops back to Wuyin. Zhang Xiu's cavalry launched a raid, but Gong defeated them. Zhang Xiu fled to Rang and joined forces with Liu Biao. Gong said to his generals, "When I surrendered Zhang Xiu and others, I failed to take their families as hostages in a timely manner, which has led us to this situation. Now I understand why I was defeated." You all should take note—henceforth, I will not suffer defeat again." He then returned to Xu. The Shi Yu states: According to the old regulations, when chancellors led troops into court audiences, they all advanced with crossed halberds at their necks. Initially, when Gong was about to campaign against Zhang Xiu, he entered court to pay homage to the Son of Heaven; at that time this regulation was first restored. From then on, Gong no longer attended court audiences.

Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
袁術欲稱帝於淮南，使人告呂布。布收其使，上其書。術怒，攻布，為布所破。秋九月，術侵陳，公東征之。術聞公自來，棄軍走，留其將橋蕤、李豐、梁綱、樂就；公到，擊破蕤等，皆斬之。術走渡淮。公還許。
Yuan Shu wanted to proclaim himself emperor in the Huainan region and sent envoys to inform Lü Bu. Lü Bu detained Yuan's envoys and submitted their letter. Yuan Shu was furious, attacked Lü Bu, but was defeated by him. In the ninth month of autumn, Yuan Shu invaded Chen, and Gong launched an eastern campaign against him. Upon hearing that Gong himself was coming, Yuan Shu abandoned his army and fled, leaving behind his generals Qiao Rui, Li Feng, Liang Gang, and Le Jiu; when Gong arrived, he defeated Qiao Rui and the others, killing them all. Yuan Shu fled across the Huai River. Gong returned to Xu.

武帝紀:
公之自舞陰還也，南陽、章陵諸縣復叛為繡，公遣曹洪擊之，不利，還屯葉，數為繡、表所侵。冬十一月，公自南征，至宛。魏書曰：臨淯水，祠亡將士，歔欷流涕，衆皆感慟。表將鄧濟據湖陽。攻拔之，生禽濟，湖陽降。攻舞陰，下之。
When Gong returned from Wuyin, the various counties of Nanyang and Zhangling rebelled again in support of Zhang Xiu. Gong dispatched Cao Hong to attack them, but without success. He then withdrew his troops to Ye, where he was repeatedly harassed by Zhang Xiu and Liu Biao. In the eleventh month of winter, Gong personally led a southern campaign and arrived at Wan. The Wei Shu records: Standing by the Lin Yu River, he paid homage to his fallen soldiers and wept bitterly; all the troops were deeply moved. Liu Biao's general Deng Ji occupied Huyang. Gong captured it, took Deng Ji alive, and Huyang surrendered. He attacked Wuyin and captured it.

武帝紀:
三年春正月，公還許，初置軍師祭酒。三月，公圍張繡於穰。夏五月，劉表遣兵救繡，以絕軍後。獻帝春秋曰：袁紹叛卒詣公云：「田豐使紹早襲許，若挾天子以令諸侯，四海可指麾而定。」公乃解繡圍。公將引還，繡兵來，公軍不得進，連營稍前。公與荀彧書曰：「賊來追吾，雖日行數里，吾策之，到安衆，破繡必矣。」到安衆，繡與表兵合守險，公軍前後受敵。公乃夜鑿險為地道，悉過輜重，設奇兵。會明，賊謂公為遁也，悉軍來追。乃縱奇兵步騎夾攻，大破之。秋七月，公還許。荀彧問公：「前以策賊必破，何也？」公曰：「虜遏吾歸師，而與吾死地戰，吾是以知勝矣。」
隆重 In the first month of spring, in the third year, Gong returned to Xu, where he established the position of Junshi Jiaojiu (Military Advisor). In March, Gong besieged Zhang Xiu at Rang. In the fifth month of summer, Liu Biao sent troops to rescue Zhang Xiu in an attempt to cut off Gong's rear supply lines. The Ch'un Qiu of Emperor Xian records: A defector from Yuan Shao's forces came to Gong and said, "Tian Feng advised Yuan Shao to attack Xu early. If he had taken the Son of Heaven hostage and issued orders to the feudal lords, the entire realm could have been subdued with a mere gesture." Gong then lifted the siege on Zhang Xiu. As Gong prepared to withdraw, Zhang Xiu's forces attacked, preventing his troops from advancing; they established a series of connected camps and gradually moved forward. Gong wrote to Xun Yu, "The bandits are chasing us. Though we can only travel several li a day, I am confident that by the time we reach Anzhong, Zhang Xiu will surely be defeated." When they reached Anzhong, Zhang Xiu and Liu Biao's forces joined together to defend the pass. Gong's army was now attacked from both front and rear. Gong then secretly dug a tunnel through the pass at night, moved all his supplies through it, and deployed an ambush force. At dawn, the enemy assumed Gong was retreating and sent their entire army in pursuit. Gong then launched his hidden forces to attack from both flanks with infantry and cavalry, completely defeating the enemy. In the seventh month of autumn, Gong returned to Xu. Xun Yu asked Gong, "Earlier you predicted that we would certainly defeat the enemy—why was that?" Gong replied, "The bandits blocked our retreating forces and forced us to fight in a desperate situation. That is why I knew we would win."

武帝紀:
呂布復為袁術使高順攻劉備，公遣夏侯惇救之，不利。備為順所敗。九月，公東征布。冬十月，屠彭城，獲其相侯諧。進至下邳，布自將騎逆擊。大破之，獲其驍將成廉。追至城下，布恐，欲降。陳宮等沮其計，求救於術，勸布出戰，戰又敗，乃還固守，攻之不下。時公連戰，士卒罷，欲還，用荀攸、郭嘉計，遂決泗、沂水以灌城。月餘，布將宋憲、魏續等執陳宮，舉城降，生禽布、宮，皆殺之。太山臧霸、孫觀、吳敦、尹禮、昌狶各聚衆。布之破劉備也，霸等悉從布。布敗，獲霸等，公厚納待，遂割青、徐二州附于海以委焉，分琅邪、東海、北海為城陽、利城、昌慮郡。
Lü Bu, acting on Yuan Shu's orders, sent Gao Shun to attack Liu Bei again. Gong dispatched Xiahou Dun to rescue him, but the campaign was unsuccessful. Liu Bei was defeated by Gao Shun. In September, Gong launched an eastern campaign against Lü Bu. In the tenth month of winter, he sacked Pengcheng and captured its chancellor Hou Xie. Advancing to Xiaopi, Lü Bu personally led cavalry forces to intercept and attack. Gong crushed them decisively and captured their elite general Cheng Lian. Pursuing them to the city walls, Lü Bu became frightened and wanted to surrender. Chen Gong and others dissuaded him from surrendering, sought aid from Yuan Shu, advised Lü Bu to sally out for battle, but after another defeat, they returned to the city to hold it tightly. Gong could not capture them. At that time, after a series of battles, Gong's troops were exhausted and he wanted to withdraw. However, following the strategy proposed by Xun You and Guo Jia, he decided instead to dam the Si and Yi rivers to flood the city. After more than a month, Lü Bu's generals Song Xian and Wei Xu captured Chen Gong and surrendered the entire city. Lü Bu and Chen Gong were taken alive but were both executed. Zang Ba, Sun Guan, Wu Dun, Yin Li, and Chang Xi of Taishan each gathered their own forces. When Lü Bu defeated Liu Bei, Zang Ba and others all followed him. After Lü Bu's defeat, Zang Ba and the others were captured. Gong treated them generously and granted them control over Qingzhou and Xuzhou, extending as far as the sea. He also divided Langya, Donghai, and Beihai into three new commanderies: Chengyang, Licheng, and Changlv.

武帝紀:
初，公為兖州，以東平畢諶為別駕。張邈之叛也，邈劫諶母弟妻子；公謝遣之，曰：「卿老母在彼，可去。」諶頓首無二心，公嘉之，為之流涕。旣出，遂亡歸。及布破，諶生得，衆為諶懼，公曰：「夫人孝於其親者，豈不亦忠於君乎！吾所求也。」以為魯相。魏書曰：袁紹宿與故太尉楊彪、大長秋梁紹、少府孔融有隙，欲使公以他過誅之。公曰：「當今天下土崩瓦解，雄豪並起，輔相君長，人懷怏怏，各有自為之心，此上下相疑之秋也，雖以無嫌待之，猶懼未信；如有所除，則誰不自危？且夫起布衣，在塵垢之間，為庸人之所陵陷，可勝怨乎！高祖赦雍齒之讎而羣情以安，如何忘之？」紹以為公外託公義，內實離異，深懷怨望。臣松之以為楊彪亦曾為魏武所困，幾至於死，孔融竟不免於誅滅，豈所謂先行其言而後從之哉！非知之難，其在行之，信矣。
Initially, when Gong served as governor of Yanzhou, he appointed Bi Chen of Dongping as Biejia (a high-ranking administrative official). When Zhang Miao rebelled, he took hostage Bi Chen's mother, younger brother, wife, and children; Gong dismissed them with thanks, saying, "Your elderly mother is there. You may go." Bi Chen knelt and vowed unwavering loyalty; Gong praised him highly and wept for him. After leaving, Bi Chen immediately fled back to Zhang Miao. After Lü Bu was defeated, Bi Chen was captured alive. Many feared for his safety, but Gong said, "A person who is filial to their parents—would they not also be loyal to their ruler? That is exactly what I seek." He was appointed as the governor of Lu. The Wei Shu records: Yuan Shao had long been at odds with former Taiwei Yang Biao, Dachangqiu Liang Shao, and Shaofu Kong Rong. He wanted Gong to find some other fault in them and have them executed. Gong said, "Nowadays, the realm is in disarray and powerful men have risen together. Those who assist or serve their lords all harbor dissatisfaction, each with thoughts of self-interest. This is a time when superiors and subordinates mutually suspect one another. Even if I treat them without suspicion, I still fear they may not trust me; if I were to eliminate anyone, who would not feel endangered? Moreover, those who rise from humble origins and struggle amidst hardship are often oppressed by ordinary people. Could such grievances possibly be counted? Emperor Gaozu pardoned You Yichang's enemies and thus calmed the sentiments of the people. How could I forget this?" Yuan Shao believed that Gong outwardly claimed public righteousness but inwardly sought to divide and alienate, and thus harbored deep resentment toward him. Min Songzhi believes that Yang Biao was also once trapped by Wei Wu and nearly put to death, while Kong Rong ultimately could not escape execution. How then can this be said to be acting in accordance with one's own words? It is not difficult to know, but the difficulty lies in putting it into practice—this is indeed true.

武帝紀:
四年春二月，公還至昌邑。張楊將楊醜殺楊，眭固又殺醜，以其衆屬袁紹，屯射犬。夏四月，進軍臨河，使史渙、曹仁渡河擊之。固使楊故長史薛洪、河內太守繆尚留守，自將兵北迎紹求救，與渙、仁相遇犬城。交戰，大破之，斬固。公遂濟河，圍射犬。洪、尚率衆降，封為列侯，還軍敖倉。以魏种為河內太守，屬以河北事。
In spring, second month of the fourth year, Gong returned to Changyi. Zhang Yang's general Yang Chou killed Zhang Yang; Su Gu then killed Yang Chou and brought his forces under Yuan Shao, stationing them at Shequan. In the fourth month of summer, Gong advanced to Linhe and ordered Shi Huan and Cao Ren to cross the river and attack them. Su Gu ordered Zhang Yang's former chief clerk Xue Hong and Hedong Taishou Miu Shang to remain as garrisons, while he personally led troops northward to meet Yuan Shao for reinforcements. He encountered Shi Huan and Cao Ren at Quancheng. After engaging in battle, they heavily defeated Su Gu's forces and beheaded Su Gu. Gong then crossed the river and laid siege to Shequan. Xue Hong and Miu Shang led their forces in surrender, were enfeoffed as Liehou (Marquises), and the army returned to Aocang. Wei Zhong was appointed Hedong Taishou, entrusted with affairs in Hebei.

初，公舉种孝廉。兖州叛，公曰：「唯魏种且不棄孤也。」及聞种走，公怒曰：「种不南走越、北走胡，不置汝也！」旣下射犬，生禽种，公曰：「唯其才也！」釋其縛而用之。
Initially, Gong had recommended Wei Zhong as a filial and upright scholar-official (Xiaolian). When Yanzhou rebelled, Gong said, "Only Wei Zhong will not abandon me." He then executed him. After capturing Shequan, Wei Zhong was captured alive. Gong said, "It is only because of his talent!" He released him from bonds and employed him.

武帝紀:
是時袁紹旣并公孫瓚，兼四州之地，衆十餘萬，將進軍攻許，諸將以為不可敵，公曰：「吾知紹之為人，志大而智小，色厲而膽薄，忌克而少威，兵多而分畫不明，將驕而政令不一，土地雖廣，糧食雖豐，適足以為吾奉也。」秋八月，公進軍黎陽，使臧霸等入青州破齊、北海、東安，留于禁屯河上。九月，公還許，分兵守官渡。冬十一月，張繡率衆降，封列侯。十二月，公軍官渡。
At this time, Yuan Shao had already annexed Gongsun Zan's territory and controlled the lands of four states. His forces numbered over 100,000, and he was preparing to advance on Xu. The generals all believed they could not match him in strength, but Gong said: "I know Yuan Shao's character well—he has great ambitions but little wisdom; his appearance is fierce, yet his courage is shallow. He is jealous and narrow-minded with little authority. His army may be large, but its organization is unclear; his generals are arrogant and their commands inconsistent. Though his territory is vast and his grain supplies abundant, these advantages will only serve to support me." In autumn, eighth month, Gong advanced his army to Liyang and dispatched Zang Ba et al. into Qingzhou to attack Qi, Beihai, and Dong'an; he left Yu Jin stationed by the river. In September, Gong returned to Xu and divided his forces to defend Guandu. In winter, eleventh month, Zhang Xiu led his troops in surrender; he was enfeoffed as a Liehou (Marquis). In December, Gong stationed his army at Guandu.

武帝紀:
袁術自敗於陳，稍困，袁譚自青州遣迎之。術欲從下邳北過，公遣劉備、朱靈要之。會術病死。程昱、郭嘉聞公遣備，言於公曰：「劉備不可縱。」公悔，追之不及。備之未東也，陰與董承等謀反，至下邳，遂殺徐州刺史車冑，舉兵屯沛。遣劉岱、王忠擊之，不克。獻帝春秋曰：備謂岱等曰：「使汝百人來，其無如我何；曹公自來，未可知耳！」魏武故事曰：岱字公山，沛國人。以司空長史從征伐有功，封列侯。魏略曰：王忠，扶風人，少為亭長。三輔亂，忠饑乏噉人，隨輩南向武關。值婁子伯為荊州遣迎北方客人；忠不欲去，因率等仵逆擊之，奪其兵，聚衆千餘人以歸公。拜忠中郎將，從征討。五官將知忠甞噉人，因從駕出行，令俳取冢間髑髏繫著忠馬鞍，以為歡笑。
After Yuan Shu was defeated in Chen and gradually became cornered, Yuan Tan sent a force from Qingzhou to receive him. Yuan Shu intended to pass north of Xuping, but Gong dispatched Liu Bei and Zhu Ling to intercept him. However, Yuan Shu died of illness at the same time. Cheng Yu and Guo Jia, upon hearing that Gong had sent Liu Bei away, advised him, saying: "Liu Bei cannot be allowed to go free." Gong regretted it but failed to catch up with him. Before Liu Bei moved east, he secretly conspired to rebel with Dong Cheng and others. Upon reaching Xuping, he killed Xu Zhou Cishi Che Zou, raised his troops, and stationed them in Pei. Gong dispatched Liu Dai and Wang Zhong to attack him, but they failed to achieve victory. The Spring and Autumn Annals of the Emperor Xian records: Liu Bei said to Liu Dai et al., "Even if you send a hundred men, what can you do to me? If Cao Gong himself comes, it remains uncertain!" The Anecdotes of Wei Wu records: Liu Dai courtesy name Gongshan was a native of Pei Guo. As Shikong Changshi, he followed on military campaigns and achieved merit; he was enfeoffed a Liehou (Marquis). The Wei Lue records: Wang Zhong, a native of Fufeng, had been a tinglei in his youth. When the Three Fu region fell into chaos, Wang Zhong suffered from hunger and starvation to the point of cannibalism; he followed others southward toward Wuguan. He encountered Lou Zibo, who had been sent by Jingzhou to welcome northern refugees; He was then appointed Zhonglangjiang and enfeoffed as Duting Hou. Wang Zhong was made Zhonglangjiang, and followed on military expeditions. The Wuguanjiang knew that Wang Zhong had once resorted to cannibalism, so when accompanying the imperial procession on an outing, he ordered a performer to retrieve a skull from a tomb and tie it onto Wang Zhong's horse saddle for amusement.

武帝紀:
五年春正月，董承等謀泄，皆伏誅。公將自東征備，諸將皆曰：「與公爭天下者，袁紹也。今紹方來而棄之東，紹乘人後，若何？」公曰：「夫劉備，人傑也，今不擊，必為後患。孫盛魏氏春秋云：荅諸將曰：「劉備，人傑也，將生憂寡人。」臣松之以為史之記言，旣多潤色，故前載所述有非實者矣，後之作者又生意改之，於失實也，不亦彌遠乎！凡孫盛製書，多用左氏以易舊文，如此者非一。嗟乎，後之學者將何取信哉？且魏武方以天下勵志，而用夫差分死之言，尤非其類。袁紹雖有大志，而見事遟，必不動也。」郭嘉亦勸公，遂東擊備，破之，生禽其將夏侯博。備走奔紹，獲其妻子。備將關羽屯下邳，復進攻之，羽降。昌狶叛為備，又攻破之。公還官渡，紹卒不出。
In spring, first month of the fifth year, Dong Cheng's plot was exposed; all were executed. Gong planned to personally lead an eastern campaign against Liu Bei, but the generals all said: "The one who competes with you for the empire is Yuan Shao. Now that Yuan Shao is about to arrive, if we abandon him and move eastward, he will strike from behind us—what then?" Gong said: "Liu Bei is a man of outstanding talent. If we do not strike him now, he will surely become a future threat. Sun Sheng's Wei Shi Chunqiu records: In response to the generals, he said, "Liu Bei is an outstanding man; his existence will bring me future worries." Min Songzhi believes that historical records of speech are often embellished, so some accounts in earlier sources are not factual. Later writers then deliberately altered them; thus, the further they stray from the truth, is it not even more distant? In general, whenever Sun Sheng composed his writings, he often used Zuo Zhuan to replace the original texts; such instances are not isolated. Alas! What can later scholars rely on for truth? Moreover, at the time Wei Wu was striving with his ambitions to rule the realm, yet he adopted words akin to those of Fu Chai who divided death—this is especially inconsistent. "Yuan Shao may have grand ambitions, but he is slow to act and will certainly not move." Guo Jia also advised Gong, so they moved eastward against Liu Bei. They defeated him and captured his general Xiahou Bo alive. Liu Bei fled to Yuan Shao for refuge, but his wife and children were captured. Liu Bei's general Guan Yu was stationed at Xuping; Gong advanced again to attack him, and Guan Yu surrendered. Chang Xi had rebelled on Liu Bei's behalf but was once more defeated by Gong's forces. Gong returned to Guandu, and Yuan Shao finally did not move out.

武帝紀:
二月，紹遣郭圖、淳于瓊、顏良攻東郡太守劉延於白馬，紹引兵至黎陽，將渡河。夏四月，公北救延。荀攸說公曰：「今兵少不敵，分其勢乃可。公到延津，若將渡兵向其後者，紹必西應之，然後輕兵襲白馬，掩其不備，顏良可禽也。」公從之。紹聞兵渡，即分兵西應之。公乃引軍兼行趣白馬，未至十餘里，良大驚，來逆戰。使張遼、關羽前登，擊破，斬良。遂解白馬圍，徙其民，循河而西。紹於是渡河追公軍，至延津南。公勒兵駐營南阪下，使登壘望之，曰：「可五六百騎。」有頃，復白：「騎稍多，步兵不可勝數。」公曰：「勿復白。」乃令騎解鞍放馬。是時，白馬輜重就道。諸將以為敵騎多，不如還保營。荀攸曰：「此所以餌敵，如何去之！」紹騎將文醜與劉備將五六千騎前後至。諸將復白：「可上馬。」公曰：「未也。」有頃，騎至稍多，或分趣輜重。公曰：「可矣。」乃皆上馬。時騎不滿六百，遂縱兵擊，大破之，斬醜、良。醜、良皆紹名將也，再戰，悉禽，紹軍大震。公還軍官渡。紹進保陽武。關羽亡歸劉備。
In the second month, Yuan Shao dispatched Guo Tu, Chunyu Qiong, and Yan Liang to attack Liu Yan, the Taishou of Dongjun, at Ba Ma. Yuan Shao led his troops to Liyang, preparing to cross the river. In the fourth month of summer, Kong moved north to rescue Liu Yan. Xun You advised Gong: "Now our forces are few and cannot match them; we must divide their strength in order to succeed. When you arrive at Yanzhen, if you appear to be preparing troops to cross and attack their rear, Yuan Shao will surely respond by moving west. Then we can send a light force to strike Ba Ma unexpectedly, catching them off guard—Yan Liang can then be captured." Gong followed his advice. Yuan Shao, upon hearing of the troop crossing, immediately split his forces to respond westward. Gong then led his army in a rapid march toward Ba Ma, and before they had covered more than ten li, Yan Liang was greatly alarmed and came out to meet them in battle. Gong ordered Zhang Liao and Guan Yu to lead the charge; they attacked, defeated Yan Liang's forces, and beheaded him. Thus, the siege of Ba Ma was lifted. The civilians were relocated, and the army followed along the river to the west. Yuan Shao then crossed the river in pursuit of Gong's forces, reaching as far south as Yanzhen. Gong stationed his troops at the southern slope below the camp and ordered someone to climb a watchtower for observation, who reported: "There are about five or six hundred cavalry." After some time, the observer reported again: "The number of horsemen is increasing slightly, and there are infantry troops too numerous to count." Gong said, "Do not report any further." He then ordered the cavalry to dismount and release their horses. At that time, the Ba Ma supply convoy was on its way. The generals believed the enemy cavalry outnumbered them and suggested retreating to defend the camp instead. Xun You said, "This is precisely a bait for the enemy; how can we abandon it!" Yuan Shao's cavalry general Wen Chou and Liu Bei, with about five or six thousand horsemen, arrived in succession. The generals once again reported: "We should mount our horses." Gong replied, "Not yet." After some time, more cavalry arrived and began to split off toward the supply convoy. Gong said: "Now is the time." Then all mounted their horses. At that time, his cavalry numbered less than six hundred; he then launched an attack and heavily defeated the enemy forces, beheading Wen Chou and Yan Liang. Wen Chou and Yan Liang were both renowned generals of Yuan Shao; in two battles, they were completely defeated. Yuan Shao's army was greatly shaken. Gong returned his forces to Guandu. Yuan Shao advanced and took refuge in Yangwu. Guan Yu fled back to Liu Bei.
