武帝紀:
八月，紹連營稍前，依沙塠為屯，東西數十里。公亦分營與相當，合戰不利。習鑿齒漢晉春秋曰：許攸說紹曰：「公無與操相攻也。急分諸軍持之，而徑從他道迎天子，則事立濟矣。」紹不從，曰：「吾要當先圍取之。」攸怒。時公兵不滿萬，傷者十二三。臣松之以為魏武初起兵，已有衆五千，自後百戰百勝，敗者十二三而已矣。但一破黃巾，受降卒三十餘萬，餘所吞并，不可悉紀；雖征戰損傷，未應如此之少也。夫結營相守，異於摧鋒決戰。本紀云：「紹衆十餘萬，屯營東西數十里。」魏太祖雖機變無方，略不世出，安有以數千之兵，而得逾時相抗者哉？以理而言，竊謂不然。紹為屯數十里，公能分營與相當，此兵不得甚少，一也。紹若有十倍之衆，理應當悉力圍守，使出入斷絕，而公使徐晃等擊其運車，公又自出擊淳于瓊等，揚旌往還，曾無抵閡，明紹力不能制，是不得甚少，二也。諸書皆云公坑紹衆八萬，或云七萬。夫八萬人奔散，非八千人所能縛，而紹之大衆皆拱手就戮，何緣力能制之？是不得甚少，三也。將記述者欲以少見奇，非其實錄也。按鍾繇傳云：「公與紹相持，繇為司隷，送馬二千餘匹以給軍。」本紀及世語並云公時有騎六百餘匹，繇馬為安在哉？紹復進臨官渡，起土山地道。公亦於內作之，以相應。紹射營中，矢如雨下，行者皆蒙楯，衆大懼。時公糧少，與荀彧書，議欲還許。彧以為「紹悉衆聚官渡，欲與公決勝敗。公以至弱當至彊，若不能制，必為所乘，是天下之大機也。且紹，布衣之雄耳，能聚人而不能用。夫以公之神武明哲而輔以大順，何向而不濟！」公從之。
In August, Yuan Shao linked his camps and gradually advanced forward, establishing encampments along the sandy ridges stretching east-west for dozens of li. Gong also divided his camps to face them in equal strength; however, their combined battle was unfavorable. Xu Xichui's Han Jin Chunqiu records: Xu You advised Yuan Shao, saying, "You should not engage Cao Cao in battle. Hastily divide your forces to contain him while taking a different route directly to welcome the Son of Heaven; then success will be assured." Yuan Shao did not follow this advice, saying, "I must first surround and capture him." Xu You became angry. At that time, Gong's forces numbered less than ten thousand, with one in every twelve or thirteen being wounded. Chen Songzhi believes that when Wei Wu first raised his army, he already had five thousand troops. Since then, through countless battles and victories, the defeated were only one in twelve or thirteen. But after defeating the Huangjin rebels once, he accepted the surrender of over 300,000 enemy soldiers. The rest that were absorbed and annexed cannot be fully recorded; although there were losses from campaigns, the number should not have been so small. Setting up camps and defending is different from breaking enemy formations in decisive battles. The Benji records: "Yuan Shao's forces numbered over 100,000 and were stationed in camps stretching east-west for dozens of miles." Although Wei Taizu was a man of extraordinary strategic ingenuity and unmatched in his generation, how could he have withstood for so long with only several thousand troops? From a logical standpoint, I secretly believe this is not the case. Yuan Shao had encampments stretching for dozens of miles; Gong was able to divide his camps and match them in strength. This indicates that his forces could not have been very small—this is the first point. If Yuan Shao had ten times the number of troops, he should logically have concentrated all his forces to surround and block off supply routes. Yet Gong sent Xu Huang and others to attack their supply wagons; Gong himself personally led an assault on Chunyu Qiong and others, raising banners as he moved back and forth without encountering any resistance. This clearly shows that Yuan Shao lacked the strength to stop them—this is the second point. All the historical records state that Gong slaughtered 80,000 of Yuan Shao's troops, or some say 70,000. Eighty thousand men fleeing in disarray could not possibly be captured by only 8,000 troops. Moreover, Yuan Shao's large forces all surrendered without resistance—how could they have been strong enough to resist? This indicates that the number was not very small—this is the third point. The account by the recorder likely aims to highlight the extraordinary feat of achieving much with little, but it does not reflect the actual situation. According to the biography of Zhong Yao: "Gong and Yuan Shao were engaged in a prolonged standoff, during which Zhong Yao served as Sili and sent over 2,000 horses to supply the army." Both the Benji and Shiyu state that at this time Gong had only over 600 cavalry horses. Where, then, were Zhong Yao's horses? Yuan Shao once again advanced to Guandu and constructed earthen mounds as well as underground tunnels. Gong also built similar structures within his own lines in response. Yuan Shao launched arrows into Gong's camp, and the projectiles rained down like rain; those on foot all covered themselves with shields, and the troops were greatly frightened. At that time, Gong had little grain supplies left. He wrote a letter to Xun Yu, discussing his intention to retreat back to Xu. Xun Yu believed that "Yuan Shao has gathered all his forces at Guandu, hoping to decide the outcome of victory or defeat with you. You are facing an extremely strong enemy with your own greatly weakened forces; if you cannot prevail, you will surely be overwhelmed. This is the decisive moment for the fate of the world." Moreover, Yuan Shao is merely a powerful man among commoners; he can gather people but cannot effectively use them. With your divine martial prowess and wisdom, supported by great righteousness, in which direction could you possibly fail!" Gong followed his advice.

Sun Ce, upon hearing that Gong and Yuan Shao were locked in a standoff, planned to launch an attack on Xu. Before he could act, however, he was killed by an assassin.

汝南降賊劉辟等叛應紹，略許下。紹使劉備助辟，公使曹仁擊破之。備走，遂破辟屯。
Liu Bi and other rebel leaders from Ru Nan who had surrendered defected to support Yuan Shao and raided the outskirts of Xu. Yuan Shao sent Liu Bei to assist Liu Bi, but Gong dispatched Cao Ren, who defeated them. Liu Bei fled, and thus the encampment of Liu Bi was broken.

武帝紀:
袁紹運穀車數千乘至，公用荀攸計，遣徐晃、史渙邀擊，大破之，盡燒其車。公與紹相拒連月，雖比戰斬將，然衆少糧盡，士卒疲乏。公謂運者曰：「却十五日為汝破紹，不復勞汝矣。」冬十月，紹遣車運穀，使淳于瓊等五人將兵萬餘人送之，宿紹營北四十里。紹謀臣許攸貪財，紹不能足，來奔，因說公擊瓊等。左右疑之，荀攸、賈詡勸公。公乃留曹洪守，自將步騎五千人夜往，會明至。瓊等望見公兵少，出陳門外。公急擊之，瓊退保營，遂攻之。紹遣騎救瓊。左右或言「賊騎稍近，請分兵拒之」。公怒曰：「賊在背後，乃白！」士卒皆殊死戰，大破瓊等，皆斬之。曹瞞傳曰：公聞攸來，跣出迎之，撫掌笑曰：「子卿遠來，吾事濟矣！」旣入坐，謂公曰：「袁氏軍盛，何以待之？今有幾糧乎？」公曰：「尚可支一歲。」攸曰：「無是，更言之！」又曰：「可支半歲。」攸曰：「足下不欲破袁氏邪，何言之不實也！」公曰：「向言戲之耳。其實可一月，為之柰何？」攸曰：「公孤軍獨守，外無救援而糧穀已盡，此危急之日也。今袁氏輜重有萬餘乘，在故市、烏巢，屯軍無嚴備；今以輕兵襲之，不意而至，燔其積聚，不過三日，袁氏自敗也。」公大喜，乃選精銳步騎，皆用袁軍旗幟，銜枚縛馬口，夜從間道出，人抱束薪，所歷道有問者，語之曰：「袁公恐曹操鈔略後軍，遣兵以益備。」聞者信以為然，皆自若。旣至，圍屯，大放火，營中驚亂。大破之，盡燔其糧穀寶貨，斬督將眭元進、騎督韓莒子、呂威璜、趙叡等首，割得將軍淳于仲簡鼻，未死，殺士卒千餘人，皆取鼻，牛馬割脣舌，以示紹軍。將士皆怛懼。時有夜得仲簡，將以詣麾下，公謂曰：「何為如是？」仲簡曰：「勝負自天，何用為問乎！」公意欲不殺。許攸曰：「明且鑒於鏡，此益不忘人。」乃殺之。紹初聞公之擊瓊，謂長子譚曰：「就彼攻瓊等，吾攻拔其營，彼固無所歸矣！」乃使張郃、高覽攻曹洪。郃等聞瓊破，遂來降。紹衆大潰，紹及譚棄軍走，渡河。追之不及，盡收其輜重圖書珎寶，虜其衆。獻帝起居注曰：公上言「大將軍鄴侯袁紹前與兾州牧韓馥立故大司馬劉虞，刻作金璽，遣故任長畢瑜詣虞，為說命錄之數。又紹與臣書云：『可都鄄城，當有所立。』擅鑄金銀印，孝廉計吏，皆往詣紹。從弟濟陰太守敘與紹書云：『今海內喪敗，天意實在我家，神應有徵，當在尊兄。南兄臣下欲使即位，南兄言，以年則北兄長，以位則北兄重。便欲送璽，會曹操斷道。』紹宗族累世受國重恩，而凶逆無道，乃至於此。輙勒兵馬，與戰官渡，乘聖朝之威，得斬紹大將淳于瓊等八人首，遂大破潰。紹與子譚輕身迸走。凡斬首七萬餘級，輜重財物巨億。」公收紹書中，得許下及軍中人書，皆焚之。魏氏春秋曰：公云：「當紹之彊，孤猶不能自保，而況衆人乎！」兾州諸郡多舉城邑降者。
Yuan Shao sent thousands of grain wagons to Guandu. Following Xun You's strategy, Gong dispatched Xu Huang and Shi Huan to intercept them, defeating the enemy in a major battle and burning all their supply carts. For months, Gong and Yuan Shao opposed each other in battle; although several enemy generals were captured or killed in successive engagements, Gong's forces remained few in number with their supplies exhausted and his soldiers weary. Gong told the supply workers: "In fifteen days, I will defeat Yuan Shao for you; you need not trouble yourselves any longer." In the tenth month of winter, Yuan Shao dispatched carts to transport grain and sent Chunyu Qiong with five others commanding over 10,000 soldiers to escort them. They camped forty li north of Yuan Shao's main encampment. Yuan Shao's trusted advisor Xu You was greedy for wealth, and Yuan Shao could not satisfy his demands. Xu You then defected to Gong and advised him to attack Chunyu Qiong's forces. Gong's attendants doubted the plan, but Xun You and Jia Xu urged Gong to proceed. Gong then left Cao Hong in charge of the defenses and personally led 5,000 infantry and cavalry at night. They arrived just before dawn. Chunyu Qiong and his men saw that Gong's forces were few and deployed their troops outside the gate. Gong immediately launched an attack, forcing Chunyu Qiong to retreat into his camp for protection, which Gong then proceeded to assault. Yuan Shao dispatched cavalry reinforcements to rescue Chunyu Qiong. Some of Gong's attendants suggested, "The enemy cavalry is approaching; please divide your forces to resist them." Gong angrily replied, "The enemy is behind us and you only report this now!" The soldiers fought with all their might in a desperate battle and completely defeated Chunyu Qiong's forces, killing him and his subordinates. The Cao Man Zhuan records: Upon hearing that Xu You had arrived, Gong rushed out barefoot to greet him and clapped his hands in joy, saying, "Ziqing has come from afar; my affairs are now assured!" After sitting down, Xu You asked Gong: "Yuan Shao's army is strong. How do you intend to deal with it?" "Now, how much grain supplies do you have?" Gong replied: "It is still enough to last for one year." Xu You said, "No, say it again!" Gong then said: "It is enough to last for half a year." Xu You replied, "Do you not wish to defeat the Yuan family? Why are your words so untrue?" Gong said: "I was merely joking before." In truth, it is only enough for one month. What should we do?" Xu You said: "You are holding out alone with an isolated army, without external reinforcements and your grain supplies have already run out. This is a critical moment of danger. Now, Yuan Shao's supply wagons number over ten thousand carts and are stationed at Gushi and Wchao. The troops guarding them have no strong defenses; if you now send a light force to attack them unexpectedly, burn their supplies and provisions, within no more than three days, Yuan Shao will collapse on his own." Gong was greatly pleased and selected a contingent of elite infantry and cavalry. They all used the banners of Yuan Shao's army, bit their tongues to silence themselves, tied up their horses' mouths, and departed at night through hidden paths. Each soldier carried bundles of firewood; when anyone along the route asked about them, they replied, "General Yuan is afraid that Cao Cao will raid his rear forces and has sent troops to reinforce the defenses." Those who heard this believed it to be true and remained calm. After arriving, they surrounded the encampment, set a great fire, and chaos erupted within the camp. They completely defeated the enemy, burning all their grain supplies and treasures. They beheaded the commanders Su Yuanjin, Ji Du Han Juzi, Lü Weihuang, Zhao Rui, and others; they cut off the nose of General Chunyu Zhongjian, who did not die, and killed over a thousand enemy soldiers, taking their noses as trophies. The lips and tongues of captured oxen and horses were also cut to demonstrate to Yuan Shao's forces. The generals and soldiers were all terrified. At that time, someone captured Chunyu Zhongjian at night and was about to bring him before Gong's command. Gong asked him, "Why have you done this?" Chunyu Zhongjian replied: "Victory or defeat is determined by Heaven; why should I answer your question!" Gong had the intention not to kill him. Xu You said: "A clear mirror reflects clearly; this man will never forget his enemies." Thus, he was executed. When Yuan Shao first heard that Gong had attacked Chunyu Qiong, he said to his eldest son Yuan Tan: "If they attack Qiong and others from the front, I will capture their camp. They will have nowhere to return!" He then sent Zhang He and Gao Lan to attack Cao Hong. Zhang He and others, upon hearing of Chunyu Qiong's defeat, surrendered immediately. Yuan Shao's entire army collapsed in panic; Yuan Shao and Yuan Tan abandoned their troops and fled across the Yellow River. Gong pursued them but failed to catch up, capturing all of Yuan Shao's supplies, documents, treasures, and taking many of his soldiers as prisoners. The Xian Di Qiju Zhu records: Gong submitted a report stating, "The Grand General Ye Hou Yuan Shao previously colluded with the Ji Zhou Mu Han Fu to establish the former Da Sima Liu Yu. They forged a golden seal and sent the former Renchang Bi Yu to Liu Yu to declare that he was destined for imperial authority." Yuan Shao also wrote a letter to me, saying: 'You should establish your capital at Juancheng and declare an imperial title.' They privately cast gold and silver seals. All filial sons, worthy men, and officials responsible for submitting reports traveled to Yuan Shao. His cousin, the Taihou of Jiyin Xv, wrote to Yuan Shao: "Now that the empire is in decline and disorder, Heaven's will truly rests with our family. Divine signs indicate that it should be upon my esteemed elder brother." "My younger brother's subordinates wish for him to ascend the throne, but my younger brother said that in terms of age, the elder brother is older; and in terms of status, the elder brother holds greater authority." "They were about to send the jade seal when Cao Cao cut off their route." Yuan Shao's family has received great favors from the state for generations, yet he was cruel and rebellious, committing inhuman acts to such an extent. I immediately mobilized my troops and fought against him at Guandu. Relying on the might of your holy dynasty, I was able to behead Yuan Shao's eight major generals, including Chunyu Qiong, and completely crushed his forces. Yuan Shao and his son Yuan Tan fled lightly clad in person. A total of over 70,000 heads were beheaded, along with countless wagons and treasures." Gong collected letters from Yuan Shao's archives addressed to people in Xu and within his own army, and burned them all. The Wei Shi Chunqiu records: Gong said, "When Yuan Shao was at his strongest, I could barely protect myself; how much less could ordinary people do so!" Many of the commanderies in Ji Zhou surrendered by raising their cities and towns.

武帝紀:
初，桓帝時有黃星見於楚、宋之分，遼東殷馗馗，古逵字，見三蒼。善天文，言後五十歲當有真人起於梁、沛之閒，其鋒不可當。至是凡五十年，而公破紹，天下莫敵矣。
Initially, during the reign of Emperor Huan, a yellow star appeared in the constellations corresponding to Chu and Song. In Liaodong, Yin Kuikui (Kuikui is an alternate form of the character Kui, as seen in San Cang). Skilled in astronomy, he stated that fifty years later a true ruler would rise between Liang and Pei, whose momentum could not be resisted. At this point, exactly fifty years had passed since then, when Gong defeated Yuan Shao, and there was no one in the world who could rival him.

武帝紀:
六年夏四月，揚兵河上，擊紹倉亭軍，破之。紹歸，復收散卒，攻定諸叛郡縣。九月，公還許。紹之未破也，使劉備略汝南，汝南賊共都等應之。遣蔡揚擊都，不利，為都所破。公南征備。備聞公自行，走奔劉表，都等皆散。
In the fourth month of summer in the sixth year, Gong mobilized his troops along the Yellow River and attacked Yuan Shao's Cangting forces, defeating them. Yuan Shao returned, regrouped his scattered soldiers, and launched attacks to pacify the rebellious commanderies and counties. In September, Gong returned to Xu. Before Yuan Shao was defeated, he sent Liu Bei to raid Ru'nan, where the bandits Gong Du and others responded to him. Cai Yang was dispatched to attack Gong Du but suffered a setback and was defeated by Gong Du. Gong personally led southern campaigns against Liu Bei. Liu Bei, hearing that Gong was leading the campaign in person, fled to seek refuge with Liu Biao, and Gong Du and others all dispersed.

武帝紀:
七年春正月，公軍譙，令曰：「吾起義兵，為天下除暴亂。舊土人民，死喪略盡，國中終日行，不見所識，使吾悽愴傷懷。其舉義兵已來，將士絕無後者，求其親戚以後之，授上田，官給耕牛，置學師以教之。為存者立廟，使祀其先人，魂而有靈，吾百年之後何恨哉！」遂至浚儀，治睢陽渠，遣使以太牢祀橋玄。襃賞令載公祀文曰：「故太尉橋公，誕敷明德，汎愛博容。國念明訓，士思令謨。靈幽體翳，邈哉晞矣！吾以幼年，逮并堂室，特以頑鄙之姿，為大君子所納。增榮益觀，皆由獎助，猶仲尼稱不如顏淵，李生之厚歎賈復。士死知己，懷此無忘。又承從容約誓之言：『殂逝之後，路有經由，不以斗酒隻雞過相沃酹，車過三步，腹痛勿怪！』雖臨時戲笑之言，非至親之篤好，胡肯為此辭乎？匪謂靈忿，能詒己疾，懷舊惟顧，念之悽愴。奉命東征，屯次鄉里，北望貴土，乃心陵墓。裁致薄奠，公其尚饗！」進軍官渡。
In the first month of spring in the seventh year, General Gong's army was stationed at Qiao, where he issued an order: "I raised my righteous troops to rid the world of tyranny and chaos. The people in our old homeland have nearly all perished or been lost, and as I walk through the country day after day, I see no one I recognize, which fills me with sorrow and grief. Since the raising of this righteous army, there are soldiers and officers who have no descendants. I seek out their relatives to carry on their line, grant them prime farmland, provide oxen for plowing from government stores, and appoint teachers to educate them. Build temples for those who remain so they may honor their ancestors. If their spirits are aware, then after my hundred years of life, what regret could I have!" He proceeded to Junyi, where he managed the Suyang Canal and sent envoys with a grand sacrifice of three animals (tailao) to honor Qiao Xuan. The commendation order recording the tribute to Gong stated: "The late Taiwei Qiao Gong, who widely spread his enlightened virtue and showed universal love and broad tolerance. The state remembers his wise teachings, and scholars reflect on his noble strategies. His spirit lingers in obscurity, how distant and rare indeed! I was a youth when I encountered his household; it was especially due to my crude and humble nature that he, the great gentleman, accepted me. The honor and recognition I received were all due to his encouragement; it was like Confucius praising Yan Yuan as superior, or Li Sheng expressing deep admiration for Jia Fu. A scholar would die for one who knows him truly, and I have never forgotten this sentiment. I also received his gracious and casual oath: "After my death, if you happen to pass by on the road, do not offer even a single cup of wine or a chicken to pour over my grave in remembrance. If your carriage passes within three steps, don't be surprised if I suffer abdominal pain!" Though these were words spoken in jest at the time, unless one had a deep and sincere bond of affection as close relatives, how could such expressions be made? It is not that the spirit would resent or bring illness upon itself; rather, thinking of old friends and looking back with care, I feel sorrowful and heartbroken. Carrying out the imperial command to campaign eastward, my troops are stationed in our hometown; looking north toward your noble land, I am filled with longing for the ancestral tombs. I offer this humble memorial sacrifice; may you partake of it, Sir!" The army advanced to Guandu.

紹自軍破後，發病歐血，夏五月死。小子尚代，譚自號車騎將軍，屯黎陽。秋九月，公征之，連戰。譚、尚數敗退，固守。
After his forces were defeated, Yuan Shao fell ill and vomited blood; he died in the fifth month of summer. Yuan Shang and Yuan Dai took over, while Yuan Tan styled himself as General Chaji, stationing his troops at Liyang. In the ninth month of autumn, Gong launched a campaign against them and engaged in continuous battles. Yuan Tan and Yuan Shang suffered repeated defeats and retreated, retreating to hold their ground.

八年春三月，攻其郭，乃出戰，擊，大破之，譚、尚夜遁。夏四月，進軍鄴。五月還許，留賈信屯黎陽。
In the third month of spring in the eighth year, they attacked the outer city; Yuan Tan and Yuan Shang then emerged to fight. They were heavily defeated, and at night, Yuan Tan and Yuan Shang fled. In the fourth month of summer, the army advanced toward Ye. In May, he returned to Xu and left Jia Xin stationed at Liyang.

58
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
己酉，令曰：「司馬法『將軍死綏』，魏書云：綏，却也。有前一尺，無却一寸。故趙括之母，乞不坐括。是古之將者，軍破於外，而家受罪於內也。自命將征行，但賞功而不罰罪，非國典也。其令諸將出征，敗軍者抵罪，失利者免官爵。」魏書載庚申令曰：「議者或以軍吏雖有功能，德行不足堪任郡國之選，所謂『可與適道，未可與權』。管仲曰：『使賢者食於能則上尊，鬬士食於功則卒輕於死，二者設於國則天下治。』未聞無能之人，不鬬之士，並受祿賞，而可以立功興國者也。故明君不官無功之臣，不賞不戰之士；治平尚德行，有事賞功能。論者之言，一似管窺虎歟！」
On the Jiyou day, an order was issued: "The 'Sima Fa' says, 'A general dies for his banner,' and the Wei Shu states: 'Sui means to retreat.'" There is a reward of one chi (about 33 cm) forward, but no retreat even by an inch. Therefore, the mother of Zhao Kuo requested that she not be held responsible for her son's actions. This is how it was with ancient generals: when their armies were defeated outside, their families suffered punishment within. Appointing generals to campaign and only rewarding merit while not punishing crimes is not in accordance with the state's regulations. Therefore, I order that all commanders who go on campaigns and suffer a defeated army shall be held accountable for their crimes, and those who suffer losses shall lose their official positions and titles." The Wei Shu records the Gengshen decree: "Some advisors argue that although military officials may have ability and accomplishments, their moral character is insufficient to qualify for selection as magistrates of commanderies or states; this is what is meant by 'they can be guided along the right path but cannot be entrusted with authority.'" Guan Zhong said: "If the wise are given positions based on their ability, then superiors will be respected; if warriors receive rewards based on merit, then soldiers will regard death lightly. When these two principles are established in a state, the world will be well governed." I have never heard of people without ability or soldiers who do not fight receiving salaries and rewards, yet being able to achieve merit and revitalize the state. Therefore, a wise ruler does not appoint officials who have no achievements, nor reward soldiers who do not fight; In times of peace and stability, virtue is valued; in times of crisis, merit and ability are rewarded. The views expressed by the debaters seem like peering at a tiger through a bamboo tube!"

武帝紀:
秋七月，令曰：「喪亂已來，十有五年，後生者不見仁義禮讓之風，吾甚傷之。其令郡國各修文學，縣滿五百戶置校官，選其鄉之俊造而教學之，庶幾先王之道不廢，而有以益於天下。」
In the seventh month of autumn, an order was issued: "Since the time of chaos and disorder began, fifteen years have passed. The younger generation no longer sees the customs of benevolence, righteousness, propriety, and humility; this deeply saddens me. Therefore, I command that each commandery and state must cultivate scholarship; in counties with a population of at least 500 households, establish school officials. Select the outstanding talents from their hometowns to educate them, so that the ways of the former kings may not be abandoned and thus benefit the world."

Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
八月，公征劉表，軍西平。公之去鄴而南也，譚、尚爭兾州，譚為尚所敗，走保平原。尚攻之急，譚遣辛毗乞降請救。諸將皆疑，荀攸勸公許之，魏書曰：公云：「我攻呂布，表不為寇，官渡之役，不救袁紹，此自守之賊也，宜為後圖。譚、尚狡猾，當乘其亂。縱譚挾詐，不終束手，使我破尚，徧收其地，利自多矣。」乃許之。公乃引軍還。冬十月，到黎陽，為子整與譚結婚。臣松之案：紹死至此，過周五月耳。譚雖出後其伯，不為紹服三年，而於再朞之內以行吉禮，悖矣。魏武或以權宜與之約言；今云結婚，未必便以此年成禮。尚聞公北，乃釋平原還鄴。東平呂曠、呂翔叛尚，屯陽平，率其衆降，封為列侯。魏書曰：譚之圍解，陰以將軍印綬假曠。曠受印送之，公曰：「我固知譚之有小計也。欲使我攻尚，得以其閒略民聚衆，比尚之破，可得自彊以乘我弊也。尚破我盛，何弊之乘乎？」
In August, Gong launched a campaign against Liu Biao, with his army stationed at Xiping. When Gong left Ye and moved southward, Yuan Tan and Yuan Shang vied for control of Ji Zhou. Yuan Tan was defeated by Yuan Shang and fled to take refuge in Pingyuan. Yuan Shang pressed his attack urgently, so Yuan Tan sent Xin Pi to request surrender and seek rescue. The generals were all doubtful, but Xun You advised Gong to accept the surrender. The Wei Shu records: Gong said, "When I attacked Lu Bu, Liu Biao did not become an enemy; during the Guandu campaign, he did not come to Yuan Shao's aid. He is merely a bandit defending his own territory and should be dealt with at a later time." Yuan Tan and Yuan Shang are cunning; we should take advantage of their chaos. Even if Yuan Tan resorts to deception and does not ultimately surrender, by defeating Yuan Shang and seizing all his territory, we will gain much benefit." Thus, he agreed. Gong then led his army back. In the tenth month of winter, he arrived at Liyang and arranged a marriage between his son Cao Zheng and Yuan Tan. Min Songzhi's annotation: From Yuan Shao's death to this point, only five months had passed. Although Yuan Tan was adopted by his uncle, he did not observe a three-year mourning period for Yuan Shao. To conduct a wedding within two years of the death is contrary to propriety. Emperor Wu of Wei may have made this arrangement out of expediency; It is not certain that the wedding was actually held in this year. Yuan Shang, hearing of Gong's northern campaign, abandoned Pingyuan and returned to Ye. Lü Kuang and Lü Xiang of Dongping rebelled against Yuan Shang, stationing their forces at Yangping. They led their troops in surrender and were enfeoffed as Marquises. The Wei Shu says: After Yuan Tan's siege was lifted, he secretly gave the seal of a general to Lü Kuang. Lü Kuang accepted the seal and presented it to Gong, who said: "I have always known that Yuan Tan had a minor scheme. He wanted me to attack Yuan Shang so that he could take advantage of the situation to gather civilians and troops. Once Yuan Shang is defeated, he would grow stronger and strike when I am weakened." Yuan Shang's defeat will be my strength; how could there then be an opportunity for him to exploit weakness?"

61
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
九年春正月，濟河，遏淇水入白溝以通糧道。二月，尚復攻譚，留蘇由、審配守鄴。公進軍到洹水，由降。旣至，攻鄴，為土山、地道。武安長尹楷屯毛城，通上黨糧道。夏四月，留曹洪攻鄴，公自將擊楷，破之而還。尚將沮鵠守邯鄲，沮音菹，河朔閒今猶有此姓。鵠，沮授子也。又擊拔之。易陽令韓範、涉長梁岐舉縣降，賜爵關內侯。五月，毀土山、地道，作圍壍，決漳水灌城；城中餓死者過半。秋七月，尚還救鄴，諸將皆以為「此歸師，人自為戰，不如避之」。公曰：「尚從大道來，當避之；若循西山來者，此成禽耳。」尚果循西山來，臨滏水為營。曹瞞傳曰：遣候者數部前後參之，皆曰「定從西道，已在邯鄲」。公大喜，會諸將曰：「孤已得兾州，諸君知之乎？」皆曰：「不知。」公曰：「諸君方見不乆也。」夜遣兵犯圍，公逆擊破走之，遂圍其營。未合，尚懼。故豫州刺史陰夔及陳琳乞降，公不許，為圍益急。尚夜遁，保祁山，追擊之。其將馬延、張顗等臨陣降，衆大潰，尚走中山。盡獲其輜重，得尚印綬節鉞，使尚降人示其家，城中崩沮。八月，審配兄子榮夜開所守城東門內兵。配逆戰，敗，生禽配，斬之，鄴定。公臨祀紹墓，哭之流涕；慰勞紹妻，還其家人寶物，賜雜繒絮，廩食之。孫盛云：昔者先王之為誅賞也，將以懲惡勸善，永彰鑒戒。紹因世艱危，遂懷逆謀，上議神器，下干國紀。荐社汙宅，古之制也。而乃盡哀於逆臣之冢，加恩於饕餮之室，為政之道，於斯躓矣。夫匿怨友人，前哲所恥，稅驂舊館，義無虛涕，苟道乖好絕，何哭之有！昔漢高失之於項氏，魏武遵謬於此舉，豈非百慮之一失也。
In the first month of spring, the ninth year, they crossed the Ji River and dammed the Qi Water into Baigou to secure the supply route. In February, Yuan Shang again attacked Yuan Tan, leaving Su You and Shen Pei in charge of defending Ye. Gong advanced his army to Huanshui, where Su You surrendered. After arriving, he launched an attack on Ye and constructed earthen hills and underground tunnels for siege operations. Yin Kai, the magistrat of Wu'an, stationed his troops at Mao Cheng to secure the grain supply route from Shangdang. In the fourth month of summer, Cao Hong was left behind to attack Ye while Gong personally led troops against Yin Kai, defeating him and returning. Yuan Shang's general Ju Gu was in charge of defending Handan; the surname Ju is pronounced Zu, and this name still exists among people in He Shuo today. Ju Gu was the son of Ju Shou. He then attacked and captured them. Han Fan, the county magistrate of Yiyang, and Liang Qi, the magistrat of She, surrendered their counties; they were granted the title of Guannei Hou (Marquis within the Passes). In May, the earthen hills and tunnels were destroyed, a surrounding trench was constructed, and the Zhang River was dammed to flood the city; More than half of those inside the city died from starvation. In the seventh month of autumn, Yuan Shang returned to relieve Ye; all the generals believed "this is a returning army, where each man fights for his own survival. It would be better to avoid them." Gong said: "If Yuan Shang comes via the main road, we should avoid him; but if he follows the western mountain route, it will be as good as capturing him already." Yuan Shang indeed followed the western mountain route and set up camp by the Fushui River. The Cao Man Zhuan records: Several groups of scouts were sent ahead and behind, all reporting "he definitely took the western route and is already in Handan." Gong was greatly pleased and summoned his generals, saying: "I have already secured Ji Zhou; do you all know this?" They all replied: "We don't know." Gong said, "You will soon see for yourselves." At night, troops were sent to assault the encampment; Gong launched a counterattack and drove them away, then proceeded to surround their camp. Before they could regroup, Yuan Shang was already afraid. Therefore, Yin Kui, the former Yu Zhou Cishi, and Chen Lin requested surrender, but Gong refused, tightening the siege even further. At night, Yuan Shang fled to take refuge at Qishan, where he was pursued and attacked. His generals Ma Yan and Zhang Yi surrendered in the midst of battle; his forces collapsed, and Yuan Shang fled to Zhongshan. All of his supplies were captured, including Yuan Shang's seals, staffs, and axes of authority. Gong sent these to Yuan Shang's surrendered men to show to their families in the city, causing panic and despair among its defenders. In August, Shen Pei's nephew, Shen Rong, opened the eastern gate of the city he was guarding at night to let in the troops. Shen Pei resisted and fought a battle but was defeated, captured alive, executed, and Ye was pacified. Gong personally visited the tomb of Yuan Shao to perform rites in his honor, weeping bitterly as he did so; he comforted and paid respects to Yuan Shao's wife, returned her family's treasures, gave them various silk goods and cotton wadding, and provided grain for their sustenance. Sun Sheng said: "In the past, when sage kings carried out punishments and rewards, it was to punish evil and encourage virtue, forever making clear a lesson for reflection." Yuan Shao, taking advantage of the perilous times, harbored rebellious intentions. He plotted against imperial authority above and violated national laws below. To desecrate ancestral temples and defile noble estates is an ancient regulation. Yet you grieve over the tomb of a traitorous minister and bestow kindness upon the house of gluttonous villains; thus, the way of governance stumbles here. To conceal resentment toward a friend is something sages of old would be ashamed of. To weep at an old inn for a departed companion, if righteousness does not allow false tears—should the path diverge and friendship break, what need is there to cry! In former times, Emperor Gaozu of Han erred in his dealings with the Xiang clan; Wei Wu followed this mistaken course in this action—was it not one error among a hundred considerations?

62
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
初，紹與公共起兵，紹問公曰：「若事不輯，則方面何所可據？」公曰：「足下意以為何如？」紹曰：「吾南據河，北阻燕、代，兼戎狄之衆，南向以爭天下，庶可以濟乎？」公曰：「吾任天下之智力，以道御之，無所不可。」傅子曰：太祖又云：「湯、武之王，豈同上哉？若以險固為資，則不能應機而變化也。」
Initially, Yuan Shao and Gong raised troops together. Yuan Shao asked Gong: "If our cause fails, where should we take refuge?" Gong replied: "What do you think, my lord?" Yuan Shao said: "I would take the southern bank of the Yellow River, block the north with Yan and Dai, unite the Rong and Di tribes, face south to contend for the empire, and perhaps thereby succeed?" Gong said: "I will rely on the wisdom and strength of all under heaven, governing them through principle; there is nothing that cannot be done." Fu Zi said: "Taizu also said: 'The kings Tang and Wu, were they not different from those above?'" "If one relies on perilous terrain as a resource, then one cannot respond to circumstances with flexibility and change."

武帝紀:
九月，令曰：「河北罹袁氏之難，其令無出今年租賦！」重豪彊兼并之法，百姓喜恱。魏書載公令曰：「有國有家者，不患寡而患不均，不患貧而患不安。袁氏之治也，使豪彊擅恣，親戚兼并；下民貧弱，代出租賦，衒鬻家財，不足應命；審配宗族，至乃藏匿罪人，為逋逃主。欲望百姓親附，甲兵彊盛，豈可得邪！其收田租畝四升，戶出絹二匹、緜二斤而已，他不得擅興發。郡國守相明檢察之，無令彊民有所隱藏，而弱民兼賦也。」天子以公領兾州牧，公讓還兖州。
In September, an edict was issued: "The region of Hebei has suffered under the calamity of Yuan's rule; therefore, no taxes or levies are to be collected for this year!" He reinforced laws against powerful and greedy land consolidation, which brought joy to the common people. The Wei Shu records an edict issued by Gong: "Those who govern a state or family need not fear scarcity but should fear inequality; they need not fear poverty but should fear instability. "Under Yuan's rule, the powerful and greedy acted with impunity, while relatives engaged in land consolidation; the common people were poor and weak, paying taxes on behalf of others, selling their family possessions to no avail, still unable to fulfill the demands; the Shen Pei clan even went so far as to hide criminals and became protectors of fugitives. How could one hope for the people's loyalty, or a strong and powerful army? It is clearly impossible!" Therefore, he collected only four sheng of grain per mu in land tax, and two bolts of silk and two jin of cotton per household; no other levies were to be arbitrarily imposed. "The magistrates and governors of commanderies and states must clearly inspect and supervise this, ensuring that the powerful do not conceal anything while the weak bear double burdens." The Son of Heaven appointed Gong as Ju Zhou Mu, but Gong declined and returned to Yan Zhou.

武帝紀:
公之圍鄴也，譚略取甘陵、安平、勃海、河閒。尚敗，還中山。譚攻之，尚奔故安，遂并其衆。公遺譚書，責以負約，與之絕婚，女還，然後進軍。譚懼，拔平原，走保南皮。十二月，公入平原，略定諸縣。
While Gong was besieging Ye, Yuan Tan swiftly captured Ganling, Anping, Bohai, and Hejian. After Yuan Shang's defeat, he retreated to Zhongshan. Yuan Tan attacked him, and Yuan Shang fled toward Gu'an, whereupon Yuan Tan absorbed his forces. Gong sent a letter to Yuan Tan, accusing him of breaking their agreement, and annulled the marriage between them. He returned his daughter before advancing with his troops. Yuan Tan was frightened, withdrew from Pingyuan, and fled to take refuge in Nanpi. In December, Gong entered Pingyuan and subdued the various counties.

65
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
十年春正月，攻譚，破之，斬譚，誅其妻子，兾州平。魏書曰：公攻譚，旦及日中不決；公乃自執桴鼓，士卒咸奮，應時破陷。下令曰：「其與袁氏同惡者，與之更始。」令民不得復私讎，禁厚葬，皆一之於法。是月，袁熙大將焦觸、張南等叛攻熙、尚，熙、尚奔三郡烏丸。觸等舉其縣降，封為列侯。初討譚時，民亡椎冰，臣松之以為討譚時，川渠水凍，使民椎冰以通舩，民憚役而亡。令不得降。頃之，亡民有詣門首者，公謂曰：「聽汝則違令，殺汝則誅首，歸深自藏，無為吏所獲。」民垂泣而去；後竟捕得。
In the first month of spring in the tenth year, Gong attacked Yuan Tan, defeated him, beheaded him, executed his wife and children, and pacified Ju Zhou. The Wei Shu says: "When Gong attacked Yuan Tan, the battle was undecided from dawn until noon; Gong then personally took up the drumsticks and struck the war drum. The soldiers were all inspired, and at once the enemy was broken and their defenses collapsed." An edict was issued: "Those who conspired with Yuan's faction in wickedness shall be given a new beginning." He ordered the people not to take private revenge, prohibited extravagant burials, and brought all matters under the law. In this month, Jiao Chu, a great general of Yuan Xi, Zhang Nan and others rebelled against Yuan Xi and Yuan Shang, attacking them. Yuan Xi and Yuan Shang fled to the Wuhuan of San Jun. Jiao Chu and others surrendered their counties; they were enfeoffed as Lie Hou (Marquises). Initially, when suppressing Yuan Tan, people fled while breaking ice. Minister Song Zhi believed that during the campaign against Yuan Tan, river channels were frozen; the people had to break the ice to allow boats to pass, and they fled due to fear of conscription for this labor. An order was issued forbidding surrender. Soon after, some of the runaway civilians came to his gate. Gong said to them: "If I listen to you, it would be a violation of my order; if I kill you, it would mean executing innocent people. Return and hide well, so that you will not fall into the hands of officials." The civilians wept bitterly as they left; later, however, they were eventually captured.

武帝紀:
夏四月，黑山賊張燕率其衆十餘萬降，封為列侯。故安趙犢、霍奴等殺幽州刺史、涿郡太守。三郡烏丸攻鮮于輔於獷平。續漢書郡國志曰：獷平，縣名，屬漁陽郡。秋八月，公征之，斬犢等，乃渡潞河救獷平，烏丸奔走出塞。
In the fourth month of summer, Zhang Yan, leader of the Heishan bandits, led more than 100,000 of his followers in surrender. He was enfeoffed as a Lie Hou (Marquis). Zhuo Du and Huo Nu of Guoan killed the You Zhou Cishi and Zhuo Jun Taishou. The Wuhuan of San Jun attacked Xianyu Fu at Guangping. Xu Han Shu: Quanguo Zhi says: "Guangping is the name of a xian, belonging to Yuyang Jun." In autumn, August: Gong led a campaign against them, beheaded Zhuo Du and others. He then crossed the Lu River to rescue Guangping; the Wuhuan fled out of the frontier.

武帝紀:
九月，令曰：「阿黨比周，先聖所疾也。聞兾州俗，父子異部，更相毀譽。昔直不疑無兄，世人謂之盜嫂；弟五伯魚三娶孤女，謂之撾婦翁；王鳳擅權，谷永比之申伯；王商忠議，張匡謂之左道：此皆以白為黑，欺天罔君者也。吾欲整齊風俗，四者不除，吾以為羞。」冬十月，公還鄴。
In September, an order was issued: "Favoritism and factionalism are abhorred by sage rulers of old. "I have heard that in Ju Zhou, father and son belong to different factions, and they slander or praise each other." "In the past, Zhi Buyi had no elder brother, yet the world called him a thief of his sister-in-law; the younger brother Wu Bo Yu married three times to orphaned women, and was said to have struck his father-in-law." Wang Feng seized power, and Gu Yong compared him to Shen Bo; Wang Shang offered loyal advice, yet Zhang Kuang called it a left-hand path: these are all cases of turning white into black, deceiving heaven and misleading the sovereign. "I wish to rectify customs; if these four practices are not eradicated, I consider it a disgrace." In winter, October: Gong returned to Ye.

武帝紀:
初，袁紹以甥高幹領并州牧，公之拔鄴，幹降，遂以為刺史。幹聞公討烏丸，乃以州叛，執上黨太守，舉兵守壺關口。遣樂進、李典擊之，幹還守壺關城。十一年春正月，公征幹。幹聞之，乃留其別將守城，走入匈奴，求救於單于，單于不受。公圍壺關三月，拔之。幹遂走荊州，上洛都尉王琰捕斬之。
Initially, Yuan Shao had appointed his nephew Gao Gan as Mu of Bing Zhou. When Gong captured Ye, Gao Gan surrendered and was therefore made Cishi (governor) of the region. When Gao Gan heard that Gong was campaigning against the Wuhuan, he rebelled with the state, seized the Taishou of Shangdang, and raised troops to defend the Huguan Pass. Gong dispatched Yue Jin and Li Dian to attack him; Gao Gan retreated to defend Huguan Cheng (Huguan City). In the first month of spring, the eleventh year: Gong led a campaign against Gao Gan. Gao Gan heard of this and left his deputy to defend the city while he fled into the Xiongnu, seeking aid from the Chanyu. The Chanyu refused to accept him. Gong besieged Huguan for three months and captured it. Gao Gan then fled to Jing Zhou, where the Shangluo Duyi Wang Yan captured and beheaded him.

武帝紀:
秋八月，公東征海賊管承，至淳于，遣樂進、李典擊破之，承走入海島。割東海之襄賁、郯、戚以益琅邪，省昌慮郡。魏書載十月乙亥令曰：「夫治世御衆，建立輔弼，誡在面從，詩稱『聽用我謀，庶無大悔』，斯實君臣懇懇之求也。吾充重任，每懼失中，頻年已來，不聞嘉謀，豈吾開延不勤之咎邪？自今已後，諸掾屬治中、別駕，常以月旦各言其失，吾將覽焉。」
In autumn, August: Gong led an eastern campaign against the pirate Guan Cheng. Upon reaching Chunyu, he dispatched Yue Jin and Li Dian who defeated him; Guan Cheng fled into a sea island. The Xiangbin, Tan, and Qi districts of Donghai were carved off to augment Langya Jun; Changlv Jun was abolished. The Wei Shu records the edict of October Yi Hai: "In governing a peaceful world and managing the people, it is essential to appoint capable assistants. One must be warned against mere nodding agreement; as the Shi Jing says, 'If you listen to my counsel, there will likely be no great regret.' This truly reflects the earnest desire between ruler and minister." "I bear a heavy responsibility, and I often fear making mistakes. In recent years, I have not heard of any wise counsel—could this be due to my own failure in encouraging open advice?" "From now on, all yuanshu, Zhizhong, and Biejia officials shall, at the beginning of each month, report my shortcomings; I will review them."

武帝紀:
三郡烏丸承天下亂，破幽州，略有漢民合十餘萬戶。袁紹皆立其酋豪為單于，以家人子為己女，妻焉。遼西單于蹋頓尤彊，為紹所厚，故尚兄弟歸之，數入塞為害。公將征之，鑿渠，自呼沲入泒水，泒音孤。名平虜渠；又從泃河口泃音句。鑿入潞河，名泉州渠，以通海。
The Wuhuan of San Jun took advantage of the chaos in the empire to attack You Zhou, capturing and ruling over more than 100,0o Han Chinese households. Yuan Shao had all their chieftains appointed as Chanyu and married his own daughters—actually the children of his family—to them. Tadun, Chanyu of Liaoxi, was especially powerful and had been favored by Yuan Shao; therefore, the brothers Yuan Shang submitted to him. They repeatedly entered the frontier regions, causing harm. Gong prepared to campaign against them and dug a canal from Huduo into Gu Shui; "Gu" is pronounced as "gu." It was named Pinglu Qu (the Canal for Subduing the Bandits); and also from Ju He Kou, where "Ju" is pronounced as "ju." A canal was dug into the Lu River and named Quanzhou Qu (Quanzhou Canal), to connect with the sea.

武帝紀:
十二月春二月，公自淳于還鄴。丁酋，令曰：「吾起義兵誅暴亂，於今十九年，所征必克，豈吾功哉？乃賢士大夫之力也。天下雖未悉定，吾當要與賢士大夫共定之；而專饗其勞，吾何以安焉！其促定功行封。」於是大封功臣二十餘人，皆為列侯，其餘各以次受封，及復死事之孤，輕重各有差。魏書載公令曰：「昔趙奢、竇嬰之為將也，受賜千金，一朝散之，故能濟成大功，永世流聲。吾讀其文，未甞不慕其為人也。與諸將士大夫共從戎事，幸賴賢人不愛其謀，羣士不遺其力，是以夷險平亂，而吾得竊大賞，戶邑三萬。追思竇嬰散金之義，今分所受租與諸將掾屬及故戍於陳、蔡者，庶以疇荅衆勞，不擅大惠也。宜差死事之孤，以租穀及之。若年殷用足，租奉畢入，將大與衆人悉共饗之。」
In December, spring in February: Gong returned from Chunyu to Ye. On the Dingchou day, an edict was issued: "I raised a righteous army to punish violence and chaos. Now it has been nineteen years since then. Every campaign I have led has ended in victory—was this due to my own merit?" It was the strength of the virtuous scholars and officials. Though the empire is not yet fully pacified, I must now join with these virtuous men to complete its unification; yet if I alone enjoy the fruits of their labor, how can I feel at peace! Therefore, quickly determine merits and bestow enfeoffments accordingly." Thus, more than twenty meritorious subjects were greatly enfeoffed as Liehou (Marquises), while the rest received lesser titles in order. Additionally, orphans of those who had died in service were also rewarded, with distinctions made according to their rank and contribution. The Wei Shu records a decree issued by Gong: "In the past, General Zhao She and Dou Ying were commanders who received a thousand gold pieces as reward but gave it all away in one day. Thus they achieved great success and left their names for eternity. "When I read about them, I have never failed to admire the kind of people they were." "Having served with generals and officials in military affairs, I was fortunate to rely on wise men who did not withhold their strategies, and the assembled scholars who did not spare their strength. Thus we overcame perilous situations and quelled chaos, allowing me to secretly receive great rewards—three ten-thousands of households under my fief." "Reflecting on Dou Ying's virtue of distributing gold, I now divide the rents from my fief among the generals, yuanshu officials, and former garrisons stationed in Chen and Cai. This is to repay their labors fairly and not monopolize great benefits for myself." It is appropriate to distinguish the orphans of those who died in service, providing them with rent grain accordingly. "If the harvest is abundant and expenses are met, once all rents and tributes have been collected, I will greatly share them with everyone to enjoy together."

武帝紀:
將北征三郡烏丸，諸將皆曰：「袁尚，亡虜耳，夷狄貪而無親，豈能為尚用？今深入征之，劉備必說劉表以襲許。萬一為變，事不可悔。」惟郭嘉策表必不能任備，勸公行。夏五月，至無終。秋七月，大水，傍海道不通，田疇請為鄉導，公從之。引軍出盧龍塞，塞外道絕不通，乃壍山堙谷五百餘里，經白檀，歷平岡，涉鮮卑庭，東指柳城。未至二百里，虜乃知之。尚、熙與蹋頓、遼西單于樓班、右北平單于能臣抵之等，將數萬騎逆軍。八月，登白狼山，卒與虜遇，衆甚盛。公車重在後，被甲者少，左右皆懼。公登高，望虜陳不整，乃縱兵擊之，使張遼為先鋒，虜衆大崩，斬蹋頓及名王已下，胡、漢降者二十餘萬口。遼東單于速僕丸及遼西、北平諸豪，棄其種人，與尚、熙奔遼東，衆尚有數千騎。初，遼東太守公孫康恃遠不服。及公破烏丸，或說公遂征之，尚兄弟可禽也。公曰：「吾方使康斬送尚、熙首，不煩兵矣。」九月，公引兵自柳城還，曹瞞傳曰：時寒且旱，二百里無復水，軍又乏食，殺馬數千匹以為糧，鑿地入三十餘丈乃得水。旣還，利問前諫者，衆莫知其故，人人皆懼。公皆厚賞之，曰：「孤前行，乘危以徼倖，雖得之，天所佐也，顧不可以為常。諸君之諫，萬安之計，是以相賞，後勿難言之。」康即斬尚、熙及速僕丸等，傳其首。諸將或問：「公還而康斬送尚、熙，何也？」公曰：「彼素畏尚等，吾急之則并力，緩之則自相圖，其勢然也。」十一月至易水，代郡烏丸行單于普富盧、上郡烏丸行單于那樓將其名王來賀。
Gong was preparing to launch a northern campaign against the Wuhuan of San Jun, and all his generals said: "Yuan Shang is merely a fugitive. The barbarians are greedy and have no loyalty—how could they possibly be used by Yuan Shang?" "Now, if we launch a deep campaign against them, Liu Bei will surely persuade Liu Biao to attack Xu." "If there is even the slightest chance of an unexpected turn of events, it would be too late to regret our decision." Only Guo Jia predicted that Liu Biao would certainly not entrust the matter to Liu Bei and advised Gong to proceed. In the fifth month of summer, they arrived at Wuzhong. In the seventh month of autumn, there was a great flood and the coastal roads were impassable. Tian Chou requested to serve as a local guide, and Gong followed his suggestion. The army led its forces out of Lulong Sai, but the roads outside the pass were completely impassable. They then dug trenches and filled valleys for more than five hundred li, passing through Baitan, crossing Pinggang, traversing Xianbei territory, and heading east toward Liu Cheng. Before reaching within two hundred li of the destination, the enemy learned of their approach. Yuan Shang and Yuan Xi, together with Tadun, Lou Ban the chanyu of Liaoxi, Nengchen Dizhi the chanyu of Youbeiping, led tens of thousands of cavalry to intercept the army. In the eighth month, they ascended Bailingang Mountain and unexpectedly encountered the enemy forces, which were very numerous. Gong's heavily laden carriages were in the rear, with few soldiers clad in armor, and those around him were all frightened. Gong ascended a high place and observed that the enemy formation was disorganized. He then ordered his troops to attack, appointing Zhang Liao as vanguard. The enemy forces collapsed in great numbers; Tadun and several named kings were beheaded, and more than 200,000 captives—both Hu and Han—surrendered. The chanyu of Liaodong, Supowan, and the various local leaders from Liaoxi and Beiping abandoned their tribes and fled with Yuan Shang and Yuan Xi to Liaodong. They still had several thousand cavalry remaining. Initially, the governor of Liaodong, Gong Sun Kang, relied on his distance and did not submit in obedience. When Gong defeated the Wuhuan, some advised him to immediately launch a campaign against Gong Sun Kang, saying that Yuan Shang and his brothers could then be captured. Gong said: "I am just about to have Gong Sun Kang execute them and send their heads, so there is no need for military action." In the ninth month, Gong led his troops back from Liu Cheng. The Cao Man Zhuan records: At that time it was cold and dry; there was no water for two hundred li. The army also lacked food, so they slaughtered several thousand horses as provisions, and had to dig more than thirty zhang into the ground before finding water. After returning, Gong asked about those who had previously advised against this campaign. No one knew the reason for his inquiry, and everyone was afraid. Gong generously rewarded them all, saying: "My previous advance was a gamble taken in peril; although I succeeded, it was aided by Heaven. However, such success cannot be relied upon as a regular occurrence. "Your advice represented the safest course of action, which is why I reward you. In the future, do not hesitate to speak freely." Gong Sun Kang immediately executed Yuan Shang, Yuan Xi, and Supowan, sending their heads. Some of the generals asked: "Why did Gong Sun Kang kill and send the heads of Yuan Shang and Yuan Xi after we returned?" Gong said: "He had long feared Yuan Shang and others. If I pressed him hard, he would unite with them; if I relaxed my pressure, they would turn on each other. It was a matter of circumstances." In the eleventh month, they arrived at Yishui. Pufulu, acting chanyu of the Wuhuan from Dai Jun, and Nalu, acting chanyu from Shangjun, led their named kings to offer congratulations.

武帝紀:
十三年春正月，公還鄴，作玄武池以肄舟師。肄，以四反。三蒼曰：「肄，習也。」漢罷三公官，置丞相、御史大夫。夏六月，以公為丞相。獻帝起居注曰：使太常徐璆即授印綬。御史大夫不領中丞，置長史一人。先賢行狀曰：璆字孟平，廣陵人。少履清爽，立朝正色。歷任城、汝南、東海三郡，所在化行。被徵當還，為袁術所劫。術僭號，欲授以上公之位，璆終不為屈。術死後，璆得術璽，致之漢朝，拜衞尉太常；公為丞相，以位讓璆焉。
In the first month of spring in the thirteenth year, Gong returned to Ye and constructed Xuanwu Chi (the Black Tortoise Pool) for training naval forces. "Yi," pronounced with four tones. The San Cang says: "Yi means to practice or rehearse." The Han dynasty abolished the offices of the Three Dukes and established instead the positions of Chancellor (Chengxiang) and Grand Censor-in-Chief (Yushi Daifu). In the sixth month of summer, Gong was appointed as Chancellor. The Xian Di Qi Ju Zhu records: The Grand Sacrificial Official Xu Qiu was sent to present the seal and sash of office. The position of Grand Censor-in-Chief did not include a Zhongcheng (Chief Censor), but one Chief Clerk (Changshi) was appointed instead. Xianxian Xingzhuang records: Qiu, courtesy name Mengping, was a native of Guangling. He was from an early age upright and clear-minded, maintaining a dignified demeanor in court affairs. Having served as governor of the three commanderies of Rencheng, Rujnan, and Donghai, wherever he was stationed, moral influence prevailed. When summoned for a recall to court service, he was intercepted by Yuan Shu. Yuan Shu assumed an imperial title and wished to bestow upon him the position of a high-ranking official, but Qiu remained steadfast and refused to yield. After Yuan Shu's death, Qiu obtained his seal of imperial authority and returned it to the Han court, for which he was appointed as Weiwei Tai Chang. When Gong became Chancellor, he offered the position to Qiu instead.

74
Jump to dictionary

武帝紀:
秋七月，公南征劉表。八月，表卒，其子琮代，屯襄陽，劉備屯樊。九月，公到新野，琮遂降，備走夏口。公進軍江陵，下令荊州吏民，與之更始。乃論荊州服從之功，侯者十五人，以劉表大將文聘為江夏太守，使統本兵，引用荊州名士韓嵩、鄧義等。衞恒四體書勢序曰：上谷王次仲善隷書，始為楷法。至靈帝好書，世多能者。而師宜官為最，甚矜其能，每書，輙削焚其札。梁鵠乃益為版而飲之酒，候其醉而竊其札，鵠卒以攻書至選部尚書。於是公欲為洛陽令，鵠以為北部尉。鵠後依劉表。及荊州平，公募求鵠，鵠懼，自縛詣門，署軍假司馬，使在祕書，以勤書自効。公甞懸著帳中，及以釘壁玩之，謂勝宜官。鵠字孟皇，安定人。魏宮殿題署，皆鵠書也。皇甫謐逸士傳曰：汝南王儁，字子文，少為范滂、許章所識，與南陽岑晊善。公之為布衣，特愛儁；儁亦稱公有治世之具。及袁紹與弟術喪母，歸葬汝南，儁與公會之，會者三萬人。公於外密語儁曰：「天下將亂，為亂魁者必此二人也。欲濟天下，為百姓請命，不先誅此二子，亂今作矣。」儁曰：「如卿之言，濟天下者，舍卿復誰？」相對而笑。儁為人外靜而內明，不應州郡三府之命。公車徵，不到，避地居武陵，歸儁者一百餘家。帝之都許，復徵為尚書，又不就。劉表見紹彊，陰與紹通，儁謂表曰：「曹公，天下之雄也，必能興霸道，繼桓、文之功者也。今乃釋近而就遠，如有一朝之急，遙望漠北之救，不亦難乎！」表不從。儁年六十四，以壽終于武陵，公聞而哀傷。及平荊州，自臨江迎喪，改葬于江陵，表為先賢也。益州牧劉璋始受徵役，遣兵給軍。十二月，孫權為備攻合肥。公自江陵征備，至巴丘，遣張憙救合肥。權聞憙至，乃走。公至赤壁，與備戰，不利。於是大疫，吏士多死者，乃引軍還。備遂有荊州、江南諸郡。山陽公載記曰：公船艦為備所燒，引軍從華容道步歸，遇泥濘，道不通，天又大風，悉使羸兵負草填之，騎乃得過。羸兵為人馬所蹈藉，陷泥中，死者甚衆。軍旣得出，公大喜，諸將問之，公曰：「劉備，吾儔也。但得計少晚；向使早放火，吾徒無類矣。」備尋亦放火而無所及。孫盛異同評曰：案吳志，劉備先破公軍，然後權攻合肥，而此記云權先攻合肥，後有赤壁之事。二者不同，吳志為是。
In the seventh month of autumn, Gong launched a southern campaign against Liu Biao. In the eighth month, Liu Biao died and his son Liu Cong succeeded him, stationing troops at Xiangyang, while Liu Bei stationed his forces at Fan. In the ninth month, Gong arrived at Xinye, and Liu Cong immediately surrendered; Liu Bei fled to Jiakou. Gong advanced his army toward Jiangling and issued an order to the officials and people of Jingzhou, promising a new beginning for all. He then evaluated the merits of those in Jingzhou who had submitted, enfeoffing fifteen as marquises. He appointed Liu Biao's prominent general Wen Pin as Tai Shou (Governor) of Jiangxia, allowing him to command his original forces and recommending distinguished local scholars from Jingzhou such as Han Song and Deng Yi. Wei Heng's "Preface to the Four Styles of Calligraphy" states: Wang Cizhong from Shanggu was skilled in clerical script and first established the rules for kaishu (regular script). By the time Emperor Lingdi favored calligraphy, many people in society had become proficient. Among them, Shi Yiguan was the most outstanding; he took great pride in his skill and often burned the slips of paper after writing on them. Liang Hu, however, devised a way to obtain them by offering him wine and waiting for him to become drunk before secretly taking the slips. Eventually, Liang Hu became known as an expert in calligraphy and was appointed as Shangshu of Xuanbu (Ministry of Personnel). At that time, Gong wished to become the magistrate of Luoyang, and Liang Hu was appointed as the Wei (commandant) of Beibu. Later, Liang Hu relied on Liu Biao for support. After Jingzhou was pacified, Gong issued a summons for Liang Hu. Fearing punishment, Liang Hu bound himself and presented himself at the gates; he was then appointed as Junjia Sima (acting military officer) and placed in charge of secretarial affairs, where he diligently practiced calligraphy to demonstrate his service. Gong once hung them in the tent and also nailed some on the wall for appreciation, saying they surpassed Shi Yiguan. Liang Hu's courtesy name was Menghuang; he was a native of Ding'an. The inscriptions on the palaces and halls in Wei were all written by Liang Hu. Huangfu Mi's Yishi Zhuan records: Wang Jun of Ru'nan, courtesy name Ziwen, was recognized from a young age by Fan Pang and Xu Zhang; he was on good terms with Cen Zhi of Nanyang. When Gong was still an ordinary citizen, he especially cherished Wang Jun; Wang Jun also praised Gong as possessing the qualities necessary to govern in a time of peace. When Yuan Shao and his brother Yuan Shu returned to Ru'nan for their mother's funeral, Wang Jun met Gong with them; the gathering attracted thirty thousand attendees. Outside, Gong whispered to Wang Jun: "The world is about to fall into chaos, and these two men will surely be the ones who lead it." "If we wish to save the world and plead for the people's lives, we must first eliminate these two men; otherwise, chaos will erupt now." Wang Jun said: "If you speak as you do, then who else besides you can save the world?" They smiled at each other. Wang Jun was a man who appeared outwardly calm but had inner clarity; he refused the appointments from three local offices of commanderies and states. When summoned by imperial decree, he did not attend, instead relocating to live in Wuling; more than a hundred families followed him there. When the emperor relocated his capital to Xu, he was again summoned as Shangshu (Minister of Personnel), but once more refused the appointment. Liu Biao, seeing Yuan Shao's strength, secretly communicated with him. Wang Jun told Liu Biao: "Cao Gong is a great man of the world; he will surely establish hegemony and continue the achievements of Huan and Wen." "Now you are abandoning a near ally to seek one far away. If there is an urgent crisis in the morning, looking for distant aid from the northern steppes—wouldn't that be difficult!" Liu Biao did not follow his advice. Wang Jun died at the age of sixty-four in Wuling, and Gong heard of it and was deeply grieved. After pacifying Jingzhou, he personally went to the riverfront to welcome Wang Jun's funeral procession and reburied him in Jiangling, honoring him as a sage of former generations. Liu Zhang, the Inspector of Yizhou, initially accepted the summons for military service and sent troops to support the army. In the twelfth month, Sun Quan attacked Hefei on behalf of Liu Bei. Gong personally led an expedition from Jiangling to attack Liu Bei, reaching Bachu and sending Zhang Xi to rescue Hefei. Sun Quan heard that Zhang Xi had arrived and withdrew his forces. Gong reached Chibi, where he engaged Liu Bei in battle but suffered a setback. At that time there was an outbreak of plague and many officials and soldiers died; thus, the army withdrew. Liu Bei then took control of Jingzhou and all the commanderies in southern Jiangnan. The Shanyang Gong Zaiji records: The ships of Gong's fleet were burned by Liu Bei. Forced to retreat, the army took the Huarong Road on foot and encountered deep mud where the path was blocked. With strong winds in the sky, they ordered all the weak soldiers to carry grass and fill it in so that the cavalry could pass through. The weakened soldiers were trampled by men and horses, sank into the mud, and many died. Once the army had managed to escape, Gong was greatly relieved. When his generals asked about it, he said: "Liu Bei is my equal." "He just acted a little too late;" "If he had set the fire earlier, none of us would have survived." Liu Bei soon also set a fire but it was ineffective. Sun Sheng's Yitong Ping records: According to the Wu Zhi, Liu Bei first defeated Gong's army, and only then did Sun Quan attack Hefei; yet this record states that Sun Quan attacked Hefei first before the Chibi campaign. The two accounts differ, but the Wu Zhi is correct.

武帝紀:
十四年春三月，軍至譙，作輕舟，治水軍。秋七月，自渦入淮，出肥水，軍合肥。辛未，令曰：「自頃已來，軍數征行，或遇疫氣，吏士死亡不歸，家室怨曠，百姓流離，而仁者豈樂之哉？不得已也。其令死者家無基業不能自存者，縣官勿絕廩，長吏存卹撫循，以稱吾意。」置揚州郡縣長吏，開芍陂屯田。十二月，軍還譙。
In the third month of spring in the fourteenth year, the army arrived at Qiao and constructed light boats while organizing a naval force. In the seventh month of autumn he led his forces from Guo into Huai, then through Fei Shui to Hefei and stationed troops there. On the Xinwei day, an order was issued: "Since recent times, our army has frequently campaigned. Some have encountered plagues and died without returning home, leaving their families grieving and abandoned, while common people suffer displacement. How could a benevolent person take pleasure in this?" "It is an unavoidable necessity." "Therefore, I order that families of the deceased who lack resources and cannot support themselves must not have their grain rations cut off by local officials. Senior magistrates should show concern, provide care, and offer comfort in accordance with my wishes." He appointed magistrates for commanderies and counties in Yangzhou and initiated the construction of Shao Bei for military farming. In December, the army returned to Qiao.

武帝紀:
十五年春，下令曰：「自古受命及中興之君，曷甞不得賢人君子與之共治天下者乎！及其得賢也，曾不出閭巷，豈幸相遇哉？上之人不求之耳。今天下尚未定，此特求賢之急時也。『孟公綽為趙、魏老則優，不可以為滕、薛大夫』。若必廉士而後可用，則齊桓其何以霸世！今天下得無有被褐懷玉而釣於渭濵者乎？又得無盜嫂受金而未遇無知者乎？二三子其佐我明揚仄陋，唯才是舉，吾得而用之。」冬，作銅爵臺。魏武故事載公十二月己亥令曰：「孤始舉孝廉，年少，自以本非巖穴知名之士，恐為海內人之所見凡愚，欲為一郡守，好作政教，以建立名譽，使世士明知之；故在濟南，始除殘去穢，平心選舉，違迕諸常侍。以為彊豪所忿，恐致家禍，故以病還。去官之後，年紀尚少，顧視同歲中，年有五十，未名為老，內自圖之，從此却去二十年，待天下清，乃與同歲中始舉者等耳。故以四時歸鄉里，於譙東五十里築精舍，欲秋夏讀書，冬春射獵，求底下之地，欲以泥水自蔽，絕賔客往來之望，然不能得如意。後徵為都尉，遷典軍校尉，意遂更欲為國家討賊立功，欲望封侯作征西將軍，然後題墓道言『漢故征西將軍曹侯之墓』，此其志也。而遭值董卓之難，興舉義兵。是時合兵能多得耳，然常自損，不欲多之；所以然者，多兵意盛，與彊敵爭，儻更為禍始。故汴水之戰數千，後還到揚州更募，亦復不過三千人，此其本志有限也。後領兖州，破降黃巾三十萬衆。又袁術僭號於九江，下皆稱臣，名門曰建號門，衣被皆為天子之制，兩婦預爭為皇后。志計已定，人有勸術使遂即帝位，露布天下，荅言『曹公尚在，未可也』。後孤討禽其四將，獲其人衆，遂使術窮亡解沮，發病而死。及至袁紹據河北，兵勢彊盛，孤自度勢，實不敵之，但計投死為國，以義滅身，足垂於後。幸而破紹，梟其二子。又劉表自以為宗室，包藏姧心，乍前乍却，以觀世事，據有當州，孤復定之，遂平天下。身為宰相，人臣之貴已極，意望已過矣。今孤言此，若為自大，欲人言盡，故無諱耳。設使國家無有孤，不知當幾人稱帝，幾人稱王。或者人見孤彊盛，又性不信天命之事，恐私心相評，言有不遜之志，妄相忖度，每用耿耿。齊桓、晉文所以垂稱至今日者，以其兵勢廣大，猶能奉事周室也。論語云『三分天下有其二，以服事殷，周之德可謂至德矣』，夫能以大事小也。昔樂毅走趙，趙王欲與之圖燕，樂毅伏而垂泣，對曰：『臣事昭王，猶事大王；臣若獲戾，放在他國，沒世然後已，不忍謀趙之徒隷，況燕後嗣乎！』胡亥之殺蒙恬也，恬曰：『自吾先人及至子孫，積信於秦三世矣；今臣將兵三十餘萬，其勢足以背叛，然自知必死而守義者，不敢辱先人之教以忘先王也。』孤每讀此二人書，未曾不愴然流涕也。孤祖父以至孤身，皆當親重之任，可謂見信者矣，以及子桓兄弟，過於三世矣。孤非徒對諸君說此，也常以語妻妾，皆令深知此意。孤謂之言：『顧我萬年之後，汝曹皆當出嫁，欲令傳道我心，使他人皆知之。』孤此言皆肝鬲之要也。所以勤勤懇懇敘心腹者，見周公有金縢之書以自明，恐人不信之故。然欲孤便爾委捐所典兵衆以還執事，歸就武平侯國，實不可也。何者？誠恐己離兵為人所禍也。旣為子孫計，又己敗則國家傾危，是以不得慕虛名而處實禍，此所不得為也。前朝恩封三子為侯，固辭不受，今更欲受之，非欲復以為榮，欲以為外援，為萬安計。孤聞介推之避晉封。申胥之逃楚賞，未甞不捨書而歎，有以自省也。奉國威靈，仗鉞征伐，推弱以克彊，處小而禽大，意之所圖，動無違事，心之所慮，何向不濟，遂蕩平天下，不辱主命，可謂天助漢室，非人力也。然封兼四縣，食戶三萬，何德堪之！江湖未靜，不可讓位；至於邑土，可得而辭。今上還陽夏、柘、苦三縣戶二萬，但食武平萬戶，且以分損謗議，少減孤之責也。」
In spring of the fifteenth year, an edict was issued: "Since ancient times, have any sovereigns who received their mandate or those who restored a dynasty ever succeeded without virtuous and noble men to assist them in governing the realm?" "When they did obtain such virtuous individuals, these men had not even left their villages—was it mere good fortune that brought them together?" "It is because those in power have failed to seek them out." "Now that the empire remains unsettled, this is precisely a time of urgent need for virtuous men." "Lord Meng Gongchuo was excellent as an elder in Zhao and Wei, but he could not serve as a magisterial official for Teng or Xue." "If only those who are incorruptible can be used, then how could Duke Huan of Qi have dominated the world!" "Now, is there not someone in the world who is clothed in coarse garments but possesses jade-like virtue, fishing by the banks of Wei?" "Or perhaps someone who has been falsely accused of stealing his sister-in-law's belongings and accepting gold but has yet to meet an impartial person?" "You, my disciples, should assist me in identifying those of humble origins and obscure status. Let us recommend only those with talent; I will appoint them to office." In winter, the Tongju Tai (Bronze Sparrow Terrace) was constructed. The Wei Wu Gu Shi records that on the Jiwei day of December, a decree was issued: "When I was first recommended as a filial and upright official, I was young. Considering myself not originally a renowned recluse or scholar, I feared being regarded by people throughout the land as an ordinary fool. Therefore, I wished to serve as a governor of a commandery, diligently implementing policies and education in order to establish my reputation so that scholars of the world would clearly recognize me; thus, while I was in Jining, I began to remove corrupt officials and eliminate corruption, impartially selecting talents, which led me to defy the eunuchs." I believed that powerful and arrogant individuals would resent this, fearing it might bring disaster upon my family, so I resigned on grounds of illness. After leaving office, I was still young. Looking at my contemporaries, some were fifty years old and had not yet been considered elderly. Reflecting on this internally, I resolved to withdraw for twenty more years until the realm became peaceful; then I would be comparable to those among my peers who had only just begun their official careers through recommendation. Therefore, I returned to my hometown in each season and built a refined study house fifty li east of Qiao. I intended to read during autumn and summer, and hunt during winter and spring. Seeking low-lying land, I wished the mud and water would naturally obscure me, cutting off expectations for visitors' comings and goings; yet this could not be fully realized as desired. Later, I was summoned to serve as Du Wei and later promoted to Dianjun Jiaowei. My aspirations then shifted toward serving the state by quelling rebels and establishing merit; I wished for a marquis title and to become General of the Western Expedition. Then, I intended that my tomb inscription would read "The Tomb of Marquis Cao, Former Western Expedition General of Han"—this was my ambition. But due to the calamity caused by Dong Zhuo, I raised a righteous army in response. At that time, it was possible to gather many troops, yet I often deliberately reduced my forces and did not wish for a large army; The reason was that having too many troops would lead to overconfidence, which could provoke conflict with powerful enemies and perhaps become the beginning of disaster. Therefore, during the battle at Bian Shui, I had only several thousand soldiers; when returning to Yangzhou later and recruiting anew, my forces did not exceed three thousand. This reflected my original limited ambition. Later, while governing Yan Zhou, I defeated and subdued thirty thousand Yellow Turban rebels. Also, Yuan Shu proclaimed himself emperor in Jiujiang; his subordinates all paid him homage. He named the main gate of his residence "Jianhao Gate," and his clothing and robes were made according to the pattern of an emperor. Two of his wives even vied for the title of empress. His plans were already set, and some advised Yuan Shu to formally assume the imperial title and announce it openly throughout the realm. He replied, "Cao Gong is still alive; it is not yet possible." Later, I captured four of his generals and seized their troops, which left Yuan Shu in dire straits. He became disheartened, fell ill, and died. When Yuan Shao occupied the region north of the Yellow River and his military strength was formidable, I assessed my own position and realized that I could not match him in power. Yet I resolved to face death for the sake of the state, sacrificing myself for righteousness, which would be sufficient to leave a legacy for future generations. Fortuitously, we defeated Yuan Shao and executed two of his sons. Liu Biao, considering himself a member of the imperial clan, harbored treacherous intentions and vacillated between advancing and retreating to observe the course of events. Holding control over Jing Zhou, I once again subdued him, thus achieving peace throughout the realm. As a prime minister, my position has already reached the highest rank among subjects of an emperor; my ambitions have long surpassed what is appropriate. Now I speak these words, and if it seems boastful, it is because I wish to lay all matters bare without concealment. If the state had no one like me, I do not know how many would proclaim themselves emperor and how many would declare themselves king. Perhaps some people, seeing my strength and knowing that I do not believe in the Mandate of Heaven, fear that out of personal bias they might judge me as having arrogant ambitions. They make groundless assumptions about me, which has always troubled me deeply. The reason why Duke Huan of Qi and Duke Wen of Jin are still remembered to this day is that, despite their formidable military power, they were still able to serve the Zhou royal court. The Analects says, "Possessing two-thirds of the realm yet serving Yin [Shang], the virtue of Zhou can be called supreme virtue," which is to say that one who holds great power still respects and serves those of lesser status. In the past, Yue Yi fled to Zhao, and King Zhao wished to ally with him against Yan. Yue Yi knelt down weeping and replied: "I served King Zhao of Yan as I would serve Your Majesty; If I were to commit a crime and be exiled to another state, I would remain loyal until my death. How could I bear to conspire against Zhao's subjects, let alone the descendants of Yan!" When Hu Hai killed Meng Tian, Meng Tian said: "From my ancestors to my descendants, our family has accumulated trust with the Qin dynasty for three generations; now I command more than 300,000 troops, and my strength is sufficient to rebel. Yet I know that death is inevitable while upholding righteousness; I dare not disgrace the teachings of my ancestors or betray the legacy of our former kings." Whenever I read about these two men, I have always been moved to tears. From my grandfather down to myself, we have all held positions of great trust and responsibility; this can truly be called being trusted. Including my son Cao Huan and his brothers, our family's service has now spanned more than three generations. I do not merely say these words to you all; I often speak of this with my wives and concubines, ensuring they fully understand its meaning. I have told them: "After my death, you will all remarry. I wish for you to convey these words and my intentions so that others may know of them." These words of mine are the most essential truths from the depths of my heart. The reason I have so earnestly and sincerely expressed these innermost thoughts is because, just as Duke of Zhou left behind the Jin Teng scroll to clarify his own intentions, I fear people may not believe me. Yet if I were suddenly to abandon the troops under my command and return them to others, resigning from office and returning to serve as marquis of Wu Ping Hou Guo, it would truly be impossible. Why is that? It is because I genuinely fear that if I leave my troops, I will be vulnerable to disaster at the hands of others. This is not only for the sake of my descendants but also because if I were to fail, the state would face grave peril. Therefore, I cannot pursue a false reputation while placing myself and others in real danger—this is something I simply cannot do. In the previous dynasty, three of my sons were bestowed marquis titles as a favor, but I firmly declined them. Now I wish to accept these honors not for personal glory, but to secure external support and ensure lasting stability for all. I have heard of Jie Tui's refusal of the Jin dynasty's offer of a title. And of Shen Xu fleeing from Chu's reward—never have I failed to lay down my book and sigh, reflecting on their actions for self-examination. Upholding the might and divine protection of our state, wielding authority to wage campaigns, we overcame the strong with the weak and subdued the mighty while in a position of weakness. Whatever I intended was always realized without failure; whatever I considered, no direction proved unattainable. Thus, I succeeded in pacifying the realm and fulfilled my sovereign's command. This can truly be said to have been Heaven aiding the Han dynasty—not merely through human effort alone. Yet now I am granted fiefs over four counties and enjoys revenues from thirty thousand households—what virtue or merit do I possess to deserve such honors! The rivers and lakes are not yet calm; I cannot relinquish my position. As for the fiefs of land, however, they may be returned. Therefore, I now return the revenues of two thousand households from Yang Xia, Zhe, and Ku counties, retaining only ten thousand households in Wu Ping. This is to share the burden of criticism and reduce my own responsibility."

武帝紀:
十六年春正月，魏書曰：庚辰，天子報：減戶五千，分所讓三縣萬五千封三子，植為平原侯，據為范陽侯，豹為饒陽侯，食邑各五千戶。天子命公世子丕為五官中郎將，置官屬，為丞相副。太原商曜等以大陵叛，遣夏侯淵、徐晃圍破之。張魯據漢中，三月，遣鍾繇討之。公使淵等出河東與繇會。
In the first month of spring in the sixteenth year, according to the Wei Shu: On the Gengchen day, the Son of Heaven responded by reducing my fief by five thousand households. Of the fifteen thousand households from the three counties I had offered back, ten thousand were divided and granted as titles for my three sons—Cao Zhi was made Gongzi of Pingyuan Hou, Cao Ju as Fan Yang Hou, and Cao Bao as Rao Yang Hou, each receiving fiefs of five thousand households. The Son of Heaven appointed the crown prince Pi as Wuguan Zhonglangjiang, established his official staff, and designated him as deputy to the prime minister. Shang Yao of Taiyuan rebelled at Daling; Xiahou Yuan and Xu Huang were dispatched to surround and defeat them. Zhang Lu occupied Hanzhong. In the third month, Zhong Yao was sent to campaign against him. The ruler ordered Yuan and others to depart from Hedong to join forces with Zhong Yáo.

武帝紀:
是時關中諸將疑繇欲自襲，馬超遂與韓遂、楊秋、李堪、成宜等叛。遣曹仁討之。超等屯潼關，公勑諸將：「關西兵精悍，堅壁勿與戰。」秋七月，公西征，魏書曰：議者多言「關西兵彊，習長矛，非精選前鋒，則不可以當也」。公謂諸將曰：「戰在我，非在賊也。賊雖習長矛，將使不得以刺，諸君但觀之耳。」與超等夾關而軍。公急持之，而潛遣徐晃、朱靈等夜渡蒲阪津，據河西為營。公自潼關北渡，未濟，超赴船急戰。校尉丁斐因放牛馬以餌賊，賊亂取牛馬，公乃得渡，曹瞞傳曰：公將過河，前隊適渡，超等奄至，公猶坐胡牀不起。張郃等見事急，共引公入船。河水急，北渡，流四五里，超等騎追射之，矢下如雨。諸將見軍敗，不知公所在，皆惶懼，至見，乃悲喜，或流涕。公大笑曰：「今日幾為小賊所困乎！」循河為甬道而南。賊退，拒渭口，公乃多設疑兵，潛以舟載兵入渭，為浮橋，夜，分兵結營於渭南。賊夜攻營，伏兵擊破之。超等屯渭南，遣信求割河以西請和，公不許。九月，進軍渡渭。曹瞞傳曰：時公軍每渡渭，輒為超騎所衝突，營不得立，地又多沙，不可築壘。婁子伯說公曰：「今天寒，可起沙為城，以水灌之，可一夜而成。」公從之，乃多作縑囊以運水，夜渡兵作城，比明，城立，由是公軍盡得渡渭。或疑于時九月，水未應凍。臣松之案魏書：公軍八月至潼關，閏月北渡河，則其年閏八月也，至此容可大寒邪！超等數挑戰，又不許；固請割地，求送任子，公用賈詡計，偽許之。韓遂請與公相見，公與遂父同歲孝廉，又與遂同時儕輩，於是交馬語移時，不及軍事，但說京都舊故，拊手歡笑。旣罷，超等問遂：「公何言？」遂曰：「無所言也。」超等疑之。魏書曰：公後日復與遂等會語，諸將曰：「公與虜交語，不宜輕脫，可為木行馬以為防遏。」公然之。賊將見公，悉於馬上拜，秦、胡觀者，前後重沓，公笑謂賊曰：「爾欲觀曹公邪？亦猶人也，非有四目兩口，但多智耳！」胡前後大觀。又列鐵騎五千為十重陣，精光耀日，賊益震懼。他日，公又與遂書，多所點竄，如遂改定者；超等愈疑遂。公乃與克日會戰，先以輕兵挑之，戰良乆，乃縱虎騎夾擊，大破之，斬成宜、李堪等。遂、超等走涼州，楊秋奔安定，關中平。諸將或問公曰：「初，賊守潼關，渭北道缺，不從河東擊馮翊而反守潼關，引日而後北渡，何也？」公曰：「賊守潼關，若吾入河東，賊必引守諸津，則西河未可渡，吾故盛兵向潼關；賊悉衆南守，西河之備虛，故二將得擅取西河；然後引軍北渡，賊不能與吾爭西河者，以有二將之軍也。連車樹柵，為甬道而南，臣松之案：漢高祖二年，與楚戰滎陽京、索之間，築甬道屬河以取敖倉粟。應劭曰：「恐敵鈔輜重，故築垣牆如街巷也。」今魏武不築垣牆，但連車樹柵以扞兩面。旣為不可勝，且以示弱。渡渭為堅壘，虜至不出，所以驕之也；故賊不為營壘而求割地。吾順言許之，所以從其意，使自安而不為備，因畜士卒之力，一旦擊之，所謂疾雷不及掩耳，兵之變化，固非一道也。」始，賊每一部到，公輒有喜色。賊破之後，諸將問其故。公荅曰：「關中長遠，若賊各依險阻，征之，不一二年不可定也。今皆來集，其衆雖多，莫相歸服，軍無適主，一舉可滅，為功差易，吾是以喜。」
At that time, the generals in Guanzhong suspected Zhong Yáo of intending to seize power for himself. Thus Ma Chao joined forces with Han Sui, Yang Qiu, Li Kan, Cheng Yi and others in rebellion. Cao Ren was dispatched to campaign against them. Ma Chao and others stationed themselves at Tongguan, so the ruler ordered his generals: "The troops from Guanxi are strong and fierce; hold fast to your defenses and do not engage in battle." In the seventh month of autumn, the ruler launched a western campaign. According to the Wei Shu: Many advisors argued, "The Guanxi troops are strong and skilled in using long spears; unless we select an elite vanguard force, we cannot confront them." The ruler said to his generals: "Victory depends on us, not on the enemy. Though they are skilled in using long spears, I will ensure that they cannot use them effectively. You all just watch." The ruler's forces and Ma Chao's troops set up camps on opposite sides of Tongguan. While the ruler urgently engaged in direct confrontation, he secretly dispatched Xu Huang and Zhu Ling to cross Pu Ban Jin at night and establish a camp on the western bank of the river. The ruler himself crossed north from Tongguan, but before he had fully crossed, Ma Chao rushed to attack his ships in an urgent battle. The captain Ding Fei released cattle and horses to lure the enemy. When the rebels became chaotic in their pursuit of the animals, the ruler was able to cross safely. According to Cao Man Zhuan: As the ruler prepared to cross the river, just as his vanguard had finished crossing, Ma Chao suddenly arrived. Yet the ruler remained seated on a Hu bed without rising. Zhang He and others, seeing the urgency of the situation, rushed to pull the ruler into the boat together. The river current was swift; they crossed northward and were carried downstream for several miles, when Ma Chao's cavalry pursued them, shooting arrows in heavy rain. The generals, seeing their forces defeated and not knowing the ruler's whereabouts, were filled with alarm and fear. When they finally saw him, they felt both sorrow and joy, some shedding tears. The ruler laughed heartily and said: "Today I was nearly trapped by these petty bandits!" Following the river, they constructed a corridor-like path to move southward. After the rebels withdrew, they took up a defensive position at Wei Kou. The ruler then deployed many decoy troops and secretly transported soldiers by boat into the Wei River to build a floating bridge. At night, he divided his forces to establish camps in Weinan. During the night, the rebels attacked the camp but were repelled by hidden troops and defeated. Ma Chao and others took up position in Weinan and sent envoys to request a truce, offering the western side of the Yellow River as a boundary. The ruler refused their proposal. In September, the army advanced across the Wei River. Cao Man Zhuan records: At that time, whenever the ruler's troops crossed the Wei River, they were constantly attacked by Ma Chao's cavalry, making it impossible to establish camps. The terrain was also sandy and unsuitable for building fortifications. Lou Zibo advised the ruler: "Now that it is cold, we can pile up sand to form a wall and pour water over it; this could be completed in one night." The ruler followed his advice and had many silk bags prepared to transport water. At night, troops crossed the river to build a wall; by dawn, it was completed. Thus, all of the ruler's forces successfully crossed the Wei River. Some may question that at this time in September, water should not yet have frozen. Min Songzhi notes in the Wei Shu: The ruler's army arrived at Tongguan by August and crossed north of the Yellow River during the intercalary month, which indicates that it was the intercalary eighth lunar month. By this time, could it have already become very cold? Ma Chao and others repeatedly challenged for battle, but were again refused; They persistently requested territorial concessions and the sending of a hostage. The ruler adopted Jia Xu's strategy, pretending to agree with their demands. Han Sui requested a meeting with the ruler. The ruler and Han Sui's father had been recommended as filial and upright officials in the same year, and they were also contemporaries of similar status. Thus, when they met on horseback for some time, they did not discuss military matters but instead spoke about old stories from the capital, clapping hands and laughing joyfully. After parting, Ma Chao asked Han Sui: "What did he say to you?" Han Sui replied: "He said nothing." Ma Chao and others became suspicious. The Wei Shu records: On the following day, the ruler met again with Han Sui and others. The generals said: "When the ruler converses with the enemy, he should not be too casual; wooden palisades could be prepared as a precaution." The ruler agreed to this suggestion. When the bandit generals saw the ruler, they all bowed from their horses. The Qin and Hu onlookers crowded in front and behind. The ruler smiled at the rebels and said: "Do you wish to see Cao Gong?" "I am also just a man, not possessing four eyes or two mouths; I merely have more wisdom!" The Hu people observed from front and back in great numbers. He also arranged five thousand armored cavalry into ten lines of formation, their gleaming armor shining under the sun; the rebels became even more frightened. On another day, the ruler wrote a letter to Han Sui again, making many corrections and deletions as if they had been revised by Han Sui himself; Ma Chao and others grew even more suspicious of Han Sui. The ruler then arranged a set date for battle. He first sent light troops to provoke the enemy, and after fighting for some time, he unleashed his elite cavalry in a pincer attack, decisively defeating them and beheading Cheng Yi, Li Kan, and others. Han Sui, Ma Chao, and the rest fled to Liangzhou; Yang Qiu ran away to Anding. The Guanzhong region was thus pacified. Some of the generals asked the ruler: "Initially, the rebels were defending Tongguan, and the route north of Wei River was vulnerable. Why did you not attack Fengyi from Hedong but instead chose to defend Tongguan first, delaying for several days before crossing northward? What was your reasoning?" The ruler said: "If the rebels were guarding Tongguan and we had entered Hedong, they would certainly have withdrawn to defend all the river crossings. In that case, it would not have been possible to cross the Xihed River. Therefore, I deliberately deployed a large force toward Tongguan; the rebels would have concentrated their entire forces to the south in defense, leaving the western river defenses weak. That is why my two generals were able to seize Xihed River unimpeded; only after that did I lead the army northward across the river. The rebels could not contest Xihed River with me because of my two generals' forces there. They linked carts and set up barriers to form a covered passage while advancing south. Minister Songzhi notes: In the second year of Emperor Gaozu's reign, during battles with Chu forces at Yingyang between Jing and Suo, he constructed a covered passage connecting to the river in order to transport grain from Aocang. Ying Shao said: "This was done out of fear that the enemy might raid our supply wagons, so walls were built like those in streets and alleys." Now, Wei Wu did not build walls but instead linked carts and erected barriers to defend both sides. This was done not only to make it impossible for the enemy to defeat us, but also to appear weak. Crossing the Wei River and building strong fortifications, yet refusing to come out when the rebels arrived—this was done to provoke their arrogance; thus, the rebels did not construct camps or fortifications but instead requested territorial concessions. I pretended to agree with their request, doing so in order to follow their wishes and make them feel secure while they neglected preparations. This allowed me to conserve the strength of my soldiers, enabling a sudden attack that was like a bolt of lightning—too fast for them to react. The changing nature of warfare is not confined to one single method." At first, whenever a rebel faction arrived, the ruler would show a look of joy on his face. After defeating the rebels, the generals asked him for an explanation. The ruler replied: "Guanzhong is vast and distant; if the rebels each take refuge in their strongholds, it would take no less than one or two years to pacify them. Now they have all gathered here; although their numbers are large, none of them submit to the others. Their army lacks a clear leader, so with one decisive strike we can annihilate them. Achieving victory will be relatively easy, and that is why I am happy."

武帝紀:
冬十月，軍自長安北征楊秋，圍安定。秋降，復其爵位，使留撫其民人。魏略曰：楊秋，黃初中遷討寇將軍，位特進，封臨涇侯，以壽終。十二月，自安定還，留夏侯淵屯長安。
In the tenth month of winter, the army departed from Chang'an to launch a northern campaign against Yang Qiu, surrounding Anding. Yang Qiu surrendered and was restored to his noble title; he was ordered to remain in the region to pacify and govern its people. The Wei Lue records: Yang Qiu was promoted to General Tiaoku, with the special rank of Tejin, and was granted the title Marquis of Linjing. He died a natural death. In the twelfth month, he returned from Anding and left Xiahou Yuan to garrison Chang'an.

武帝紀:
十七年春正月，公還鄴。天子命公贊拜不名，入朝不趨，劔履上殿，如蕭何故事。馬超餘衆梁興等屯藍田，使夏侯淵擊平之。割河內之蕩陰、朝歌、林慮，東郡之衞國、頓丘、東武陽、發干，鉅鹿之廮陶、曲周、南和，廣平之任城，趙之襄國、邯鄲、易陽以益魏郡。
In the first lunar month of spring in the seventeenth year, the ruler returned to Ye. The emperor ordered that when paying homage to him, officials should not mention his name in their greetings; he could enter the court without hurrying and was allowed to carry a sword and wear shoes on the imperial dais, following the precedent of Xiao He. The remnants of Ma Chao's forces, including Liang Xing, were garrisoned in Lantian; Xiahou Yuan was sent to attack and pacify them. Territories were carved out from Dangyan, Chao'ge, and Linlv in Hedong; Weiguo, Dunqiu, Dongwuyang, and Faguan in Dongjun; Yingtao, Quzhou, and Nanhe in Ju Lu; Rencheng in Guangping; Xiangguo, Handan, and Yiyang in Zhao—these were all added to Wei Jun.
