In the first lunar month of spring, he advanced his troops to Ruxukou and attacked Sun Quan's camp on the western bank of the Yangtze River, breaking through it and capturing Sun Quan's military commissioner Gongsun Yang. He then withdrew his army back. An imperial edict merged fourteen provinces into nine provinces again. In the fourth month of summer, he arrived at Ye.

武帝紀:
五月丙申，天子使御史大夫郗慮持節策命公為魏公續漢書曰：慮字鴻豫，山陽高平人。少受業於鄭玄，建安初為侍中。虞溥江表傳曰：獻帝甞特見慮及少府孔融，問融曰：「鴻豫何所優長？」融曰：「可與適道，未可與權。」慮舉笏曰：「融昔宰北海，政散民流，其權安在也！」遂與融互相長短，以至不睦。公以書和解之。慮從光祿勳遷為大夫。曰：
On the Bingshen day of the fifth month (May 28, 214 AD), the emperor sent Yu Shidafu Xi Lü with a staff to bestow an imperial decree appointing him as Duke of Wei. The Xushan Shu records: Xi Lü courtesy name Hongyu was a native of Gaoping, Shanyang. He studied under Zheng Xuan when he was young and in the early Jianshan period served as Shizhong (Attendant-in-Ordinary). Yu Pu's Jiangbiao Zhuan records: Emperor Xian once specially summoned Xi Lü and the Minister of Works Kong Rong, asking Kong Rong: "What are Hongyu's special strengths?" Kong Rong replied: "He can be trusted to follow the right path, but he cannot be entrusted with authority." Xi Lü raised his tablet and said: "In the past, Rong governed Donghai but failed to govern properly, causing administrative disorder and people fleeing. Where was his authority then?" Thus, they criticized each other's strengths and weaknesses until their relationship became strained. The ruler sent a letter to reconcile them. Xi Lü was promoted from the position of Guangluxun to Daifu (Minister of Justice). Said:

84

武帝紀:
朕以不德，少遭愍凶，越在西土，遷于唐、衞。當此之時，若綴旒然，公羊傳曰：「君若贅旒然。贅猶綴也。」何休云：「旒，旂旒也。以旒譬者，言為下所執持東西也。」宗廟乏祀，社稷無位；羣凶覬覦，分裂諸夏，率土之民，朕無獲焉，即我高祖之命將墜于地。朕用夙興假寐，震悼于厥心，曰「惟祖惟父，股肱先正，文侯之命曰：「亦惟先正。」鄭玄云：「先正，先臣。謂公卿大夫也。」其孰能恤朕躬」？乃誘天衷，誕育丞相，保乂我皇家，弘濟于艱難，朕實賴之。今將授君典禮，其敬聽朕命。
"I, unworthy as I am, suffered misfortune at an early age and was exiled to the western regions, moving between Tang and Wei." At that time, I was like a pendant hanging loosely. The Gongyang Zhuan says: "The ruler is like a tassel on a banner." "Zhu still means to hang or attach." He Xiu said: "Liu refers to the tassels of a banner. To use liu as an analogy is to say that it is something held and moved by those below." The ancestral temples lacked offerings, and the state had no ruler; wicked men plotted to seize power, and the various states of Zhuxia were divided. The people across the land had no one to turn to, and I was powerless—this meant that my high ancestor's mandate would fall to the ground. Therefore, I have risen early and feigned sleep, deeply grieving in my heart: "Only our ancestors and fathers, the loyal ministers of old, did the Mandate of Wen Hou say: 'Also only the loyal ministers of old.'" Zheng Xuan said: "Xianzheng refers to former ministers." That is, the dukes, grandees, and high officials." Who among them could care for me?" Thus, Heaven's will was guided to produce the Chancellor, who protected and assisted our royal house, aiding us through times of hardship—on whom I truly rely. Now I shall bestow upon you the official ceremony; listen attentively to my decree.

武帝紀:
昔者董卓初興國難，羣后釋位以謀王室，左氏傳曰：「諸侯釋位以間王政。」服虔曰：「言諸侯釋其私政而佐王室。」君則攝進，首啟戎行，此君之忠于本朝也。後及黃巾反易天常，侵我三州，延及平民，君又翦之，以寧東夏，此又君之功也。韓暹、楊奉專用威命，君則致討，克黜其難，遂遷許都，造我京畿，設官兆祀，不失舊物，天地鬼神於是獲乂，此又君之功也。袁術僭逆，肆於淮南，懾憚君靈，用丕顯謀，蘄陽之役，橋蕤授首，稜威南邁，術以隕潰，此又君之功也。迴戈東征，呂布就戮，乘轅將返，張楊殂斃，眭固伏罪，張繡稽服，此又君之功也。袁紹逆亂天常，謀危社稷，憑恃其衆，稱兵內侮，當此之時，王師寡弱，天下寒心，莫有固志，君執大節，精貫白日，奮其武怒，運其神策，致屆官渡，大殲醜類，詩曰：「致天之屆，于牧之野。」鄭玄云：「屆，極也。」鴻範曰：「鯀則殛死。」俾我國家拯於危墜，此又君之功也。濟師洪河，拓定四州，袁譚、高幹，咸梟其首，海盜奔迸，黑山順軌，此又君之功也。烏丸三種，崇亂二世，袁尚因之，逼據塞北，束馬縣車，一征而滅，此又君之功也。劉表背誕，不供貢職，王師首路，威風先逝，百城八郡，交臂屈膝，此又君之功也。馬超、成宜，同惡相濟，濵據河、潼，求逞所欲，殄之渭南，獻馘萬計，遂定邊境，撫和戎狄，此又君之功也。鮮卑、丁零，重譯而至，箄于、白屋，請吏率職，此又君之功也。君有定天下之功，重之以明德，班敘海內，宣美風俗，旁施勤教，恤慎刑獄，吏無苛政，民無懷慝；敦崇帝族，表繼絕世，舊德前功，罔不咸秩；雖伊尹格于皇天，周公光于四海，方之蔑如也。
In the past, when Dong Zhuo first stirred up national turmoil, many officials abandoned their posts to plan for the royal house. The Zuozhuan says: "The feudal lords left their positions in order to interfere with the king's administration." Fu Qian said: "This means that the feudal lords abandoned their private governance to assist the royal house." You assumed command and led the military campaign first—this is your loyalty to this dynasty. Later, when the Huangjin rebels overturned the natural order of Heaven and invaded our three states, spreading to common people, you again crushed them, bringing peace to eastern Zhuxia—this is another one of your achievements. Han Xian and Yang Feng monopolized authority, but you launched a campaign to punish them, overcame their rebellion, and thus moved the capital to Xu Du. You established our imperial capital, set up officials, initiated ancestral rites, and preserved what was traditional; as such, Heaven, Earth, and spirits were pacified—this is yet another one of your achievements. Yuan Shu acted in rebellion, spreading his defiance in Huainan. Fearing your power, he devised a grand plan; at the Battle of Qiyang, Qiao Rui was captured and executed. Your authority extended southward, and Yuan Shu collapsed—this is again one of your achievements. Turning westward to launch an eastern campaign, you executed Lu Bu. On your way back, Zhang Yang died; Sui Gu was captured and punished, and Zhang Xiu submitted—this is once again one of your achievements. Yuan Shao violated the natural order of Heaven, plotting to endanger the state. Relying on his large forces, he raised arms against us from within. At that time, our royal army was weak and few in number; people across the land were chilled with fear, none holding firm resolve. Yet you upheld great virtue, your loyalty piercing the sun itself. You unleashed martial fury and employed divine strategy, leading to the decisive battle at Guandu where we annihilated the enemy forces. The Shi says: "The heavens decreed this meeting on the plains of Mu." Zheng Xuan said: "Jue means extreme or culmination." Hongfan says: "Guan was executed for his crimes." Thus, you saved our nation from peril and collapse—this is again one of your great achievements. You crossed the great river with your army, expanded and pacified four states; Yuan Tan and Gao Gan were both executed. Pirates fled in disarray, and the Black Mountain rebels submitted to order—this is once more one of your achievements. The three tribes of Wuhuan had been in rebellion for two generations. Yuan Shang took advantage of this, seizing control north of the frontier. You led your forces with horses tethered and chariots suspended, launching a single campaign that destroyed them—this is again one of your merits. Liu Biao acted defiantly, refusing to fulfill his tribute duties. When the royal army advanced, your authority and prestige preceded you; a hundred cities and eight commanderies surrendered without resistance—this is once again one of Your achievements. Ma Chao and Cheng Yi conspired together in their wickedness, occupying the banks of the Wei and Tong rivers to pursue their ambitions. You annihilated them at Weinan, capturing countless enemy heads, thus securing our borders and pacifying the Rong and Di peoples—this is again one of Your great achievements. The Xianbei and Dingling, after multiple translations, arrived to pay homage; the Biayu and Baiwu requested officials be appointed to govern them—this is once again one of You achievements. You have the merit of stabilizing the world, and you further it with virtuous conduct. You arranged order throughout the land, promoted good customs, diligently taught the people, showed care in judicial matters, ensured officials did not impose harsh policies, and prevented the populace from harboring evil intentions; you honored the imperial clan, restored those whose lineages had been cut off, and ensured that past virtues and former achievements were all properly recognized; Even compared to Yi Yin who harmonized with Heaven or Duke of Zhou whose virtue shone across the four seas, they would seem insignificant in comparison.

武帝紀:
朕聞先王並建明德，胙之以土，分之以民，崇其寵章，備其禮物，所以藩衞王室，左右厥世也。其在周成，管、蔡不靜，懲難念功，乃使邵康公賜齊太公履，東至于海，西至于河，南至于穆陵，北至于無棣，五侯九伯，實得征之，世祚太師，以表東海；爰及襄王，亦有楚人不供王職，又命晉文登為侯伯，錫以二輅、虎賁、鈇鉞、秬鬯、弓矢，大啟南陽，世作盟主。故周室之不壞，繄二國是賴。今君稱丕顯德，明保朕躬，奉荅天命，導揚弘烈，緩爰九域，莫不率俾，盤庚曰：「綏爰有衆。」鄭玄曰：「爰，於也，安隱於其衆也。」君奭曰：「海隅出日，罔不率俾。」率，循也。俾，使也。四海之隅，日出所照，無不循度而可使也。功高于伊、周，而賞卑於齊、晉，朕甚恧焉。朕以眇眇之身，託于兆民之上，永思厥艱，若涉淵冰，非君攸濟，朕無任焉。今以兾州之河東、河內、魏郡、趙國、中山、常山、鉅鹿、安平、甘陵、平原凡十郡，封君為魏公。錫君玄土，苴以白茅；爰契爾龜，用建冢社。昔在周室，畢公、毛公入為卿佐，周、邵師保出為二伯，外內之任，君實宜之，其以丞相領兾州牧如故。又加君九錫，其敬聽朕命。
I have heard that in ancient times, wise kings established virtuous men as rulers of fiefs, granting them land and people, bestowing honors and ceremonial gifts. This was done to serve as a defense for the royal house and to support its rule through generations. In the time of King Cheng of Zhou, Guan and Cai were rebellious. To punish this disorder while remembering past meritorious service, Shao Kanggong was sent to bestow territory upon Tai Gong of Qi: eastward to the sea, westward to the Yellow River, southward to Muling, northward to Wudi. The five marquises and nine regional lords were actually subject to his authority. He was granted a hereditary title as Grand Tutor, marking him as the ruler of the East Sea region; Later, during the reign of King Xiang, there were also people from Chu who failed to fulfill their duties to the king. The king then appointed Duke Wen of Jin as a marquis and regional lord, bestowing upon him two ceremonial chariots, tiger-bearers, axes of authority,秬鬯 (a sacred wine), bows and arrows, greatly expanding his territory in Nanyang, where he became a hereditary leader of alliances. Thus, the Zhou dynasty's survival was due entirely to these two states. Now, you have demonstrated great virtue and clearly safeguarded my person. You have fulfilled Heaven's mandate, promoted noble achievements, and extended peace across the nine regions; none fail to follow your lead. Pangeng said: "Bring peace to all the people." Zheng Xuan says: "Yuan means 'yu,' meaning to bring peace and security to your people." Junshi said: "The sun rises over the sea's edge, and none fail to follow its light." "Shuai" means to follow or abide by. "Bǐ" means "to make" or "to cause." The corners of the four seas, wherever the rising sun shines, nothing fails to follow order and be guided. Your achievements surpass those of Yi Yin and the Duke of Zhou, yet your rewards are less than those given to Qi and Jin; this makes me deeply ashamed. I, with my humble self, have been entrusted to rule over the myriad people. I constantly reflect on the difficulties ahead, as if treading thin ice over a deep abyss; without your support and guidance, I am unable to bear this responsibility. Now, I bestow upon you the title of Duke of Wei, granting you ten commanderies: Hedong, Henan, Weiqu, Zhao Guo, Zhongshan, Changshan, Julu, Anping, Ganling, and Pingyuan in Ji Zhou. I bestow upon you black soil as a symbol of the land, placed on white reeds to mark its sacredness; We shall carve an oath into your oracle turtle shell, thereby establishing your ancestral shrine and earth god altar. In ancient Zhou times, Bi Gong and Mao Gong served as high ministers within the court, while Duke Zhou and Shao Gong, as regents, were appointed as regional lords outside. The responsibilities of both internal governance and external administration are truly suited to you; therefore, you shall continue serving as Chancellor and Administrator of Ji Zhou as before. Furthermore, I bestow upon you nine additional honors; please listen respectfully to my decree.

武帝紀:
以君經緯禮律，為民軌儀，使安職業，無或遷志，是用錫君大輅、戎輅各一，玄牡二駟。君勸分務本，穡人昏作，盤庚曰：「墮農自安，不昏作勞。」鄭玄云：「昏，勉也。」粟帛滯積，大業惟興，是用錫君衮冕之服，赤舄副焉。君敦尚謙讓，俾民興行，少長有禮，上下咸和，是用錫君軒縣之樂，六佾之舞。君翼宣風化，爰發四方，遠人革面，華夏充實，是用錫君朱戶以居。君研其明哲，思帝所難，官才任賢，羣善必舉，是用錫君納陛以登。君秉國之鈞，正色處中，纖豪之惡，靡不抑退，是用錫君虎賁之士三百人。君糾虔天刑，章厥有罪，「糾虔天刑」語出國語，韋昭注曰：「糾，察也。虔，敬也。刑，法也。」犯關干紀，莫不誅殛，是用錫君鈇鉞各一。君龍驤虎視，旁眺八維，掩討逆節，折衝四海，是用錫君彤弓一，彤矢百，玈弓十，玈矢千。君以溫恭為基，孝友為德，明允篤誠，感于朕思，是用錫君秬鬯一卣，珪瓚副焉。魏國置丞相已下羣卿百寮，皆如漢初諸侯王之制。往欽哉，敬服朕命！簡恤爾衆，時亮庶功，用終爾顯德，對揚我高祖之休命！後漢尚書左丞潘勗之辭也。勗字元茂，陳留中牟人。魏書載公令曰：「夫受九錫，廣開土宇，周公其人也。漢之異姓八王者，與高祖俱起布衣，刱定王業，其功至大，吾何可比之？」前後三讓。於是中軍師王凌、謝亭侯荀攸、前軍師東武亭侯鍾繇、左軍師涼茂、右軍師毛玠、平虜將軍華鄉侯劉勳、建武將軍清苑亭侯劉若、伏波將軍高安侯夏侯惇、揚武將軍都亭侯王忠、奮威將軍樂鄉侯劉展、建忠將軍昌鄉亭侯鮮于輔、奮武將軍安國亭侯程昱、太中大夫都鄉侯賈詡、軍師祭酒千秋亭侯董昭、都亭侯薛洪、南鄉亭侯董蒙、關內侯王粲、傅巽、祭酒王選、袁奐、王朗、張承、任藩、杜襲、中護軍國明亭侯曹洪、中領軍萬歲亭侯韓浩、行驍騎將軍安平亭侯曹仁、領護軍將軍王圖、長史萬潛、謝奐、袁霸等勸進曰：「自古三代，胙臣以土，受命中興，封秩輔佐，皆所以襃功賞德，為國藩衞也。徃者天下崩亂，羣凶豪起，顛越跋扈之險，不可忍言。明公奮身出命以徇其難，誅二袁篡盜之逆，滅黃巾賊亂之類，殄夷首逆，芟撥荒穢，沐浴霜露二十餘年，書契已來，未有若此功者。昔周公承文、武之迹，受已成之業，高枕墨筆，拱揖羣后，商、奄之勤，不過二年，呂望因三分有二之形，據八百諸侯之勢，暫把旄鉞，一時指麾，然皆大啟土宇，跨州兼國。周公八子，並為侯伯，白牡騂剛，郊祀天地，典策備物，擬則王室，榮章寵盛如此之弘也。逮至漢興，佐命之臣，張耳、吳芮，其功至薄，亦連城開地，南面稱孤。此皆明君達主行之於上，賢臣聖宰受之於下，三代令典，漢帝明制。今比勞則周、呂逸，計功則張、吳微，論制則齊、魯重，言地則長沙多；然則魏國之封，九錫之榮，況於舊賞，猶懷玉而被褐也。且列侯諸將，幸攀龍驥，得竊微勞，佩紫懷黃，蓋以百數，亦將因此傳之萬世，而明公獨辭賞於上，將使其下懷不自安，上違聖朝歡心，下失冠帶至望，忘輔弼之大業，信匹夫之細行，攸等所大懼也。」於是公勑外為章，但受魏郡。攸等復曰：「伏見魏國初封，聖朝發慮，稽謀羣寮，然後策命；而明公乆違上指，不即大禮。今旣虔奉詔命，副順衆望，又欲辭多當少，讓九受一，是猶漢朝之賞不行，而攸等之請未許也。昔齊、魯之封，奄有東海，疆域井賦，四百萬家，基隆業廣，易以立功，故能成翼戴之勳，立一匡之績。今魏國雖有十郡之名，猶減於曲阜，計其戶數，不能參半，以藩衞王室，立垣樹屏，猶未足也。且聖上覽亡秦無輔之禍，懲曩日震蕩之艱，託建忠賢，廢墜是為，願明公恭承帝命，無或拒違。」公乃受命。魏略載公上書謝曰：「臣蒙先帝厚恩，致位郎署，受性疲怠，意望畢足，非敢希望高位，庶幾顯達。會董卓作亂，義當死難，故敢奮身出命，摧鋒率衆，遂值千載之運，奉役目下。當二袁炎沸侵侮之際，陛下與臣寒心同憂，顧瞻京師，進受猛敵，常恐君臣俱陷虎口，誠不自意能全首領。賴祖宗靈祐，醜類夷滅，得使微臣竊名其間。陛下加恩，授以上相，封爵寵祿，豐大弘厚，生平之願，實不望也。口與心計，幸且待罪，保持列侯，遺付子孫，自託聖世，永無憂責。不意陛下乃發盛意，開國備錫，以貺愚臣，地比齊、魯，禮同藩王，非臣無功所宜膺據。歸情上聞，不蒙聽許，嚴詔切至，誠使臣心俯仰偪迫。伏自惟省，列在大臣，命制王室，身非己有，豈敢自私，遂其愚意，亦將黜退，令就初服。今奉疆土，備數藩翰，非敢遠期，慮有後世；至於父子相誓終身，灰軀盡命，報塞厚恩。天威在顏，悚懼受詔。」
For having you establish and regulate rites and laws, serving as a model for the people, enabling them to maintain their occupations without wavering in purpose, I now bestow upon you one ceremonial chariot and one military chariot, each drawn by two teams of four black stallions. You encourage the people to focus on their duties and cultivate the land, making farmers rise early to work. Pangeng said: "Those who neglect farming for comfort do not labor diligently from dawn." Zheng Xuan says: "Hun means 'to encourage' or 'to urge on.'" Grain and silk have accumulated, great undertakings are flourishing; therefore, I bestow upon you ceremonial robes and headdresses of the highest rank, with red court shoes as a complement. You have earnestly promoted humility and courtesy, encouraging the people to follow proper conduct. The young respect the old, etiquette is observed among all, and harmony prevails between superiors and inferiors; therefore, I bestow on you the music of Xuan Xian and a dance formation of six rows. You have diligently promoted moral influence, spreading it to all directions; distant peoples have changed their ways, and the lands of China are now flourishing. Therefore, I bestow upon you a residence with vermilion doors as a mark of honor. You have cultivated wisdom and considered the emperor's difficulties, appointing capable officials and virtuous men, ensuring that all good deeds are recognized; therefore, I bestow a raised step for you to ascend with honor. You hold the balance of state power, maintaining a dignified and impartial stance; even the slightest evil is suppressed and driven back. Therefore, I bestow three hundred elite warriors upon you as an honor. "Correcting and enforcing the heavenly laws," this phrase comes from Guo Yu. Wei Zhao annotated: "Jiu means to investigate." Qian means reverence or respect. "Xing means law." Those who violate laws and disrupt order are all punished without exception; therefore, I bestow one axe of authority (fu) and one great 钺 (yue) upon you. You rise like a dragon and gaze like a tiger, surveying the eight directions. You suppress rebellion and quell disturbances across the four seas; therefore, I bestow you one red bow, one hundred red arrows, ten black bows, and one thousand black arrows. You have taken gentleness and humility as your foundation, filial piety and kindness toward friends as virtues; you are wise, trustworthy, and sincere, deeply moving my thoughts. Therefore, I bestow on you one yóu of the sacred 秬鬯 wine, with a jade 瓒 to accompany it. The State of Wei shall establish chancellors and all ranks of officials below them, following the system of the early Han dynasty's feudal kings. Go forth with reverence! Diligently obey my decree! Be kind and compassionate to your people, diligently accomplish all tasks, so that you may complete your noble virtue, and thus honor and uphold the glorious mandate of my ancestors! These were the words spoken by Pan Xu, Left Chancellor of the Later Han. Pan Xu's courtesy name was Yuanmao; he was a native of Zhongmou, Chenliu. The Records of the Wei dynasty record an imperial decree stating: "To receive nine honors and greatly expand one's territory is what Duke Zhou accomplished. "The eight non-royal kings of the Han dynasty rose from commoners alongside the Gaozu, establishing the imperial cause; their achievements were immense. How can I possibly compare to them?" He declined the honor three times, both before and after. At this time, Zhongjunshi Wang Ling, Xieting Hou Xun You, Qianjunshi Dongwu Tinghou Zhong Yao, Zuojunshi Liang Mao, Youjunshi Mao Jie, Pinglu Jiangjun Huaxiang Hou Liu Xun, Jianwu Jiangjun Qingyuan Tinghou Liu Ruo, Fubo Jiangjun Ga' an Hou Xiahou Dun, Yangwu Jiangjun Duting Hou Wang Zhong, Fenwei Jiangjun Lexiang Hou Liu Zhan, Jianzhong Jiangjun Changxiang Tinghou Xianyu Fu, Fenwu Jiangjun Anguo Tinghou Cheng Yu, Taizhong Daifu Duxiang Hou Jia Xu, Junshi Jisui Qianqiu Tinghou Dong Zhao, Duting Hou Xue Hong, Nanxiang Tinghou Dong Meng, Guannei Hou Wang Can, Fu Xun, Jisui Wang Xuan, Yuan Huan, Wang Lang, Zhang Cheng, Ren Fan, Du Xi, Zhonghujun Guoming Tinghou Cao Hong, Zhonglingjun Wansui Tinghou Han Hao, Xing Xiaoqi Jiangjun Anping Tinghou Cao Ren, Linghu Junjiangjun Wang Tu, Changshi Wan Qian, Xie Huan, Yuan Ba and others urged him to accept the title, saying: "Since ancient times in the Three Dynasties, ministers of merit were granted fiefs. Those who received Heaven's mandate and restored dynastic order were enfeoffed with ranks and positions as assistants; all these were done to honor virtue and reward achievement, serving as defenders for the state." In the past, when the world fell into chaos and numerous villains rose in power, the dangers of upheaval and tyranny were unbearable to speak of. Your illustrious virtue risked life and limb to relieve the crisis, punishing the rebellious usurpers of the two Yans, exterminating the Yellow Turban bandits, eliminating the leaders of rebellion, clearing away corruption and disorder. For over twenty years you have endured frost and dew; since records began, there has been no achievement like yours. In ancient times, the Duke of Zhou inherited the legacy of King Wen and King Wu, receiving an already established cause. He rested with ease, merely holding a brush in hand, bowing to feudal lords. His efforts against Shang and Yan lasted no more than two years. Jiang Taigong, taking advantage of a situation where two out of three regions were under his control, held the authority over eight hundred feudal lords for only a short time, yet still greatly expanded territory, spanning states and annexing lands. The Duke of Zhou had eight sons, all enfeoffed as marquises and regional lords. White stallions and red oxen were sacrificed in the suburbs to worship Heaven and Earth; rituals and records were complete with ceremonial objects, following the model of the royal court. The honors and distinctions bestowed upon him were thus grand indeed. When the Han dynasty arose, those who assisted in its founding—Zhang Er and Wu Rui—had relatively minor achievements; yet they were still granted cities and territories, ruling as sovereigns facing south. These were all carried out by enlightened rulers above and accepted by virtuous ministers below; they are the exemplary institutions of the Three Dynasties and the clear regulations of the Han emperors. Now, in terms of labor and effort, you surpass Zhou Gong and Jiang Taigong; in terms of merit, you exceed Zhang Er and Wu Rui; in terms of system and status, you rival Qi and Lu; in terms of territory, you outmatch Changsha. Yet the fiefdom of Wei and the honor of nine grants are still less than past rewards, like holding a jade in one's hand while wrapped in coarse cloth. Moreover, the marquises and generals have been fortunate to ride on your success, earning minor merits and wearing purple and yellow insignias—there are hundreds of them. They will pass these honors down through generations; yet you alone refuse rewards from above. This will make those below feel uneasy, offending the joy of the holy court above and disappointing the great expectations of officials and scholars below. It is a betrayal of your duty as an assistant to the throne and a misplaced emphasis on the conduct of an ordinary man—this is what we greatly fear." Thus, he ordered that only the commandery of Wei be accepted, declining all other honors. Xun You and others replied: "We have observed that when the State of Wei was first enfeoffed, the holy court deliberated carefully, consulting with all officials before issuing the decree; yet you have long disregarded the emperor's will and delayed accepting this great honor. Now that you have respectfully accepted the imperial decree and fulfilled public expectations, yet still wish to reject much and accept little, declining nine honors for just one, this is as if the Han dynasty's rewards were not carried out, and our request remains unapproved. In the past, the fiefs of Qi and Lu controlled the East Sea, with vast territories and four million households. With such a strong foundation and broad domain, it was easy to accomplish great achievements; thus they were able to establish meritorious service in supporting the throne and achieve the feat of uniting the realm. Now, although the State of Wei is named with ten commanderies, its territory is still less than that of Qufu. Calculating the number of households, it cannot even reach half; as a fief to defend the royal house and establish walls and barriers, this remains insufficient. Moreover, the emperor has reflected on the calamity of Qin's downfall due to lack of support and learned from past hardships. He now entrusts loyal and virtuous men with positions to prevent such decline. We hope you will respectfully accept the imperial decree without refusal or defiance." He then accepted the decree. The Wei Lue records that he submitted a memorial in gratitude, saying: "I have received the great grace of the late emperor and was elevated to an official post. By nature I am weary and sluggish; my aspirations were always modest, never daring to hope for high rank or distinction. When Dong Zhuo stirred up rebellion, it was my duty to die for righteousness; thus I dared to risk life and limb, leading troops into battle. Fortuitously, I encountered a once-in-a-millennium opportunity and now serve under your command. During the time when the two Yans raged and violated, Your Majesty and I shared deep concern. Looking toward the capital, we advanced against fierce enemies, always fearing that both ruler and subject would fall into a tiger's jaws. Indeed, I never expected to survive with my head intact. Thanks to the blessings of our ancestors, these wicked foes were exterminated, allowing a humble servant like me to secretly gain recognition among them. Your Majesty has shown grace, appointing me as a high minister and bestowing noble titles and generous rewards. The honors are abundant and profound—such wishes were never part of my life's expectations. With mouth and mind in agreement, I am fortunate to serve while bearing the burden of office. To maintain my marquis title and pass it on to future generations is a trust placed upon me by this holy age; thus, I shall forever be free from worries or burdens. I did not expect Your Majesty to show such great favor, establishing a state and bestowing all honors upon me as a reward for my humble service. The territory rivals that of Qi and Lu, the rites are equal to those of vassal kings—this is not something I, without merit, deserve or should hold. Returning my feelings to the throne for consideration, Your Majesty did not grant approval. The strict decree is urgent and heartfelt, truly making me feel constrained and pressured in my heart. Reflecting upon myself, I am among the high ministers; my life and position belong to the royal house. How dare I act selfishly or follow my own foolish desires? Rather, I should be demoted and return to a humble post. Now, receiving territory as part of the royal defense, I do not dare hope for distant future generations; my concern is only for what may come after me. As for myself and my descendants vowing to serve our entire lives, sacrificing body and soul to repay this great kindness— With the majesty of Heaven upon us, I am filled with awe and fear as I accept the decree."

武帝紀:
秋七月，始建魏社稷宗廟。天子娉公三女為貴人，少者待年於國。獻帝起居注曰：使使持節行太常大司農安陽亭侯王邑，齎璧、帛、玄纁、絹五萬匹之鄴納娉，介者五人，皆以議郎行大夫事，副介一人。九月，作金虎臺，鑿渠引漳水入白溝以通河。冬十月，分魏郡為東西部，置都尉。十一月，初置尚書、侍中、六卿。魏氏春秋曰：以荀攸為尚書令，涼茂為僕射，毛玠、崔琰、常林、徐奕、何夔為尚書，王粲、杜襲、衞覬、和洽為侍中。
In autumn, the seventh month, the ancestral temples and state altars of Wei were first established. The emperor betrothed three daughters of the Duke to be concubines, with the youngest awaiting her turn in the state. The Annals of Emperor Xian's Daily Life records: The emperor sent an envoy, Wang Yi, who held the titles of Taichang, Dasi Nong, and Anyang Tinghou. He carried jade, silk, black and red ceremonial cloth, and five thousand bolts of fine silk to Ye as a marriage offering. Five attendants accompanied him, all serving as Yilang acting as 大夫 (ministers), with one assistant attendant. In the ninth month, the Jinhu Terrace was built; a canal was dug to divert Zhang River water into Baigou to connect with the Yellow River. In winter, the tenth month, Wei Qu was divided into eastern and western sections, each administered by a Duwei (military commissioner). In the eleventh month, the offices of Shangshu, Shizhong, and the Six Senior Ministers were first established. The Spring and Autumn Annals of Wei records: Xun You was appointed as Shangshu Ling (Minister of the Secretariat), Liang Mao as Puye, Mao Jie, Cui Yan, Chang Lin, Xu Yi, He Kui as Shushu (Secretaries), Wang Can, Du Xi, Wei Ji, and He Qia as Shizhong (Attendants in Attendance).

馬超在漢陽，復因羌、胡為害，氐王千萬叛應超，屯興國。使夏侯淵討之。
Ma Chao was at Hanyang and once again incited the Qiang and Hu peoples to cause harm. Di Wang Qianwan rebelled in support of Ma Chao, establishing a garrison at Xingguo. Xiahou Yuan was sent to campaign against them.

武帝紀:
十九年春正月，始耕籍田。南安趙衢、漢陽尹奉等討超，梟其妻子，超奔漢中。韓遂徙金城，入氐王千萬部，率羌、胡萬餘騎與夏侯淵戰，擊，大破之，遂走西平。淵與諸將攻興國，屠之。省安東、永陽郡。
In the first month of spring, the nineteenth year, the imperial plowing ceremony for the sacrificial fields began. Zhao Qu from Nan'an and Yin Feng from Hanyang attacked Ma Chao, beheading his wife and children. Ma Chao fled to Hanzhong. Han Sui moved to Jincheng and joined the Di Wang Qianwan, leading over ten thousand cavalry of Qiang and Hu tribes to fight Xiahou Yuan. Xiahou Yuan attacked and decisively defeated them; Han Sui fled westward to Xiping. Xiahou Yuan, along with his generals, attacked Xingguo and sacked it. The commanderies of Andong and Yongyang were abolished.

武帝紀:
安定太守毌丘興將之官，公戒之曰：「羌，胡欲與中國通，自當遣人來，慎勿遣人徃。善人難得，必將教羌、胡妄有所請求，因欲以自利；不從便為失異俗意，從之則無益事。」興至，遣校尉范陵至羌中，陵果教羌，使自請為屬國都尉。公曰：「吾預知當爾，非聖也，但更事多耳。」獻帝起居注曰：使行太常事大司農安陽亭侯王邑與宗正劉艾，皆持節，介者五人，齎束帛駟馬，及給事黃門侍郎、掖庭丞、中常侍二人，迎二貴人于魏公國。二月癸亥，又於魏公宗廟授二貴人印綬。甲子，詣魏公宮延秋門，迎貴人升車。魏遣郎中令、少府、博士、御府乘黃廄令、丞相掾屬侍送貴人。癸酉，二貴人至洧倉中，遣侍中丹將宂從虎賁前後駱驛往迎之。乙亥，二貴人入宮，御史大夫、中二千石將大夫、議郎會殿中，魏國二卿及侍中、中郎二人，與漢公卿並升殿宴。
When Guanqiu Xing, the new Taihou of Pingding, was about to assume his post, the Duke warned him: "If Qiang and Hu people wish to communicate with China, they will send envoys themselves. Be cautious not to send anyone to them." Virtuous people are hard to find; they will surely teach the Qiang and Hu to make unreasonable requests, seeking personal gain thereby; if you refuse them, it would be seen as violating their customs; if you comply, there will be no benefit." When Guanqiu Xing arrived in office, he sent a Jiao Wei named Fan Ling to the Qiang. As expected, Fan Ling instructed the Qiang people to request that they be granted the title of Zhugu Guwei (commander of an affiliated territory). The Duke said: "I foresaw this would happen, not because I am wise, but simply because I have more experience." The Annals of Emperor Xian's Daily Life records: The emperor dispatched Wang Yi, acting as Taichang and holding the title Dasi Nong and Anyang Tinghou, along with Liu Ai from Zongzheng. Both were granted imperial seals; five attendants accompanied them, carrying bolts of silk and four horses. Additionally, two officials—Ge Shi Huangmen Shilang (Attendant in Attendance), Yeting Cheng (Chamberlain of the Palace), and Zhongchangshi (Imperial Eunuch)—were sent to welcome the two concubines from the Duke of Wei's state. On the Guihai day of the second month, seals and sashes were again bestowed upon the two concubines at the Duke of Wei's ancestral temple. On the Jiashi day, they arrived at the Yanyou Gate of the Duke of Wei's palace to escort the concubines into their carriages. Wei dispatched Langzhongling, Shaofu, Bohu, Yufu Chenghuangjiuling, and Chanying Shushu to serve as attendants accompanying the concubines. On the Guiyou day, the two concubines arrived at Weicang Zhong. The emperor dispatched Shizhong Dan to lead a retinue of elite warriors and camel caravans stationed along the way to meet them. On the Yihai day, the two concubines entered the palace. The Grand Censor, officials of Zhong Erqianshi rank, senior ministers, and Yilang gathered in the Hall of Audience. Two senior ministers from Wei's court, along with two Shizhong and Zhonglang officers, joined Han dynasty ministers on the dais for a banquet.

三月，天子使魏公位在諸侯王上，改授金璽，赤紱、遠遊冠。獻帝起居注曰：使左中郎將楊宣、亭侯裴茂持節、印授之。
In March, the emperor elevated the Duke of Wei to a rank above feudal kings and bestowed upon him a golden seal, red sash, and Yuanyou Crown. The Annals of Emperor Xian records: The emperor dispatched Zuo Zhonglang Jiang Yang Xuan and Tinghou Pei Mao, both holding imperial seals and official seals, to bestow the honors.

武帝紀:
秋七月，公征孫權。九州春秋曰：參軍傅幹諫曰：「治天下之大具有二，文與武也；用武則先威，用文則先德，威德足以相濟，而後王道備矣。往者天下大亂，上下失序，明公用武攘之，十平其九。今未承王命者，吳與蜀也，吳有長江之險，蜀有崇山之阻，難以威服，易以德懷。愚以為可且按甲寢兵，息軍養士，分土定封，論功行賞，若此則內外之心固，有功者勸，而天下知制矣。然後漸興學校，以導其善性而長其義節。公神武震於四海，若修文以濟之，則普天之下，無思不服矣。今舉十萬之衆，頓之長江之濵，若賊負固深藏，則士馬不能逞其能，奇變無所用其權，則大威有屈而敵心未能服矣。唯明公思虞舜舞干戚之義，全威養德，以道制勝。」公不從，軍遂無功。幹字彥材，北地人，終於丞相倉曹屬。有子曰玄。
In autumn, the seventh month of this year, the Duke launched a campaign against Sun Quan. The Spring and Autumn Annals records: The military advisor Fu Gan advised, "There are two essential elements to governing the world: literature and martial prowess; When employing military might, one must first establish authority; when using civil governance, one must first cultivate virtue. When both authority and virtue are sufficient to complement each other, then the Way of Kingship is complete. In the past, when chaos reigned across the world and order between superiors and inferiors was lost, Your Lordship used military force to quell it, pacifying nine out of ten regions. Now, those who have yet to accept the king's mandate are Wu and Shu. Wu is protected by the perilous Yangtze River, while Shu is shielded by towering mountains; these regions are difficult to subdue through force but can be easily won over through virtue. I humbly suggest that we should temporarily cease military campaigns, rest the troops and cultivate our soldiers, divide territories for fiefdoms, discuss rewards according to merit. If this is done, then both internal and external loyalties will be strengthened; those who have rendered service will be encouraged, and all under heaven will recognize the system of governance. Only then can we gradually establish schools to guide their virtuous nature and cultivate righteousness and integrity among them. Your Lordship's martial might has already reverberated across the four seas; if now you cultivate civil virtue to complement it, then all under heaven will have no choice but to submit. Now, mustering an army of one hundred thousand and stationing it by the banks of the Yangtze River—if the enemy retreats into fortified positions deep within their territory—then our soldiers and horses will be unable to demonstrate their strength, and our strategies for surprise and change will have no opportunity to employ their advantages. In this case, great authority may suffer setbacks, and the enemy's heart will not yet be subdued. May Your Lordship reflect upon the meaning of Emperor Shun wielding shields and axes in dance, preserving authority while cultivating virtue, and achieve victory through the Way." The Duke did not follow this advice, and as a result, the campaign achieved no success. Fu Gan, courtesy name Yancai, was a native of Beidi; he eventually served as an officer in the Cangcao Department under the Prime Minister. He had a son named Xuan.

武帝紀:
初，隴西宋建自稱河首平漢王，聚衆枹罕，改元，置百官，三十餘年。遣夏侯淵自興國討之。冬十月，屠枹罕，斬建，涼州平。
Initially, Song Jian of Longxi proclaimed himself King Pinghan of Heshou, gathered a following in Fuhang, established a new era name, and appointed officials, maintaining this for over thirty years. Xiahou Yuan was dispatched from Xingguo to campaign against him. In winter, the tenth month, Fuhang was sacked, Song Jian was beheaded, and Liangzhou was pacified.

公自合肥還。
The Duke returned from Hefei.

Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
十一月，漢皇后伏氏坐昔與父故屯騎校尉完書，云帝以董承被誅怨恨公，辭甚醜惡，發聞，后廢黜死，兄弟皆伏法。曹瞞傳曰：公遣華歆勒兵入宮收后，后閉戶匿壁中。歆壞戶發壁，牽后出。帝時與御史大夫郗慮坐，后被髮徒跣過，執帝手曰：「不能復相活邪？」帝曰：「我亦不自知命在何時也。」帝謂慮曰：「郗公，天下寧有是乎！」遂將后殺之，完及宗族死者數百人。
In the eleventh month, Empress Fu of the Han dynasty was implicated for having previously written to her father, the former Tunnan General Wan, stating that the emperor resented and hated the Duke due to Dong Cheng's execution. The contents were extremely derogatory; when this became known, the empress was deposed, disgraced, and died, while her brothers were all executed according to law. The Records of Cao Man state: The Duke dispatched Hua Xin, leading troops into the palace to arrest the empress. The empress shut herself in a room and hid within a wall cavity. Xin broke down the door and pried open the wall, dragging the empress out. At that time, the emperor was seated with Grand Censor Xi Lü; as the empress passed by in disheveled hair and barefoot, she took the emperor's hand and said, "Could you not save me anymore?" The emperor replied, "I myself do not know when my life will end." The emperor said to Lü, "Master Xi, can there be such a thing in the world!" They then executed the empress; Wan and hundreds of members of his clan were also put to death.

Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
十二月，公至孟津。天子命公置旄頭，宮殿設鍾虡。乙未，令曰：「夫有行之士未必能進取，進取之士未必能有行也。陳平豈篤行，蘇秦豈守信邪？而陳平定漢業，蘇秦濟弱燕。由此言之，士有偏短，庸可廢乎！有司明思此義，則士無遺滯，官無廢業矣。」又曰：「夫刑，百姓之命也，而軍中典獄者或非其人，而任以三軍死生之事，吾甚懼之。其選明達法理者，使持典刑。」於是置理曹掾屬。
In December, the Duke arrived at Mengjin. The emperor ordered the Duke to set up a banner and have bells installed in his palace halls. On the Yiwei day, an edict was issued: "A man of virtue may not necessarily be capable of advancement and achievement; a man who seeks advancement and success may not necessarily possess virtue. Was Chen Ping truly virtuous? Was Su Qin really trustworthy?" Yet it was Chen Ping who secured the Han dynasty's cause, and Su Qin who rescued the weak state of Yan. From this we can see that a scholar may have certain shortcomings—should he therefore be discarded? If those in charge clearly reflect on this meaning, then no capable person will remain overlooked and no official post will lack its duties fulfilled." He also said: "Punishment is the life of the common people, yet in the army, those responsible for judicial affairs are sometimes unqualified individuals entrusted with matters concerning the life and death of the entire military force. I am greatly concerned about this. Therefore, select those who are wise and well-versed in legal principles to oversee judicial matters." Thus, the office of Licao Yushu was established.

二十年春正月，天子立公中女為皇后。省雲中、定襄、五原、朔方郡，郡置一縣領其民，合以為新興郡。
In spring, the first month of the twentieth year, the emperor enfeoffed the Duke's second daughter as empress. The commanderies of Yunzhong, Dingxiang, Wuyuan, and Shuofang were abolished; one county was established in each to administer the local population, collectively forming a new Xinxing Commandery.

99
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
三月，公西征張魯，至陳倉，將自武都入氐；氐人塞道，先遣張郃、朱靈等攻破之。夏四月，公自陳倉以出散關，至河池。氐王竇茂衆萬餘人，恃險不服，五月，公攻屠之。西平、金城諸將麴演、蔣石等共斬送韓遂首。典略曰：遂字文約，始與同郡邊章俱著名西州。章為督軍從事。遂奉計詣京師，何進宿聞其名，特與相見，遂說進使誅諸閹人，進不從，乃求歸。會涼州宋揚、北宮玉等反，舉章、遂為主，章尋病卒，遂為揚等所劫，不得已，遂阻兵為亂，積三十二年，至是乃死，年七十餘矣。劉艾靈帝紀曰：章，一名元。秋七月，公至陽平。張魯使弟衞與將楊昂等據陽平關，橫山築城十餘里，攻之不能拔，乃引軍還。賊見大軍退，其守備解散。公乃密遣解𢢼、高祚等乘險夜襲，大破之，斬其將楊任，進攻衞，衞等夜遁，魯潰奔巴中。公軍入南鄭，盡得魯府庫珍寶。魏書曰：軍自武都山行千里，升降險阻，軍人勞苦；公於是大饗，莫不忘其勞。巴、漢皆降。復漢寧郡為漢中；分漢中之安陽、西城為西城郡，置太守；分錫、上庸郡，置都尉。
In March of this year, the Duke marched westward to campaign against Zhang Lu and arrived at Chen Cang, intending to enter through Wudu into the Di region; The Di people blocked the roads. The Duke first dispatched Zhang He, Zhu Ling and others to attack and break through their defenses. In summer, the fourth month, the Duke departed from Chen Cang via the Sanguan Pass and arrived at Hechi. Di King Dou Mao commanded over ten thousand men, relying on his advantageous terrain to resist submission. In the fifth month, the Duke attacked and sacked their forces. The generals Qu Yan, Jiang Shi of Xiping and Jincheng jointly beheaded Han Sui and sent his head to the Duke. The Dianlue records: Han Sui, courtesy name Wenyue, initially became famous in Xizhou together with Bian Zhang of his native commandery. Zhang served as a military supervisor and officer. Sui presented his reports to the capital. He Jin had long heard of Sui's reputation and specially met with him; Sui advised He Jin to eliminate the eunuchs, but He Jin did not follow this suggestion, so Sui requested permission to return home. At that time, Song Yang and Beigong Yu of Liangzhou rebelled, elevating Zhang and Sui as their leaders. Soon after, Zhang died from illness; Sui was then seized by Yang and others, unwillingly taking up arms in rebellion. For thirty-two years he resisted, until now, when he finally perished at over seventy years old. The Records of Emperor Ling by Liu Ai states: Zhang, another name Yuan. In autumn, the seventh month, the Duke arrived at Yangping. Zhang Lu dispatched his younger brother Wei and general Yang Ang to occupy the Yangping Pass, where they built a wall across the mountain for over ten li. The Duke's forces could not capture it, so he withdrew his troops. The rebels saw that the main army had retreated and consequently dispersed their defenses. The Duke then secretly dispatched Jie Xian and Gao Zuo to launch a surprise night attack from the perilous terrain, achieving a decisive victory. Their general Yang Ren was beheaded. Advancing on Wei, Wei and others fled under cover of darkness; Zhang Lu's forces collapsed as he fled toward Bazhong. The Duke's army entered Nanzheng and seized all the treasures from Zhang Lu's treasury. The Records of Wei state: The army traveled a thousand li through the Wudu Mountains, ascending and descending treacherous terrain; the soldiers endured great hardship. Therefore, the Duke held a grand banquet to honor them, ensuring no one was forgotten for their efforts. Ba and Han both surrendered. The commandery of Hanning was restored to its former name, Hanzhong; the counties of Anyang and Xicheng from Hanzhong were separated to form the new Xicheng Commandery, with a governor appointed; the commanderies of Xi and Shangyong were divided, each being assigned a military commander.

八月，孫權圍合肥，張遼、李典擊破之。
In August, Sun Quan besieged Hefei; Zhang Liao and Li Dian defeated him.

101
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
九月，巴七姓夷王朴胡、賨邑侯杜濩舉巴夷、賨民來附，孫盛曰：朴音浮。濩音戶。於是分巴郡，以胡為巴東太守，濩為巴西太守，皆封列侯。天子命公承制封拜諸侯守相。孔衍漢魏春秋曰：天子以公典任于外，臨事之賞，或宜速疾，乃命公得承制封拜諸侯守相，詔曰：「夫軍之大事，在茲賞罰，勸善懲惡，宜不旋時，故司馬法曰『賞不逾日』者，欲民速覩為善之利也。昔在中興，鄧禹入關，承制拜軍祭酒李文為河東太守，來歙又承制拜高峻為通路將軍，察其本傳，皆非先請，明臨事刻印也，斯則世祖神明，權達損益，蓋所用速示威懷而著鴻勳也。其春秋之義，大夫出疆，有專命之事，苟所以利社稷安國家而已。況君秉任二伯，師尹九有，實征夷夏，軍行蕃甸之外，失得在於斯須之間，停賞俟詔以滯世務，固非朕之所圖也。自今已後，臨事所甄，當加寵號者，其便刻印章假授，咸使忠義得相獎勵，勿有疑焉。」
In September, the seven clans of Ba's Yi King Puhu and Duhuo, Marquis of Congyi, led their Yi people from Ba and the Cong people to submit. Sun Sheng said: The pronunciation of "Pu" is Fu. The pronunciation of "Hu" is Hu. At this time, the Ba Commandery was divided; Pu Hu was appointed as Tai Shou of Badong and Du Huo as Tai Shou of Bazhou, both being enfeoffed as Marquises. The emperor authorized the Duke to bestow titles and appointments upon marquises, commandery governors, and other officials according to imperial decree. Kong Yan's Han Wei Chunqiu records: The emperor, considering the Duke was entrusted with authority in distant regions and that rewards for meritorious acts during military affairs should be swift, authorized him to bestow titles upon marquises and commandery governors according to imperial mandate. An edict stated: "The great matters of a military campaign lie in these rewards and punishments; encouraging virtue and punishing evil must not be delayed. Hence the 'Military Laws' state that 'rewards must not exceed one day,' so as to allow the people quickly to witness the benefits of doing good." "In the past, during the reign of the Middle Revival (Han dynasty), Deng Yu entered Guan and, under imperial mandate, appointed Jun Jiaoshi Li Wen as Tai Shou of Hedong. Again, Lai Xi, also acting on such authority, appointed Gao Jun as Tonglu General. Upon examining their original biographies, neither had first requested permission; clearly, they were authorized to engrave seals immediately in the field. This was a demonstration of Emperor Guangwu's wisdom and flexibility—adjusting policies for expediency—to swiftly display authority and benevolence while establishing great achievements." This reflects the principles of the Spring and Autumn Annals: when a high minister leaves the capital, he may act independently in matters entrusted to him, provided it serves the benefit of the state and ensures national stability. How much more so when a ruler entrusts authority to two great ministers, commanding the Nine Provinces and leading campaigns against both Huaxia and foreign tribes. When military forces operate beyond the borders of the fiefdoms, gains or losses may occur in an instant; to delay rewards awaiting imperial decree would hinder state affairs—this is certainly not my intention. "From now on, in the event of meritorious acts occurring during military campaigns where honors must be bestowed, seals may immediately be engraved and titles conferred. Let loyalty and righteousness always be rewarded without hesitation or doubt."

Jump to dictionary

武帝紀:
冬十月，始置名號侯至五大夫，與舊列侯、關內侯凡六等，以賞軍功。魏書曰：置名號侯爵十八級，關中侯爵十七級，皆金印紫綬；又置關內外侯十六級，銅印龜紐墨綬；五大夫十五級，銅印環紐，亦墨綬，皆不食租，與舊列侯關內侯凡六等。臣松之以為今之虛封蓋自此始。
In winter, the tenth month of this year, titles were first established ranging from Minghao Hou to Wudaifu. Combined with the existing ranks of Liehou and Guannei Hou, there were now six grades in total, used to reward military merit. The Records of Wei states: Eighteen ranks were established for the title of Minghao Hou, and seventeen ranks for Guanzhong Hou, all with golden seals and purple sashes; furthermore, sixteen ranks were established for Guanneiwaiguo Hou, each bearing copper seals with turtle-shaped fastenings and black sashes; the rank of Wudaifu had fifteen levels, with copper seals and ring-shaped fastenings, also paired with black sashes. None received land revenues; together with the old ranks of Liehou and Guanneihou, there were six grades in total. Chen Songzhi believes that the current practice of granting empty titles likely began from this time.

武帝紀:
十一月，魯自巴中將其餘衆降。封魯及五子皆為列侯。劉備襲劉璋，取益州，遂據巴中；遣張郃擊之。
In November, Zhang Lu led his remaining forces in surrendering from Bazhong. Zhang Lu and his five sons were all enfeoffed as Liehou (Marquises). Liu Bei attacked Liu Zhang, seized Yizhou, and thus occupied Bazhong; The Duke dispatched Zhang He to attack him.

104
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
十二月，公自南鄭還，留夏侯淵屯漢中。是行也，侍中王粲作五言詩以美其事，曰：「從軍有苦樂，但問所從誰。所從神且武，安得乆勞師？相公征關右，赫怒振天威，一舉滅獯虜，再舉服羌夷，西牧邊地賊，忽若俯拾遺。陳賞越山嶽，酒肉踰川坻，軍中多饒飫，人馬皆溢肥，徒行兼乘還，空出有餘資。拓土三千里，往反速如飛，歌舞入鄴城，所願獲無違。」
In December, the Duke returned from Nanzheng, leaving Xiahou Yuan stationed in Hanzhong. On this campaign, Shizhong Wang Can composed a five-character poem to praise the event: "Military service brings both hardship and joy; it all depends on whom one follows. When following a leader who is divine and martial, how could the army endure prolonged toil?" The Prime Minister marched westward into Guanyou, his wrath shaking the heavens with imperial might. In one campaign he crushed the Xun bandits; in another, pacified the Qiang and Yi tribes. The rebels on the western borders were vanquished as easily as picking up fallen objects from the ground. The rewards were distributed across mountains and hills; wine and meat flowed over the riverbanks. In camp, there was abundance in food; both men and horses grew plump. On foot or on horseback, returning with surplus supplies, they departed empty-handed yet returned richly provisioned. They expanded territory by three thousand li, returning swiftly as if on wings; dancing and singing into Ye City, achieving all they had wished for without failure."

武帝紀:
二十一年春二月，公還鄴。魏書曰：辛未，有司以太牢告至，策勳于廟，甲午始春祠，令曰：「議者以為祠廟上殿當解履。吾受錫命，帶劔不解履上殿。今有事于廟而解履，是尊先公而替王命，敬父祖而簡君主，故吾不敢解履上殿也。又臨祭就洗，以手擬水而不盥。夫盥以絜為敬，未聞擬向不盥之禮，且『祭神如神在』，故吾親受水而盥也。又降神禮訖，下階就幕而立，須奏樂畢竟，似若不愆，烈祖遲祭，不速訖也。故吾坐俟樂闋送神乃起也。受胙納神以授侍中，此為敬恭不終實也，古者親執祭事，故吾親納于神，終抱而歸也。仲尼曰『雖違衆，吾從下』，誠哉斯言也。」三月壬寅，公親耕籍田。魏書曰：有司奏：「四時講武於農隙。漢承秦制，三時不講，唯十月都試車馬，幸長水南門，會五營士為八陣進退，名曰乘之。今金革未偃，士民素習，自今已後，可無四時講武，但以立秋擇吉日大朝車騎，號曰治兵，上合禮名，下承漢制。」奏可。夏五月，天子進公爵為魏王。獻帝傳載詔曰：「自古帝王，雖號稱相變，爵等不同，至乎襃崇元勳，建立功德，光啟氏姓，延于子孫，庶姓之與親，豈有殊焉。昔我聖祖受命，刱業肇基，造我區夏，鑒古今之制，通爵等之差，盡封山川以立藩屏，使異姓親戚，並列土地，據國而王，所以保乂天命，安固萬嗣。歷世承平，臣主無事。世祖中興而時有難易，是以曠年數百，無異姓諸侯王之位。朕以不德，繼序弘業，遭率土分崩，羣兇縱毒，自西徂東，辛苦卑約。當此之際，唯恐溺入于難，以羞先帝之聖德。賴皇天之靈，俾君秉義奮身，震迅神武，捍朕于艱難，獲保宗廟，華夏遺民，含氣之倫，莫不蒙焉。君勤過稷、禹，忠侔伊、周，而掩之以謙讓，守之以彌恭，是以往者初開魏國，錫君土宇，懼君之違命，慮君之固辭，故且懷志屈意，封君為上公，欲以欽順高義，須俟勳績。韓遂、宋建，南結巴、蜀，羣逆合從，圖危社稷，君復命將，龍驤虎奮，梟其元首，屠其窟栖。曁至西征，陽平之役，親擐甲冑，深入險阻，芟夷蝥賊，殄其兇醜，盪定西陲，懸旌萬里，聲教遠振，寧我區宇。蓋唐、虞之盛，三后樹功，文、武之興，旦、奭作輔，二祖成業，英豪佐命；夫以聖哲之君，事為己任，猶錫士班瑞以報功臣，豈有如朕寡德，仗君以濟，而賞典不豐，將何以荅神祇慰萬方哉？今進君爵為魏王，使使持節行御史大夫、宗正劉艾奉策璽玄土之社，苴以白茅，金虎符第一至第五，竹使符第一至十。君其正王位，以丞相領兾州牧如故。其上魏公璽綬符冊。敬服朕命，簡恤爾衆，克綏庶績，以揚我祖宗之休命。」魏王上書三辭，詔三報不許。又手詔曰：「大聖以功德為高美，以忠和為典訓，故刱業垂名，使百世可希，行道制義，使力行可效，是以勳烈無窮，休光茂著。稷、契載元首之聦明，周、邵因文、武之智用，雖經營庶官，仰歎俯思，其對豈有若君者哉？朕惟古人之功，美之如彼，思君忠勤之績，茂之如此，是以每將鏤符析瑞，陳禮命冊，寤寐慨然，自忘守文之不德焉。今君重違朕命，固辭懇切，非所以稱朕心，而訓後世也。其抑志撙節，勿復固辭。」四體書勢序曰：梁鵠以公為北部尉。曹瞞傳曰：為尚書右丞司馬建公所舉。及公為王，召建公到鄴，與歡飲，謂建公曰：「孤今日可復作尉否？」建公曰：「昔舉大王時，適可作尉耳。」王大笑。建公名防，司馬宣王之父。臣松之案司馬彪序傳，建公不為右丞，疑此不然，而王隱晉書云趙王篡位，欲尊祖為帝，博士馬平議稱京兆府君昔舉魏武帝為北部尉，賊不犯界，如此則為有徵。代郡烏丸行單于普富盧與其侯王來朝。天子命王女為公主，食湯沐邑。秋七月，匈奴南單于呼廚泉將其名王來朝，待以客禮，遂留魏，使右賢王去卑監其國。八月，以大理鍾繇為相國。魏書曰：始置奉常宗正官。
In spring, the second month of the twenty-first year, the Duke returned to Ye. The Records of Wei records: On the Xinwei day, officials offered a grand sacrifice with three oxen to announce their return and record meritorious deeds in the ancestral temple. On the Jiawu day, spring sacrifices began; an edict was issued stating: "Some argue that when ascending the dais in the ancestral temple for worship, one should remove one's shoes." "I have received imperial mandate and may ascend the dais with sword at my side without removing my shoes. If I now remove my shoes for worship in the temple, it would mean honoring my ancestors at the expense of imperial authority, revering father and grandfather while neglecting the sovereign. Therefore, I dare not ascend the dais without my shoes." Furthermore, when approaching the altar for sacrifice to perform ritual washing, he merely gestured toward the water with his hands but did not actually wash. "To wash one's hands is to express reverence through cleanliness; I have never heard of a ritual where one merely gestures toward water without actually washing. Moreover, 'When offering sacrifices to spirits, treat them as if they are present.' Therefore, I personally take the water and perform the rite." After the ritual of summoning spirits was completed, he descended from the dais and stood under a canopy until the music had finished playing. This seemed to delay proceedings, as if reluctant to conclude the ceremony hastily for the veneration of his illustrious ancestor. Therefore, I remained seated until the music ended and the spirits were properly sent off before rising. To receive the sacrificial meat and then hand it to a Shizhong for presentation to the deity is not complete reverence. In ancient times, one personally performed all aspects of the sacrifice; therefore, I myself presented the offering to the spirits and finally carried them back in my arms. Confucius said, 'Even if it goes against the majority, I follow what is right.' How true these words are." On the Rinyin day of the third month, the Duke personally tilled the ceremonial fields. The Records of Wei states: Officials presented a proposal: "Military exercises should be conducted during intervals in agricultural work throughout the four seasons." The Han dynasty inherited the Qin system, conducting no military exercises during three seasons; only in the tenth month was a general inspection of chariots and horses held. The emperor visited the southern gate of Changshui, where troops from the five camps assembled to demonstrate formations advancing and retreating in an eight-formation array, known as "Chengzhi." "Now, since the age of war has not yet ended and soldiers and civilians are already well-trained, from now on there is no need for military exercises in all four seasons. Instead, select a propitious day after the beginning of autumn to hold a grand inspection of chariots and cavalry, called 'Zhibing.' This conforms to ritual principles above and continues the Han system below." The proposal was approved. In summer, fifth month, the Son of Heaven elevated the Duke's title to King of Wei. The biography of Emperor Xian records the edict as saying: "Since ancient times, emperors and kings, though their titles may have changed and ranks differed, when it came to honoring those with great merit, establishing virtue and achievement, glorifying their families, and extending honor to descendants, commoners and nobles were no different. "In the past, my venerated ancestor received his mandate and founded our dynasty. He established the foundation of our realm, examining ancient and modern systems to harmonize differences in ranks. He fully enfeoffed mountains and rivers as barriers for defense, allowing both commoners and relatives to be granted territories, ruling states as kings—thus safeguarding Heaven's will and securing peace for countless generations." For successive generations, the realm enjoyed peace, with no troubles between ruler and subjects. When Emperor Shizu revived the dynasty, times varied in difficulty; thus, for several centuries, there was no position of a marquis or king among non-royal families. "I, unworthy as I am, have inherited and expanded the great cause. Yet I encountered a time of national disintegration, with many villains spreading chaos from west to east, enduring hardships and living humbly." At such a time, I feared being overwhelmed by calamity, bringing shame upon the holy virtue of my predecessors. Thanks to the grace of Heaven, you have upheld righteousness and taken action with divine might. You defended me in times of hardship, preserving our ancestral temple; all the remaining people of China, those who breathe, have been saved by your efforts. Your diligence surpasses that of Ji and Yu, your loyalty equals that of Yi and Zhou. Yet you have concealed these virtues with humility and maintained them through even greater reverence. Therefore, when the Wei state was first established, we granted you territory, fearing you might refuse our command or firmly decline the title. Thus, we withheld our full intent and humbly bestowed upon you the rank of Shanggong (Grand Duke), hoping to honor your noble virtue while awaiting further meritorious achievements. Han Sui and Song Jian, linking with the southern Ba and Shu regions, united various rebels to threaten the state. You once again accepted command; like a dragon soaring or a tiger leaping, you beheaded their leaders and destroyed their strongholds. Later, during the western campaign and the Battle of Yangping, you personally donned armor and led troops deep into perilous terrain. You eradicated bandits and destroyed their wicked forces, pacifying the western frontier. Your banners flew a thousand li away; your influence spread far and wide, bringing peace to our realm. In the flourishing age of Tang and Yu, three virtuous rulers established their achievements; in the rise of Wen and Wu, Dan and Shi served as assistants. The two ancestors completed their cause with the aid of heroes and sages. Even a sage and wise ruler, taking all affairs as his own responsibility, still bestowed honors and treasures to reward meritorious subjects. How much more so for me, of humble virtue, who relies on you to achieve success? If rewards are not generous, how can I repay Heaven and Earth or satisfy the people throughout the realm? Therefore, I now advance your title to King of Wei. Envoys carrying imperial edicts and serving as Acting Director of the Office of Censors, along with Zongzheng Liu Ai, will present you with the decree, seal, black earth from the sacred soil, wrapped in white reeds, five gold tiger tokens (first through fifth), and ten bamboo envoy tokens (first through tenth). You should now assume the royal title, yet continue to serve as Chancellor and Administrator of Ji Zhou as before. Present your seal, sash, tokens, and decree of the Duke of Wei. Respectfully accept my command, govern your people with care, achieve peace and success, and thus honor the glorious legacy of our ancestors." King Wei submitted a letter three times declining the title; the emperor issued three replies refusing to allow it. Another handwritten edict stated: "The great sages valued virtue and achievement as the highest excellence, and loyalty and harmony as exemplary teachings. Therefore, they established their cause and left behind a name that future generations could aspire to; they set forth principles of righteousness so that diligent conduct might be emulated. Thus, meritorious deeds endure without end, and noble glory becomes widely renowned." Ji and Xie served under a wise ruler, while Zhou and Shao relied on the wisdom of Wen and Wu. Though they managed many officials and reflected both upward and inward in their governance, could any of them compare to you? I reflect on the achievements of ancient men, whose virtues were so great. Considering your loyalty and diligence, I find my own merits equally outstanding. Therefore, whenever I prepare tokens and treasures or present ceremonial decrees, I feel deeply moved in both wakefulness and sleep, forgetting that I am but an unworthy ruler bound by convention. Now you insist on defying my command and refuse with earnest sincerity, which is not in accordance with my wishes or suitable for instructing future generations. Therefore, restrain your humility and moderation, and do not persist in declining." The preface to the Four Styles of Calligraphy records: Liang Hu appointed the Duke as Northern Commandant. The biography of Cao Man states: He was recommended by Sima Jian Gong, Right Assistant Minister of the Secretariat. When the Duke became king, he summoned Sima Jian Gong to Ye and drank with him joyfully. He said to Sima Jian Gong: "Might I still serve as a commandant today?" Sima Jian Gong replied: "At the time when I recommended you, it was just right for you to be a commandant." The king laughed heartily. Sima Jian Gong's given name was Fang, the father of Sima Xuanwang. Min Songzhi examined the preface and biography by Sima Biao, which states that Jian Gong was not a Right Assistant Minister. I suspect this account is incorrect. However, Wang Yin's Records of the Jin dynasty mentions that when the Prince of Zhao usurped the throne, he wished to honor his ancestor as emperor. The scholar Ma Ping argued that Jingzhao Fu Jun had once recommended Emperor Wu of Wei as Northern Commandant, and during that time, no bandits dared cross into his territory—thus providing evidence for this claim. The acting Chanyu Pufulu of the Wuhuan in Dai Jun, along with his marquises and kings, came to pay homage. The Son of Heaven ordered the King's daughter to be made a princess, granting her a fief for her personal expenses. In autumn, seventh month, Chuchuanquan, the Southern Chanyu of the Xiongnu, led his prominent kings to pay homage. He was treated with guestly courtesy and remained in Wei; the Right Worthy King Qubi was appointed to oversee their state. In August, Zhong Yao, Minister of Punishments, was appointed as Chancellor. The Records of Wei state: The offices of Fengchang and Zongzheng were first established.

武帝紀:
冬十月，治兵，魏書曰：王親執金鼔以令進退。遂征孫權，十一月至譙。
In winter, tenth month, military exercises were held. The Records of Wei states: The King personally held the golden drum to command advances and retreats. He then launched a campaign against Sun Quan, arriving at Qiao in the eleventh month.

武帝紀:
二十二年春正月，王軍居巢，二月，進軍屯江西郝谿。權在濡須口築城拒守，遂逼攻之，權退走。三月，王引軍還，留夏侯惇、曹仁、張遼等屯居巢。
In spring, first month of the twenty-second year, King Wei's army was stationed at Jucha; in February, they advanced and established a garrison at Haoxi on the western bank of the Yangtze River. Sun Quan constructed a city at Ruxukou to resist, so he launched an attack and forced him to retreat. In March, the King led his army back, leaving Xiahou Dun, Cao Ren, Zhang Liao and others to garrison Jucha.

武帝紀:
夏四月，天子命王設天子旌旗，出入稱警蹕。五月，作泮宮。六月，以軍師華歆為御史大夫。魏書曰：初置衞尉官。秋八月，令曰：「昔伊摯、傅說出於賤人，管仲，桓公賊也，皆用之以興。蕭何、曹參，縣吏也，韓信、陳平負汙辱之名，有見笑之恥，卒能成就王業，聲著千載。吳起貪將，殺妻自信，散金求官，母死不歸，然在魏，奏人不敢東向，在楚則三晉不敢南謀。今天下得無有至德之人放在民間，及果勇不顧，臨敵力戰；若文俗之吏，高才異質，或堪為將守；負汙辱之名，見笑之行，或不仁不孝而有治國用兵之術：其各舉所知，勿有所遺。」冬十月，天子命王冕十有二旒，乘金根車，駕六馬，設五時副車，以五官中郎將丕為魏太子。
In summer, fourth month, the Son of Heaven granted the King permission to use imperial banners and standards, with announcements made for his comings and goings. In May, the Pan Palace was constructed. In June, Jushi Huaxin was appointed as Director of the Office of Censors. The Records of Wei states: The office of Weiyi was first established. In autumn, eighth month, an edict was issued: "Long ago, Yi Zhi and Fu Yue rose from humble origins; Guan Zhong had once been a traitor to Duke Huan. Yet all were employed and brought about prosperity. Xiao He and Cao Can were merely county officials, while Han Xin and Chen Ping bore reputations of disgrace and shame. Yet in the end, they all achieved great success for their kings, leaving a name remembered through the ages." Wu Qi was a greedy general who killed his wife to prove himself, spent gold to seek office, and did not return home even when his mother died. Yet while in Wei, the people dared not face east; when he served Chu, the three states of Jin never plotted southward against it. Nowadays, could there not be men of great virtue hidden among the common people, or those who are brave and fearless, fighting fiercely on the battlefield? Or perhaps there are officials of refined character with exceptional talent and unique qualities, capable of serving as generals or administrators; Or those who bear disgraceful reputations and actions that invite ridicule, or even those lacking in benevolence and filial piety but possessing strategies for governing states and commanding armies: you are all to recommend the people you know, leaving no one out." In winter, tenth month, the Son of Heaven decreed that the King should wear a twelve-pearl headdress, ride in a golden root chariot drawn by six horses, and be accompanied by five auxiliary carriages for different seasons. He also appointed Wu Guan Zhonglangjiang Pi as Crown Prince of Wei.

劉備遣張飛、馬超、吳蘭等屯下辯；遣曹洪拒之。
Liu Bei dispatched Zhang Fei, Ma Chao, Wu Lan and others to garrison Xi Bian; Cao Hong was sent to resist them.

Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
二十三年春正月，漢太醫令吉本與少府耿紀、司直韋晃等反，攻許，燒丞相長史王必營，魏武故事載令曰：「領長史王必，是吾披荊棘時吏也。忠能勤事，心如鐵石，國之良吏也。蹉跌乆未辟之，捨騏驥而弗乘，焉遑遑而更求哉？故教辟之，已署所宜，便以領長史統事如故。」必與潁川典農中郎將嚴匡討斬之。三輔決錄注曰：時有京兆金禕字德禕，自以世為漢臣，自日磾討莽何羅，忠誠顯著，名節累葉。覩漢祚將移，謂可季興，乃喟然發憤，遂與耿紀、韋晃、吉本、本子邈、邈弟穆等結謀。紀字季行，少有美名，為丞相掾，王甚敬異之，遷侍中，守少府。邈字文然，穆字思然，以禕慷慨有日磾之風，又與王必善，因以閒之，若殺必，欲挾天子以攻魏，南援劉備。時關羽彊盛，而王在鄴，留必典兵督許中事。文然等率雜人及家僮千餘人夜燒門攻必，禕遣人為內應，射必中肩。必不知攻者為誰，以素與禕善，走投禕，夜喚德禕，禕家不知是必，謂為文然等，錯應曰：「王長史已死乎？卿曹事立矣！」必乃更他路奔。一曰：必欲投禕，其帳下督謂必曰：「今日事竟知誰門而投入乎？」扶必奔南城。會天明，必猶在，文然等衆散，故敗。後十餘日，必竟以創死。獻帝春秋曰：收紀、晃等，將斬之，紀呼魏王名曰：「恨吾不自生意，竟為羣兒所誤耳！」晃頓首搏頰，以至於死。山陽公載記曰：王聞王必死，盛怒，召漢百官詣鄴，令救火者左，不救火者右。衆人以為救火者必無罪，皆附左；王以為「不救火者非助亂，救火乃實賊也」。皆殺之。
In spring, first month of the Twenty-third year, Han Taishi Ling Ji Ben, Shaofu Geng Ji, Sizhi Wei Huang and others rebelled, attacking Xu, burning the camp of Chancellor's Chief Clerk Wang Bi. The Annals of Wei Wu records an edict stating: "Chief Clerk Wang Bi is a clerk who served me during my days of braving thorns and brambles. He was loyal, diligent in his duties, with a heart as firm as iron or stone; he was an outstanding official of the state. To have delayed his promotion for so long without appointment is like abandoning a fine steed and refusing to ride it—how could one then anxiously seek elsewhere? Therefore, I have ordered his appointment. The proper position has already been assigned; he should continue to serve as Chief Clerk and oversee affairs as before." Wang Bi, along with Yan Kuang, Director of Agriculture for Yingchuan Commandery, suppressed the rebellion and executed them. The annotations of Jue Lu of the Three Fu regions state: At that time, there was a man from Jingzhao named Jin Yi, courtesy name De Yi. He considered his family to have been lifelong subjects of Han. Since Dayidi's campaign against Mang Heluo, their loyalty and devotion had long been renowned, with distinguished names and virtuous conduct passed down through generations. Observing that the Han dynasty's mandate was about to shift, he believed it was time for a revival and thus sighed with indignation. He then conspired together with Geng Ji, Wei Huang, Ji Ben, Ben's son Miao, Miao's younger brother Mu, and others. Geng Ji, courtesy name Jixing, was young and well known for his virtue. He served as an assistant to the Chancellor; the King held him in great respect and regarded him highly. He later advanced to Shizhong and served concurrently as Shaofu. Miao, courtesy name Wenran, and Mu, courtesy name Siran, admired Jin Yi for his boldness and the spirit of Dayidi. They also had good relations with Wang Bi, so they used this as an opportunity to manipulate him. If Wang Bi were killed, they intended to seize the Son of Heaven and attack Wei from the north while seeking southern support from Liu Bei. At that time, Guan Yu was powerful; the King was in Ye, leaving Wang Bi to command troops and oversee affairs in Xu. Wenran led over a thousand miscellaneous men and household attendants to attack Wang Bi by night, burning the gates. Jin Yi sent someone as an inside accomplice who shot at Wang Bi, hitting his shoulder. Wang Bi did not know who was attacking. Since he had always been on good terms with Jin Yi, he fled and sought refuge at Jin's residence, calling out "De Yi" in the night. Jin Yi's family did not recognize him as Wang Bi but thought it was Wenran and others, mistakenly responding: "Has Director Wang died?" "Your cause has succeeded!" Wang Bi then took another route to flee. One account says: Wang Bi intended to take refuge with Jin Yi, but his subordinate officer said to him, "On such a day of turmoil, how can you know whose gate to run to?" He helped Wang Bi flee toward the southern city. Just as dawn broke, Wang Bi was still alive; Wenran's forces dispersed and thus failed in their rebellion. More than ten days later, Wang Bi finally died from his wounds. The Spring and Autumn Annals of Emperor Xian records: Geng Ji, Wei Huang and others were captured and about to be executed. Geng Ji called out the King's name and said, "I regret not having devised a better plan myself; I was ultimately misled by these young men!" Wei Huang kowtowed repeatedly and struck his cheeks in despair until he died. The Records of the Shanyang Gong state: Upon hearing Wang Bi's death, the King was furious and summoned all Han officials to Ye. He ordered those who had fought the fire to stand on his left side and those who did not fight it to stand on his right. Everyone assumed that those who had helped extinguish the fire would be innocent, so they all gathered on the left side; The King declared: "Those who did not help put out the fire were not aiding the rebellion, but those who did fight it were in fact traitors." He had them all executed.

曹洪破吳蘭，斬其將任夔等。三月，張飛、馬超走漢中，陰平氐強端斬吳蘭，傳其首。
Cao Hong defeated Wu Lan, slaying his general Ren Kui and others. In March, Zhang Fei and Ma Chao retreated to Hanzhong; Qiang Duan of the Yinping Di people beheaded Wu Lan and sent his head as a trophy.

武帝紀:
夏四月，代郡、上谷烏丸無臣氐等叛，遣鄢陵侯彰討破之。魏書載王令曰：「去冬天降疫癘，民有凋傷，軍興于外，墾田損少，吾甚憂之。其令吏民男女：女年七十已上無夫子，若年十二已下無父母兄弟，及目無所見，手不能作，足不能行，而無妻子父兄產業者，廩食終身。幼者至十二止，貧窮不能自贍者，隨口給貸。老耄須待養者，年九十已上，復不事，家一人。」
In summer, fourth month, Wuhuan tribes of Dai Jun and Shanggu, including Wu Chen Di, rebelled. The King dispatched Yanling Hou Zhang to suppress them and defeated the rebels. The Records of Wei records an edict issued by the King: "Last winter, a plague fell upon us; many people were afflicted and their lives ruined. With military campaigns ongoing outside, cultivated fields have suffered losses, which greatly concerns me." Therefore, I order all officials and commoners: women aged seventy or older who are widowed without children, or girls under twelve with no parents or brothers; those who are blind, unable to work with their hands, or unable to walk on foot; and anyone lacking a spouse, father, elder brother, or property—such individuals shall be provided food for life. For the young, this provision applies up to age twelve; those too poor to support themselves shall receive loans according to their household size. Those who are elderly and require care, aged ninety or above, shall be exempt from labor duties; one member of each family may remain at home to attend to them."

113
Jump to dictionary
Show parallel passages
武帝紀:
六月，令曰：「古之葬者，必居瘠薄之地。其規西門豹祠西原上為壽陵，因高為基，不封不樹。周禮冢人掌公墓之地，凡諸侯居左右以前，卿大夫居後，漢制亦謂之陪陵。其公卿大臣列將有功者，宜陪壽陵，其廣為兆域，使足相容。」
In the sixth month, an edict was issued: "In ancient times, burials were always conducted in barren and thin soil. Designate the western plain west of the Temple of Xi Men Bao as the site for my mausoleum. Build it on high ground, without a mound or trees planted." According to the Rites of Zhou, the official Zhong Ren was in charge of public burial grounds. All feudal lords were buried on either side ahead, while ministers and high officials were placed behind; this Han dynasty system was also called "pei ling." Those among the ministers, high officials, and generals who have rendered meritorious service should be buried as attendants at my mausoleum; therefore, we shall expand the designated burial area to ensure it is sufficiently spacious to accommodate them."

Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
秋七月，治兵，遂西征劉備，九月，至長安。
In autumn, seventh month, he reviewed his troops and launched a western campaign against Liu Bei. In the ninth month, he arrived at Chang'an.

Jump to dictionary

武帝紀:
冬十月，宛守將侯音等反，執南陽太守，劫略吏民，保宛。初，曹仁討關羽，屯樊城，是月使仁圍宛。
In winter, tenth month, Hou Yin, a commander defending Wan, rebelled, seized the governor of Nanyang, and looted officials and civilians, taking refuge in Wan. Initially, Cao Ren had campaigned against Guan Yu and stationed at Fan Cheng; this month he was ordered to lay siege to Wan.

116
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
二十四年春正月，仁屠宛，斬音。曹瞞傳曰：是時南陽間苦繇役，音於是執太守東里襃，與吏民共反，與關羽連和。南陽功曹宗子卿往說音曰：「足下順民心，舉大事，遠近莫不望風；然執郡將，逆而無益，何不遣之。吾與子共戮力，比曹公軍來，關羽兵亦至矣。」音從之，即釋遣太守。子卿因夜踰城亡出，遂與太守收餘民圍音，會曹仁軍至，共滅之。
In the first month of spring, twenty-fourth year [of reign], Ren sacked Wan and beheaded Hou Yin. The Biography of Cao Man states: At that time, the people between Nanyang were suffering from heavy corvée labor. Hou Yin therefore seized the governor Dongli Bao and rebelled together with officials and civilians, forming an alliance with Guan Yu. Zong Ziqing, the Gongcao of Nanyang, went to persuade Hou Yin and said: "You have followed public sentiment and launched a great cause; people near and far look up to you with admiration. Yet by holding the commander of the commandery, you are acting rebelliously without benefit—why not release him?" "Let me and you work together. By the time Cao Gong's army arrives, Guan Yu's forces will have arrived as well." Hou Yin followed his advice and immediately released the governor. Zong Ziqing then fled over the city walls at night and escaped, joining forces with the governor to gather the remaining civilians and surround Hou Yin. When Cao Ren's army arrived, they jointly crushed the rebellion.

117
Jump to dictionary
武帝紀:
夏侯淵與劉備戰於陽平，為備所殺。三月，王自長安出斜谷，軍遮要以臨漢中，遂至陽平。備因險拒守。九州春秋曰：時王欲還，出令曰「雞肋」，官屬不知所謂。主簿楊脩便自嚴裝，人驚問脩：「何以知之？」脩曰：「夫雞肋，棄之如可惜，食之無所得，以比漢中，知王欲還也。」
Xiahou Yuan fought Liu Bei at Yangping and was killed by him. In the third month, the King departed from Chang'an through Xiegou Valley, stationing troops to block key passes and approach Hanzhong. He then arrived at Yangping. Liu Bei took advantage of the rugged terrain to resist and defend. The Nine Provinces Spring and Autumn Annals states: At that time, the King wanted to withdraw and issued an order saying "chicken ribs," leaving his officials puzzled about its meaning. The chief clerk Yang Xiu immediately began making preparations for departure. People were surprised and asked Xiu, "How did you know?" Xiu replied: "A chicken rib is something that one finds too valuable to discard, yet eating it yields nothing. Comparing this to Hanzhong, I know the King wants to withdraw."

In summer, fifth month, he led his army back to Chang'an.
